1401 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bates


CR050123681, MV050341440


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1404



May 5, 2006, Decided  
May 5, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dismissed by State v. Bates, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1493 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 17, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of narcotics, possession of drug paraphernalia, and operating under the influence in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-279(a) , 21a-267(a), and 14-227a. Before jury selection, the State filed a two-count part B information charging him as a second-time offender. Defendant filed a motion under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-8 to dismiss the second count on grounds of vindictive prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State had vindictively filed the second count of the part B information, which charged him as a second-time drug offender, because he had rejected a plea bargain. He argued that this violated his constitutional rights. The court held that as the information had been filed before the trial, defendant had to show actual vindictiveness. A prosecutor could lawfully file additional charges and seek a greater sentence if a defendant did not accept the State's offer. The prosecutor had represented that he did not know defendant prior to trial and that he regularly filed a part B information if a defendant had a prior conviction. Additionally, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-279(a) clearly stated an increased penalty for second offenders, and defendant knew whether he had a previous drug conviction. Thus, the prosecutor's failure to inform defendant after he declined a plea bargain that he would be filing the amendment did not support an appearance of actual vindictiveness. Furthermore, the prosecutor was legally justified in filing the part B information, and therefore the increase in the potential penalty did not lead the court to find actual vindictiveness.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1402 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. Warden


CV044000182


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1319



May 4, 2006, Decided  
May 4, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Carter v. Comm'r of Corr., 106 Conn. App. 464, 942 A.2d 494, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 99 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Carter, 84 Conn. App. 263, 853 A.2d 565, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 335 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus which challenged his convictions for assault in the first degree, attempt to commit assault in the first degree, risk of injury to a child, and criminal possession of a firearm. The prisoner alleged, inter alia, ineffective assistance of counsel, prosecutorial misconduct, and actual innocence.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner an individual along an alleyway while shooting at him. A young girl was shot. The court held that it was clear that the prisoner's trial counsel exercised a reasonable strategic approach on the sufficiency of the evidence issue. The decision of both trial and appellate counsel not to focus on the sufficiency of the evidence claim regarding the element of intent was reasonably sound given the theory of the case pursued by the defense and the evidence presented at the criminal trial. Consequently, the prisoner failed to overcome the presumption that under the circumstances, the challenged action was sound trial and appellate strategy. There was no evidence of prosecutorial misconduct. Since the jury could have reasonably found that the prisoner discharged his firearm with the intent to physically injury one person and that act was at the same time likely to impair the health of a child, there was no reason for the attorneys to assert a legally inconsistent verdict claim. The prisoner did not submit any newly discovered evidence and thus, failed to even make the threshold requirement by which a claim of actual innocence could be pursued.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1403 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mulvehill v. Pope


FA054004366S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1251



April 28, 2006, Decided  
April 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother sought a determination of paternity, an order of custody, educational support and any other equitable relief. Defendant putative father argued, inter alia, that the mother failed to show that the court had personal jurisdiction over him pursuant to the Connecticut long-arm statute for paternity matters and otherwise failed to show the existence of minimum contacts.


OVERVIEW: At all relevant times, the putative father claimed to have resided in Florida. No evidence was provided to show that he resided within Connecticut at any relevant time. There was no personal jurisdiction over him pursuant to the language of the long-arm statute for paternity matters, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-160. The court found notice was performed in the manner prescribed for service of process within Connecticut and was therefore found to be sufficient for the purposes of the Uniform Child Custody Jurisdiction and Enforcement Act (UCCJEA). The putative father neither acknowledged paternity nor was found to be the father of the child. He was therefore not a "parent" for the purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-61. Furthermore, there was no existing jurisdictional basis for the mother to pursue such a finding in Connecticut. The putative father had sufficient notice of the custody claim, pursuant to the UCCJEA, to protect his interest in participating in the child's future care and control. An order of sole custody in favor of the mother did not offend traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice.


OUTCOME: The putative father's motion to dismiss as to paternity was granted. To the extent that the mother sought sole custody of the minor child, the motion to dismiss was denied. To the extent that the mother sought an order of educational support, the motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1404 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Northeast v. Fleming


CV064019420


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1122



April 18, 2006, Decided  
April 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by C. R. Klewin Northeast v. Fleming, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 434 (Conn., Oct. 23, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff contractor applied for an order for defendant state officials to show cause why a writ of mandamus should not issue commanding them to implement a compromise and pay the contractor for work done by the contractor. The state officials responded with a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the doctrine of sovereign immunity barred the action.


OVERVIEW: The contractor provided services to the State of Connecticut in the construction and renovation of buildings at a community college. After disputes arose as to the value of the contractor's services; negotiations ensued, and a compromise was agreed to between the contractor and the administrator of the state agency to which the services were provided. The Attorney General of Connecticut, recommended to the Governor of Connecticut, that the compromise be accepted. The Governor agreed, and, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 3-7(c), authorized the agency administrator to pay the compromise amount in full settlement of the disputed claim. However, the agency administrator did not pay the contractor, despite the contractor's demands for payment. The contractor then alleged that the inaction of state officers in not paying the contractor was in excess of or in contravention of their duties. The court found that the complaint sufficiently alleged that the failure of state officials to pay the contractor's claim as authorized by the Governor was in violation of their duties under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-5 and 3-117(a). Thus, the doctrine of sovereign immunity did not bar the contractor's claim.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1405 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dziedzic Props., LLC v. Torrington Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV054002406S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1081



April 10, 2006, Decided  
April 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer appealed a decision of defendant zoning board of appeals which denied its appeal from a decision of the zoning enforcement officer (ZEO) who denied the developer's application for a zoning permit to construct a single-family dwelling on the property. The ZEO determined the application did not meet requirements for frontage per zoning definitions for frontage on a street.


OVERVIEW: The developer had a contract to purchase the property from the record owner. The property was landlocked in a section of wooded acreage which was surrounded by residential development. It appeared to be an early development plan showing that the property would be bounded on the south by a proposed street and on the north by a proposed street. The streets were never built or accepted by the city. The property did not have any frontage on an abutting street accepted by the city or state. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-27 had no bearing on a situation where a town through its zoning regulations restricted building to lots adjoining city streets or state roads. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-27 applied to building on unaccepted streets. There was no unaccepted street involved. The taking argument failed because there was no evidence that the city's decision was confiscatory in nature. Implied acceptance did not apply because it was without doubt that no work of any kind had been performed within 250 feet of the property.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1406 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Weinberg v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV970574120


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 937



March 29, 2006, Decided  
March 29, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Weinberg v. Warden, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2040 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 6, 2006)
Appeal dismissed by Weinberg v. Comm'r of Corr., 2009 Conn. App. LEXIS 5 (Conn. App. Ct., Jan. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Weinberg, 215 Conn. 231, 575 A.2d 1003, 1990 Conn. LEXIS 185 (1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding against respondent Commissioner of Correction, Connecticut, petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus following his conviction on a charge of murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. Ann. § 53a-54a and the imposition of a 60-year sentence. In seeking habeas relief, the inmate argued that he was denied the effective assistance of counsel that was due him under both the federal and state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The inmate murdered a woman and took his girlfriend to the crime scene where she saw some burned items. She told the police about the site, and they found parts of items that the victim was known to have had and some of her hair. The inmate had trial counsel, and in addition to other witnesses, the girlfriend testified against the inmate. In considering the habeas petition, the court explained the test applicable under Strickland to a claim of ineffective assistance, ruling that while counsel had committed minor errors, they did not in the aggregate amount to a deprivation of the inmate's Sixth Amendment right to the effective assistance of counsel and that perfect representation was not required. The court also explained the history of habeas corpus relief, ruling that while the State had the burden of proof in the criminal trial, the inmate had the burden of proving his entitlement to a writ of habeas corpus. The court also concluded that his conviction was reliable, based on the evidence admitted, which included his girlfriend's important testimony. The clear import of her testimony was that he had led her to the site, so that he must have been the one who committed the crime.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

1407 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Massey v. Town of Branford


(X10)NNHCV04048778S(CLD)


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 952



March 28, 2006, Decided  
March 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a suit against defendants, the Town of Branford, Connecticut, and its officials, challenging a property tax assessment. They also included a claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and an administrative appeal from the action of the Town of Branford Board of Assessment Appeals in valuing the property. A central issue was whether the taxpayers had a private right of action for damages or whether the statutory scheme was exclusive.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers relied on several statutes and the state and federal constitutions. The court, with one exception, dismissed the counts in the complaint. Defendants raised the statute of limitations with regard to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-121f, but the court ruled that they had no right to raise the issue in a motion to strike as there was a conflict as to the relevant assessment dates and because an action had been available at common law to challenge an assessment, precluding that defense. The court rejected the constitutional claims raised under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, ruling that there was a comprehensive statutory scheme in place to address an assessment and valuation and that a § 1983 action thus did not lie. The court also found that the statutory remedies, as they appeared in Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-121f, 12-117a, and 12-119, were adequate, noting that when an appeal from an administrative decision was available, the appeal constituted an adequate alternate legal remedy under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court also ruled that the Branford, Conn., Code did not provide a private right of action for damages, that neither did the state constitution, and that there was no official misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to strike 11 counts of the complaint and dismissed four counts. To the extent that claims were made personally against the officials, the court struck counts 11 and 17. The court denied the balance of the motion to strike those counts and denied the motion to strike counts one through nine and 23. The court ordered an amended complaint to be filed and gave specific directions about its structure.

 

1408 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Page v. State


CV054008109


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 941



March 27, 2006, Decided  
March 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Page v. State Marshal Comm'n, 108 Conn. App. 668, 950 A.2d 529, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 330 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state marshal (SM) filed suit against defendants, the State of Connecticut and the State Marshal Commission, seeking a declaratory judgment that, inter alia, defendants exceeded their statutory authority by treating SMs as state employees and that SMs were unconstitutionally deprived of their property and were forced into involuntary servitude. The SM also sought injunctive relief and damages. Defendants sought dismissal.


OVERVIEW: The Commission implemented a policy in order to ensure the timely processing of restraining orders, wherein SMs were required to be present at an assigned courthouse during set hours. The SM filed suit, seeking declarations regarding the unlawfulness and unconstitutionality of the policy, seeking to enjoin further enforcement of it, and requesting damages for his compliance with the policy. Defendants sought dismissal of the complaint on sovereign immunity grounds. The court held that there was no applicable legislative waiver of sovereign immunity for purposes of the first exception to sovereign immunity. As to the second exception, the policy did not interfere with any of the SM's constitutional rights, as service could be made as the SM saw fit, he was not deprived of an interest of constitutional magnitude, and he did not have to do the job if he chose not to for purposes of the involuntary servitude claim. Accordingly, there was no violation of U.S. Const. amends. V, XIII, or XIV, or Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. Further, there was no excess of authority by the Commission, as it was authorized under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-38b(g) and (k) to implement the policy.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss the complaint in its entirety.

 

1409 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence Mall of New Haven, Inc. v. City of W. Haven


X06CV030183330S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 816



March 20, 2006, Decided  
March 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Lawrence Mall of New Haven v. City of W. Haven, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2691 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 22, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the City of West Haven (Connecticut) and its delinquent tax collection agent, moved to dismiss and for summary judgment on the sole remaining issue in the action filed by plaintiff taxpayers. The remaining issue centered on whether defendants were constitutionally required to provide prior notice that a 15% collection fee would be imposed on delinquent taxpayers if their real property taxes were not paid on time.


OVERVIEW: Defendants' motion to dismiss was based on the argument that the court was without jurisdiction to consider the taxpayers' claim because the taxpayers had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The motion for summary judgment was based on the argument that due process did not require prior notice of the tax collection fee. The court denied the motion to dismiss, holding that no administrative procedure, including the procedure in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-129, was available to taxpayers to contest the legality of the collection of fees. The motion for summary judgment was granted. Due process did not require a pre-deprivation proceeding prior to the exaction of taxes. The provision of post-payment procedures for contesting taxes satisfied due process. The taxpayers did not provide any support for their proposition that notice be given prior to the tax deprivation where only post-deprivation relief was required, and the court found no such support itself. Further, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-166, which authorized tax collectors to impose collection fees on unpaid taxes, provided the taxpayers with prior notice that the fees could be assessed.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to dismiss was denied, but their motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1410 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Minn. Methane, LLC v. Conn. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


CV040527217S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 846



March 20, 2006, Decided  
March 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at, Summary judgment granted by Wheelabrator Lisbon, Inc. v. Conn. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 45571 (D. Conn., June 23, 2006)
Affirmed by Minn. Methane, LLC v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 341 (Conn., Aug. 28, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electricity producer appealed, pursuant to the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183, and pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-35, a decision by defendant Connecticut Department of Public Utility Control (DPUC), which granted a petition for a declaratory ruling filed by an electric company regarding the company's ownership of certain Generation Information System Certificates (GISCs).


OVERVIEW: The company argued that, under its energy purchase agreement (EPA) with the producer, it was entitled to a certain landfill facilities' entire electrical output, including the GISCs that came into existence after the parties signed the EPA. The DPUC agreed with the company and awarded it the GISCs and any funds the producer received from any sale of those GISCs. The producer appealed. The parties agreed to submit only state issues on the DPUC's jurisdiction and on whether substantial evidence supported the determination, and they withheld all other issues for an appeal in federal court. The court found that the DPUC had jurisdiction pursuant to the declaratory judgment statute of the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176(a). The DPUC had jurisdiction over the company's petition regarding its right under the EPA as the DPUC had approved the EPA. Also, the DPUC had jurisdiction over interpretations and applications of its own regulations and decisions. Finally, there was sufficient evidence to support the DPUC's determination that the GISCs were an integral part of the renewable energy that the company bought from the producer under the EPA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the DPUC's decision and dismissed the producer's appeal.

 

1411 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wheelabrator Lisbon v. Conn. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


CV054003405


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 858



March 20, 2006, Decided  
March 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Wheelabrator Lisbon, Inc. v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 366 (Conn., Aug. 28, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff energy producer brought an administrative appeal under the Uniform Administrative Procedure Act (UAPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-35 to challenge a decision by defendant Connecticut Department of Public Utility Control (DPUC), which granted ownership of Generation Information System Certificates (GISCs) to a power company that purchased energy from the producer.


OVERVIEW: In a decision on separate petitions for declaratory rulings, the DPUC granted the company ownership of GISCs that were issued for one of the producer's trash to energy facilities. The facility's electrical output was delivered to the company under an energy purchase agreement (EPA) that was approved by the DPUC many years before the GISCs came into existence. The DPUC agreed with the company's position that the EPA entitled it to the facility's entire electrical output, including the GISCs. The GISCs could be sold to other electrical suppliers so those suppliers could meet the DPUC's renewable energy regulations and decisions created pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 16-243(a), 245a. The DPUC rejected the producer's argument that the GISCs were unrelated to electricity that was sold to the company. On appeal, the court agreed with the DPUC's finding that the GISCs were a quantification of the renewable energy attributes of the generated electricity and that the GISCs did not exist apart from that electricity. Under the EPA, the company bought the facility's entire electrical output, which included GISCs that were inseparable from the renewable energy produced at the facility.


OUTCOME: The Appeal is dismissed. the DPUC decision is affirmed.

 

1412 of 1861 DOCUMENTS



Balikci v. Greenwich Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV034012864


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 844



March 17, 2006, Decided  
March 17, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two cases brought by plaintiffs, various property owners and a homeowners association, were consolidated on appeal with regard to their challenge of the adoption by defendant, a town planning and zoning commission, of building and zoning regulation amendments concerning the Floor Area Ratio (FAR) within residential zones. One suit was brought under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8 to void the amendments and the second suit sought a declaratory judgment.


OVERVIEW: The declaratory judgment action sought to have the FAR amendments declared unconstitutional. With regard to the first suit brought by plaintiffs, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8, the court agreed that all plaintiffs were aggrieved parties as required under the statute but that the suit was time barred as a result of plaintiffs failing to file their appeal within one year from the commission's action/decision. Namely, commissions's decision on the attic and basement amendments took place on April 16, 2002, and plaintiffs commenced their action on April 29, 2003. The court held that a failure to file a zoning appeal within the statutory time period deprived the court of jurisdiction over the appeal. As to the declaratory judgment action, the court found that substantial evidence in the record supported the commission's action. The court found that the commission's actions in reducing the FAR standards between 8 or 10 percent in areas with a previous FAR, and creating FAR standards in areas without previous restrictions based upon the housing stock in those areas, were in accordance with the town plan and in furtherance of the public health, safety, and welfare of the town.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed both appeals.


 

1413 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Binns v. Binns


FA044006103S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 773



March 16, 2006, Decided  
March 16, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff's wife's action for dissolution of marriage, defendant husband filed a motion for an order requiring plaintiff wife to act as his sponsor in an immigration process to allow him to remain in the country even though his temporary right to remain and work in the United States expired.


OVERVIEW: Prior to marriage, the wife became a permanent resident of the United States. After the parties' marriage in Jamaica, she filed immigration papers to sponsor the husband to live in the United States. His temporary right to live and work in the country expired, and, if divorce was ordered before he completed the remainder of his immigration process, he could not remain in the country. The wife was the only person who could validly sponsor him. The husband claimed the family court had the power to order the wife to sponsor him either under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-1 as a matter affecting dissolution of marriage or under the court's equity power. The court found it could complete all aspects of the dissolution without entering that order and forcing the wife to participate in an immigration process that was lengthy and costly and could force her into a potential obligation to support the husband as his sponsor was not related to any of the family matters under § 46b-1. Regardless, the court would not exercise its discretion to enter the requested order. The parties had no relationship and had not lived together for six years, so there was no reason to delay the parties' divorce.


OUTCOME: The court denied the husband's motion.

 

1414 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mainville v. Zoning Comm'n of Meriden


CV980265281S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 748



March 15, 2006, Decided  
March 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Mainville v. Zoning Comm'n of Meriden, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2280 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Mainville v. Zoning Comm'n of Meriden, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3472 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 22, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city zoning commission filed a motion to dismiss claims by plaintiff property owners that the commission's approval of a zoning amendment constituted an unconstitutional taking of their property in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V and Conn. Const. art. I, § 11. The owners opposed the motion to dismiss and moved to file additional evidence.


OVERVIEW: The owners appealed approval of a zoning amendment on various grounds. The court allowed the owners to amend the appeal to add unconstitutional taking claims. The commission moved to dismiss the additional claims, arguing they were not ripe without a final decision applying the amendment to disallow any reasonable use of the property. The owners contended that the motion should be denied because it was not made within 30 days of the commission's appearance, as required by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-30, and that the court's decision to allow amendment to add the claim was law of the case. They also argued the claim was ripe. The court found that ripeness impacted subject matter jurisdiction, which could be challenged at any time, and that the issue was not previously considered, so law of the case was inapplicable. Some of the claims were not ripe without action applying the amendment to cause economic loss for which the owners were not compensated. But, claims that the commission exceeded its authority in approving the amendment and that the amendment did not fit the city's comprehensive plan were facial challenges that were ripe when the amendment was enacted.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed those parts of the owners' additional claims that raised as-applied taking claims, but the court denied the motion to dismiss those claims that raised facial challenges to the amendment.

 

1415 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


D'Amato v. Gov't Admin. & Elections Comm.


CV054012032


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 740



March 9, 2006, Decided  
March 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the state legislature's government administration and elections committee, and the committee's co-chairs (GAEC), moved to dismiss an action by plaintiffs, a building company and several individuals , who filed a complaint for injunctive and declaratory relief that would protect them against enforcement of legislative subpoenas that the GAEC issued to compel plaintiffs' attendance at committee hearings.


OVERVIEW: In seeking protection from the GAEC's subpoenas, the plaintiffs alleged that the GAEC was not authorized to issue them, that the subpoenas were improperly served, and that issuance of the subpoenas fell outside the protections of the speech or debate clause (SDC) of Conn. Const. art. III, § 15. The GAEC moved to dismiss, claiming the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction due to SDC immunity. They claimed that the subpoenas were issued in furtherance of the GAEC's consideration of possible revisions to state ethics laws, which was squarely within the matters delegated to the GAEC by the state's joint rules of the senate and house of representatives. The court found that, if the GAEC's subpoenas were within its sphere of legitimate legislative activity, the GAEC was absolutely immune from judicial review. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 2-46(a) specifically authorized the legislature to issue subpoenas. Op. Conn. Att'y. Gen. 84-130 (November 16, 1984) stated that the § 2-46(a) subpoena powers were intended to be comprehensive. Since the GAEC's ethics investigation was within its sphere of legitimate legislative activity, issuance of the subpoenas was protected by the SDC.


OUTCOME: The court granted the GAEC's motion to dismiss.

 

1416 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Watkins v. Snider


CV054011876


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 729



March 7, 2006, Decided  
March 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed suit against defendants, his attorney, his attorney's office, the retired chief of legal services for the public defender services, and the State of Connecticut, for violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and common law claims. The Attorney General for Connecticut filed a motion to dismiss on behalf of the State and the retired chief of legal services. The attorney filed a motion to dismiss on behalf of himself and his law office.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that (1) he did not have proper assistance of counsel; (2) the attorney misled the inmate; (3) the attorney gave him false information under oath and committed perjury against the inmate, and (4) the chief of legal services was negligent in his actions and responsible for the actions of the attorney. The court found that (1) the doctrine of sovereign immunity barred the inmate from suing the State of Connecticut; (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 barred the claims against the chief of legal services as there were no allegations that he acted recklessly, wantonly, or maliciously or outside the scope of his employment; (3) 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 did not support a claim based on respondeat superior; (4) the allegation that the chief of legal services was negligent in failing to respond to letters by the inmate was not a constitutional tort under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; and (5) the attorney, as a special public defender, did not act under color of state law under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. However the attorney and his office were not immune to the common law claims. Further, the inmate stated a cause of action against the attorney and his office as to the common law claims.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the complaint against the retired chief of legal services and the State of Connecticut was granted. The motion to dismiss the civil rights claims against the attorney and his law office was also granted, but the motion to dismiss the common law claims against the attorney and his law office was denied.

 

1417 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Plourde v. Hartford Hosp.


HHDCV020814180S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 608



February 28, 2006, Decided  
February 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a doctor and a physicians company (doctors), moved for summary judgment on the counts against them in plaintiff administrator's wrongful death complaint. The administrator brought consortium claims individually and wrongful death claims as temporary administrator for the estate of his wife, alleging medical malpractice against the doctors and against other health care provider defendants who did not move for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The administrator alleged that negligent care provided by the doctors and others resulted in serious injuries to, and the subsequent death of, his wife. Before expiration of the two year statute of limitations under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555 (SOL), the administrator filed for, and received, an automatic 90-day extension of the SOL pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a(b). On summary judgment, the doctors argued that the § 52-190a(b) petition was facially defective, and that § 52-190a(b) was unconstitutional since it divested a property right in the limitations period provided by the SOL through an ex parte procedure. The court found that a facial error in transposing names was not fatal to the petition. Also, the SOL was modified by § 52-190a(b) after the administrator filed a good faith certificate in compliance with § 52-190a(a), thereby creating a property right to a limitations period of 2 years and 90 days. The certificate was a benefit to the doctors by forcing an adequate investigation of the claims, and it was a burden on the administrator that ordinary personal injury and wrongful death claimants did not have. The automatic extension was necessary to offset that burden.


OUTCOME: The court denied the doctors' motion for summary judgment.

 

1418 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Concepcion v. Caban


FA900308116S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 493



February 14, 2006, Decided  
February 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Family Support Magistrate (Connecticut), which found in favor of respondent father and dismissed petitioner mother's action for child support from the father.


OVERVIEW: This was an appeal by the State from a decision dismissing the mother's action for child support from the father, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-231(n). The father filed a motion to dismiss the appeal, arguing that the appeal was untimely and moot. The court did dismiss the appeal, stating that in order to prevail the State was required to establish that the magistrate interfered with a function that had been assigned exclusively to the office of the attorney general. Nothing in the State's legislative or constitutional scheme granted the office of the attorney general the power to direct the conduct of support enforcement officers, employees of the judicial branch. Nothing prevented magistrates from imposing reasonable rules and regulations upon those support enforcement officers. Thus, the separation of powers argument failed. The State also argued that the magistrate interfered with support enforcement's authority to act pursuant to § 46b-231(s)(1). The court disagreed however, stating that the restriction was on a non-party. There was no injunction. There were no monetary sanctions. The litigants were allowed to file any motion they wished to pursue.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the State's appeal.

 

1419 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Chamberland v. Physicians for Women's Health, LLC


CV010164040S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 451



February 8, 2006, Decided  
February 8, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the parents of a child born with spina bifida, sued defendant physicians group, claiming that, as a result of defendant's negligence, the mother did not have a blood test that was available during pregnancy to determine the risk of the defect. A jury awarded economic damages of five million dollars to the parents and awarded non-economic damages of five million dollars to the mother and two million dollars to the father.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed motions to set aside the verdict, for judgment notwithstanding the verdict, for remittitur, to preclude an award of interest under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a, and to offset the verdict by collateral source payments. The court denied those motions, holding that the law in Connecticut permitted damages for emotional distress in wrongful birth cases where, as in the case at bar, the emotional distress was a direct and proximate result of the defendant's negligence. The court also held that: (1) there was no support for the contention that defendant owed no duty to the father, and the jury finding as to the father was supported by sufficient evidence, even though the father did testify about his own emotional distress; (2) there was no error in admitting evidence of the licensing status of an employee midwife, evidence from the mother concerning the course she would have taken, or evidence of the child's physical condition and his interaction with the parents; (3) the evidence supported the damage awards; and (4) an award of prejudgment interest under Conn. Gen. Stat § 52-192a was proper because, contrary to defendant's argument, the statute did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motions.

Walsh v. State


X03CV054006939


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 359



February 1, 2006, Decided  
February 1, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Corrections (DOC), the Deputy Commissioner of the DOC, a warden, a social worker, psychiatrists, a nurse, a psychologist, and corrections officers, moved to dismiss nine counts of a complaint brought by plaintiff estate administrators for violations of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1985, the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution, and intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: The administrators, the decedent's father and sister, brought an action against defendants, alleging that the decedent hung himself with a bedsheet tied to the top bunk in his cell while in the custody of the Connecticut Department of Corrections. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-30, defendants filed a motion to dismiss nine counts of the complaint. Defendants claimed that all of the claims against them were barred by state common-law sovereign immunity and state statutory immunity. The court found that the motion to dismiss based on sovereign immunity should be denied. The complaint could be reasonably construed to bring claims against defendants in their individual capacities. Further, statutory immunity, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165, was not available to defendants. To permit the defense of state statutory immunity to be asserted would undermine the supremacy of federal law. Finally, the ninth count, which alleged intentional infliction of emotional distress, alleged conduct that was wanton, reckless, or malicious, bringing the alleged conduct within the exception contained in § 4-165b.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss nine counts of the complaint.

Town of Canterbury v. Vargas


CV044000431


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WINDHAM, AT PUTNAM


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 458



January 26, 2006, Decided  
January 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a town, its planning commission (commission), and its wetlands commission, sued defendant business owners contending that their junkyard violated Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 14-67g et seq. and 22a-36 et seq., as well as the town's zoning regulations. Plaintiffs also sought injunctive relief. The business owners answered, asserting five special defenses, and filed a post-trial brief challenging the town's zoning and wetland regulations.


OVERVIEW: All of the claims posed by the business owners as to the validity or enforceability of the town's zoning and wetlands regulations, as well as their constitutional claims, could have been raised in the context of an administrative appeal or in an independent declaratory judgment action. Further, the business owners failed to present any authority, nor was any authority found, indicating that such claims could, instead, be raised as special defenses to an enforcement action. The business owners also failed to appeal from the supplemental cease and desist order issued by the zoning enforcement officer, nor did they demonstrate that such an appeal would have been futile. In fact, though they loosely attempted to attack the validity of the regulations applied against them in issuing the cease and desist orders, the Zoning Board of Appeals could have offered practical relief to them by either revoking or modifying the cease and desist order.


OUTCOME: The court lacked jurisdiction to address the business owners' special defenses regarding the enforceability and validity of the regulations upon which the orders were issued.


 

1422 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Simsbury-Avon Pres. Soc'y, LLC v. Town of Simsbury


X01CV044001892S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 453



January 26, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff preservation society's claim for mandamus relief, which alleged that the town had a duty to enforce federal, state, and municipal laws and not to allow town residents, specifically defendant company, to violate those laws. The company brought an apportionment complaint against defendant Department of Public Safety officials under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-102(b), asserting, inter alia, negligence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff argued that the exhaustion of administrative remedies would be futile because the town had demonstrated an absolute unwillingness to act. The court rejected plaintiff's claim of futility. It was undisputed that no evidence had been adduced that plaintiff, or any of its members, ever exercised the right to appeal a zoning officer's opinion following her investigation. Because plaintiff offered no analysis, the court could not conclude that the remedies available to it by way of injunctive and/or declaratory relief against the company were inadequate. Nor could the court conclude that plaintiff had a clear legal right to the relief sought in that discovery was ongoing and the evidence was incomplete. The court found that the apportionment complaint did not sound in a cause of action other than negligence and that the officials were not immune from suit in their official capacities under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. However, the court concluded that it was without personal jurisdiction over the officials regarding plaintiff's original complaint because the apportionment complaint was untimely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-102b.


OUTCOME: The court granted the town's motion to dismiss. The court also granted the officials' motion to dismiss.

 

1423 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


JV III Constr., Inc. v. Town of Rocky Hill


CV000803959S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 241



January 24, 2006, Decided  
January 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff incorporated businesses brought an action against defendant town, seeking a declaration that an ordinance regulating truck traffic had been enacted in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-298 and that it violated due process and equal protection guarantees under the United States and Connecticut Constitutions. They also sought awards of money damages to cover the losses they claimed to have sustained.


OVERVIEW: When the town decided to limit truck traffic in an area that had grown increasingly residential, it modeled its ordinance on one that had been found constitutional some years earlier, and it adopted the same weight limit for trucks to be banned from a stretch of road. The ordinance contained an exemption for certain truck-owning businesses that were near the beginning of the restricted stretch, on grounds that avoiding the road would cause their trucks to drive through even more residential neighborhoods. Other local businesses that had not been exempted challenged the ordinance, first, as violating § 14-298, which required approval of a state agency for any local legislation that affected through traffic and, second, as violating constitutional guarantees. The latter claim boiled down to a challenge under the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The court held, first, that since the businesses' trucks were not engaged in through traffic, since they were based in the town, they lacked standing under § 14-298. Second, the ordinance was rationally based in the desire to reduce noise and protect pedestrians in residential neighborhoods.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment for the town on all counts.

 

1424 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hicks v. Warden


CV020345064S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 191



January 20, 2006, Decided  
January 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Hicks, 101 Conn. App. 16, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 192 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Hicks, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3546 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 26, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner was convicted of burglary in the first degree and assault in the first degree. The petitioner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner argued, inter alia, that a witness should not have been called because her cross-examination brought out the fact that she had pleaded guilty to conspiracy to commit burglary. The habeas court disagreed. Counsel called the witness based on the petitioner's assertion that the witness had indicated that the victim had changed her story and was not sure if the petitioner had been one of the persons who committed the crime. Counsel's litigation decision to call the witness was made after the petitioner informed counsel that her testimony could be used to discredit the victim's testimony. That was an informed strategic choice made by counsel for the petitioner on information supplied by the petitioner and clearly met the performance prong of Strickland. A fair assessment of counsel's performance required that every effort be made to eliminate the distorting effects of hindsight and to reconstruct the circumstances of counsel's challenged conduct and evaluate the conduct from counsel's perspective at the time. The petitioner failed to prove that counsel's performance was deficient and also failed to prove that his performance in calling the witness prejudiced the defense.


OUTCOME: The petition was dismissed.

 

1425 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Desimini v. Bristol Hosp., Inc.


HHBCV054003250S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 120



January 12, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executrix, on behalf of an estate and herself, brought a wrongful death action against defendant hospital, for alleged medical malpractice that caused the death of the decedent. The executrix, as an executrix, obtained a 90-day extension of the applicable statute of limitations from the clerk of the superior court pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a. The hospital filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The hospital claimed that service of the complaint was untimely. It further claimed it was deprived of a vested property right in violation of the due process clause of the Fourteenth Amendment as the ex parte procedure in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a(b), which extended the statute of limitations by 90 days, deprived the hospital of its vested property right to an exemption, if suit was not brought within two years. The court found that the hospital had property rights, not in a two-year limitation period, but in a statute of limitations of two years and 90 days. Because the hospital did not have a vested property right in a two-year statute of limitations, the automatic extension in § 52-190a(b) did not give rise to a violation of constitutional rights. Further, a loss of consortium claim was not untimely under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555 as the executrix's petition for extension of the statute of limitation extended by 90 days the time in which the claim had to be brought. Finally, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-593a, a remedial statute, applied to extend the statute of limitations contained in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555, which was extended by the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-190a(b).


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was denied.

Van Winkle v. Town of Stonington


CV030567071S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 132



January 12, 2006, Decided  
January 13, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-111, appealed the assessment of his property to appellee Board of Assessment Appeals of the Town of Stonington, Connecticut, which reduced the assessment. The property owner petitioned for review of the Board's assessment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a.


OVERVIEW: The owner disputed the value that was assigned to his property in an assessment. He alleged the violation of two Connecticut statutes; namely, Con. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-62a(b) and 12-119; and a violation of the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, as well as a violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 20. The owner claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119 provided relief to taxpayers who proved that an assessment was manifestly excessive as a result of the assessors violating statutory directives in arriving at the assessment. As to the constitutional challenges, the owner claimed that by assessing shoreline properties at a higher rate than inland properties the assessor and the Board placed a higher burden on owners of shoreline properties in violation of their right to equal protection. The court found that the property assessed in the town, including the owner's property, was valued at 70 percent in compliance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-62a(b). Accordingly, the assessment of the owner's property was neither excessive nor illegal, and the assessment did not violate Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119. Further, there was no evidence which supported an equal protection violation.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Groton Landing, LTD v. Lambtown Dev., LLC


4004594


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 74



January 11, 2006, Decided  
January 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss denied without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant paving company moved to dismiss plaintiff property owner's application to dissolve the company's mechanic's lien pursuant to the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-35b.


OVERVIEW: The owner did not pay the company for paving work on its in-state property, which resulted in a mechanic's lien. The owner commenced an action to dissolve the lien. The company moved to dismiss the action, claiming Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-921(a) precluded the owner from bringing an action in the state since it failed to obtain a certificate of authority (CA) to transact business in the state. The owner claimed that its rights to open courts and to not have its property alienated by the lien would be violated if the action were dismissed. The owner further contended that § 33-921 was unconstitutional because it was tantamount to a bill of attainder and violated due process. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 33-921(c) permitted a stay to allow foreign businesses an opportunity to obtain a CA. The stay would not bar the owner from protecting any of its rights to open courts or to the non-alienation of property. Finally, the court determined that the stay procedure in § 33-921 was not a bill of attainder since it applied to future, not past, conduct and since it had a clear, nonpunitive purpose of equalizing tax burdens between foreign and domestic corporations.


OUTCOME: The court denied the company's motion to dismiss without prejudice and ordered the owner to obtain a CA to transact business in the state. The court stayed the owner's motion to dissolve the mechanic's lien it obtained a CA or until further orders by the court.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a prison inmate, sued defendants, doctors and university officials, alleging medical malpractice. Defendants moved to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner alleged that the doctors failed to prescribe the proper medications and tests or to order the proper diet for the control of his diabetes and cholesterol problems, and that a university review committee failed to institute proper medical protocols for inmate treatment and testing. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint because it improperly alleged a class action, and because the action was barred either by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The court found that the prisoner had abandoned any claims concerning class action status. The court found that the prisoner filed the action against defendants in their official capacities as state officers. When a plaintiff brought an action for money damages against the state, the plaintiff had to proceed through the office of the Claims Commissioner pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 et seq. Otherwise, the action had to be dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction under the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The complaint in this case did not sufficiently allege any statutory exceptions to sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

Machado v. City of New Haven


CV044004852S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3619



December 27, 2005, Decided  
December 27, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion to strike denied by Machado v. City of New Haven, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2709 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 11, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to strike all three counts of the plaintiff's complaint granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city filed a motion to strike plaintiff car owner's claims that his constitutional rights were violated by the city's enforcement of parking regulations and by its use of an infrared license plate scanning device to identify vehicles with delinquent tax obligations, vehicles that are improperly registered, stolen vehicles and citizens with criminal violations, and that a temporary injunction was warranted.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected all of the owner's constitutional challenges, including his illegal search and seizure claims under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 7, and his due process claims under U.S. Const. amend. V, XIV, and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. the owner did not allege any facts that would demonstrate an illegal seizure of his vehicle, especially where police were allowed to remove and impound automobiles that violated parking ordinances, impeded traffic, or threatened public safety. As to due process, the owner's own allegations showed that he received notice of the city's parking policies and his violation of these policies. Moreover, he had notice on his parking tickets of the appeal period and of the city's policy of towing vehicles that accrued more than $ 200 in fines. Therefore, he failed to show a lack of due process. The owner had no privacy interest in the city observing his license plate number where such license plates were required to be displayed under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-18. Finally, without proof of likelihood of success, the owner was not entitled to an injunction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the city's motion to strike all counts of the owner's complaint.

 

1431 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fair Haven Dev. Corp. v. City of New Haven


CV030480003S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3540



December 15, 2005, Decided  
December 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed without opinion by Fair Haven Dev. Corp. v. City of New Haven, 100 Conn. App. 905, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 164 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-profit corporation filed suit against defendant City seeking to quiet title to certain real property. The corporation was permitted to conform its complaint to the evidence. The amended complaint re-alleged that any claimed delay in the corporation's performance of its obligations was caused by the City's failure to release funds to it.


OVERVIEW: The corporation argued that the deed and the agreement were ambiguous and vague. The trial court held that the corporation failed to submit floor plans and specifications of proposed rehabilitation work as required by the agreement. "Commenced construction of the improvements" was not too vague and ambiguous to have been understood by the parties. The corporation did not begin construction on the property. The corporation's construction obligations were not contingent on an award of funds from the City. The reversionary interest in the deed was valid. The City took action to divest the corporation of the property as required by the quitclaim deed. The corporation was not prejudiced by any failure to comply with the quiet title statute. The City was not equitably estopped from claiming a default. The claim that the reversionary interest was void as it violated the rule against perpetuities was rejected as it was not raised in the pleadings. Further, the rule against perpetuities was not applicable to the City. The documents were not illegal or in violation of any public policy. Finally, the claim that the reversionary interest allowed an unconstitutional taking was not considered.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered in favor of the City. Title to the subject property was found to be in the City, to the exclusion of the corporation.

 

1432 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Toffolon v. Plainville Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV030522278S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3277



November 22, 2005, Decided  
November 22, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a landowner owner and a proposed lessee of the land (applicants), appealed denial of their special exception application and site plan approval by defendant local planning and zoning commission.


OVERVIEW: The applicants sought a special exception under Plainville, Ct., Zoning Regulations, § 502, to operate a weekly wholesale motor vehicle auction week and to allow related inventory accumulation and distribution activities. The commission denied the application. The applicants appealed, raising four claims: (1) that the commission's use of the local plan of conservation and development to reject the applications was erroneous; (2) that the commission did not form a consensus that the proposed use was a prohibited junk yard; (3) that, assuming storing "junk" was one of the commission's reasons for denying the application, the definition of "junk" in the zoning regulations was vague; and (4) that the reasons given by the commission lacked substantial evidence. The court found that the zoning regulations for granting special exceptions required compliance with the plan, so denial could be based on failure to satisfy the plan. Moreover, the record showed that the commission found the proposed use was to store "junk," the definition of "junk" was not unconstitutionally vague, and substantial evidence supported a finding that storing inoperable motor vehicles constituted storing "junk."


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the applicants' appeal.

Cambodian Buddhist Soc'y of Ct., Inc. v. Newtown Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV030350572S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3158



November 18, 2005, Decided  
November 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Cambodian Buddhist Soc'y of Conn. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Newtown, 2008 Conn. LEXIS 41 (Conn., Feb. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Cambodian Buddhist Danbury Soc'y of Conn., Inc. v. Newtown Planning & Zoning Comm'n, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1405 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 25, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff religious society appealed a decision by defendant town planning and zoning commission denying the society's application for a special exception to construct a place of religious worship on its property, which was zoned farming and residential, but did not permit the religious structure. The society added defendant abutting landowners when they sought to intervene.


OVERVIEW: In appealing the commission's denial of its application for a special exception to build a place of religious worship on its property, the society claimed the decision: (1) was arbitrary, illegal, and an abuse of its discretion; (2) violated the Connecticut Religious Freedom Act (RFA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-571b; and (3) violated the Religious Land Use and Institutionalized Persons Act (RLUIPA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000cc et seq. The court found the society did not show selective treatment to make out a prima facie equal protection claim. It also did not show the commission placed a substantial burden, as required for a RLUIPA claim, or even a burden, as required for a RFA claim, on the exercise of its religion. There was no evidence that the society could not use other sites in the town to build its place of worship, nor was there evidence that the commission would not impose the same traffic and safety requirements on any other entity seeking to build on the property. Finally, the commission did not act illegally, arbitrarily, or in abuse of discretion in applying town traffic and health regulations as reasons to deny the application.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the society's appeal.

Hanton v. Massarri


CV05400314


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2935



November 2, 2005, Decided  
November 2, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former halfway house resident filed an amended complaint seeking to bring five causes of action based on alleged violations of his right to practice religion under the federal constitution, the state constitution, and federal and state statutory law. He also attempted to assert a breach of contract claim. Defendant halfway house officials moved to strike the claims and his request for punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The former halfway house resident filed a pro se amended complaint that sought to bring causes of action based on an alleged violation of his right to practice religion under the United States Constitution, the Connecticut Constitution, the Connecticut General Statutes, and the federal Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb (Act). He also contended that the halfway house officials retaliated against him for filing a civil complaint against them, again in violation of Connecticut state statutes, and that they breached a contract with the resident, also allegedly in violation of Connecticut statutes. The halfway house officials filed a motion to strike the claims and the former halfway house resident's request for punitive damages. The trial court granted the motion and ordered that all of the claims and the request for punitive damages be stricken. The trial court found that none of the claims stated a cause of action; indeed, it found that the Act had been declared invalid by the United States Supreme Court. It also held that the resident had not pled sufficient facts to show the wanton, wilful, or malicious conduct necessary to recover punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The trial court ordered that all five counts of the former halfway house resident's complaint be stricken. Likewise, the trial court ordered that his claim for relief for punitive damages be stricken.

 

1435 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV000800455


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2845



October 26, 2005, Decided  
October 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus for review of his conviction and sentence for felony murder under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54a and 53a-54c. Petitioner alleged that he was deprived of the effective assistance of trial counsel due to his counsel's failure to perfect an application for sentence review as provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-195 and that there was insufficient evidence to sustain the guilty verdict.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought habeas relief based on his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. The court found that trial counsel's failure to perfect petitioner's sentence review application as provided in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-195 was deficient performance, but that there was no basis upon which the court could conclude that there was any unreliability in his murder conviction; therefore the court granted limited habeas relief and restored petitioner's right to sentence review and denied habeas relief as to the conviction. The court found that petitioner's trial counsel provided quality representation, which resulted in petitioner being spared the death penalty despite the egregious and horrendous nature of his crimes. The court also held that petitioner's felony murder conviction was supported by sufficient evidence that showed petitioner's brother shot a police officer during the commission of a robbery with petitioner. The court found that it was petitioner's decision to exercise his constitutional right to silence at his trial and that even if he had testified there was no probability that the result would have been any different.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's request for a writ of habeas corpus in the narrow form of restoring petitioner's right to a sentence review but denied his habeas petition as to his felony murder conviction.

Johnson v. Conn. Juvenile Training Sch.


CV054003278


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2726



October 20, 2005, Decided  
October 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Connecticut Juvenile Training School (school); the Connecticut Department of Children & Families (DCF); the DCF Commissioner; the school's Superintendent; and the former school Superintendent, all sought dismissal of plaintiff employee's four-count intentional tort complaint filed against them on subject matter jurisdiction grounds pursuant to the doctrine of sovereign immunity. This matter followed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the present action because the employee did not receive permission to sue them from the claims commission or, in the alternative, because she failed to bring the action pursuant to a statute in which the State had consented to be sued. However, the employee relied on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 by alleging that defendants engaged in intentional tortuous conduct. She also argued that her claims were viable in that they were based on conduct by defendants that violated § 4-165, but her reliance on this statute was misplaced. Additionally, the third and fourth criteria under the test outlined in Spring v. Constantino were not met and the state indemnification statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-141d, was not applicable if the state officer/employee was wanton, reckless, or malicious in his or her acts. Thus, a judgment against the Commissioner, the Superintendent, and the former Superintendent on the basis of wanton, reckless, or malicious conduct would not subject the state to liability.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss is granted with respect to the school and the DCF and the individual defendants, the Commissioner, the Superintendent, and the former Superintendent in their official capacities.
