Chieffo v. Clifford


CV040287687S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2816



October 20, 2005, Decided  
October 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured person sued defendants, a car driver, a car lessor, and a car lessee, after the vehicle the injured person was driving was struck by a vehicle being driven by the car driver. The car lessor had leased the car driver's car to the car lessee. The car lessor moved for summary judgment to challenge the injured person's claim that it was vicariously liable to her.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was hurt when the vehicle she was operating was struck by a vehicle being operated by the car driver. The car driver's vehicle was owned by the car lessor and had been leased to the car lessee. The injured person alleged that the car lessor was vicariously liable for her injuries pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a, which applied to renters and lessors. The car lessor moved for summary judgment and supplied supporting documents that it claimed showed it could not be held liable pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b)(1), which carved out an exception to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a liability for lessors, because it had met Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b)(1)'s exception requirements. The injured party did not dispute that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-154a(b)(1) applied, but claimed that it had an impermissible retroactive effect, it violated equal protection, and it violated public policy. The trial court granted the car lessor's summary judgment motion. It found that the statute was in effect on the day of the accident and, thus, was not applied retroactively, that it did not violate constitutional equal protection, and that it did not violate public policy.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the car lessor's motion for summary judgment.

 

1438 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Noemi B.


H14CP05008118A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, JUVENILE MATTERS AT PLAINVILLE


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2936



October 20, 2005, Decided  
October 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Findings of fact/conclusions of law at, Judgment entered by In re Shakyra C., 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1844 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 15, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner guardian ad litem (GAL) for respondent teenage minor sought a continuation of the court's earlier issued, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-129, order of temporary custody (OTC) placing custody in the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF). Nominal respondent parents urged the petition be granted, while the minor, through her attorney, and DCF opposed it.


OVERVIEW: The minor's parents could not handle her. Her truancy and substance abuse were ongoing, and she eventually ran away to live with an older boyfriend. Although her attorney had not seen her in months, he appeared on her behalf when a GAL argued for the need to continue the OTC that had been in place, to at least give the State an opportunity to try to save her, if she could be found. The court held that Connecticut case law established the same burdens of proof for ex parte OTC proceedings and for formal contested proceedings. The petitioner in such a case had to show by a fair preponderance of the evidence that the child's safety and well-being were actually in danger. The showing could, however, be predictive, that is, a showing by a fair preponderance that the child would be endangered if not protected could support an OTC. The court held that in the minor's case, the evidence was more than adequate that the minor could not be cared for adequately by either parent. Therefore, it granted the continuation petition.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition.

 

1439 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lagassey v. State


CV010807201S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


50 Conn. Supp. 130; 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2810; 913 A.2d 1153



October 18, 2005, Decided  
October 19, 2005, Memorandum Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 9, 2007.
Affirmed by Lagassey v. State, 281 Conn. 1, 914 A.2d 509, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 8 (Conn., Jan. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Lagassey v. State, 268 Conn. 723, 846 A.2d 831, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 183 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the wife of a decedent, filed a wrongful death and loss of consortium action against defendant, the State of Connecticut. The State moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The decedent died while being treated at a university hospital operated by the State. The wife argued that hospital personnel failed to failing to properly diagnose and/or treat a leaking aneurysm, and negligently failed to operate to correct the condition. In the summary judgment motion, the State argued that the action was barred by the statute of limitation for wrongful death actions under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-555(a). The wife argued that the tolling provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160(d) renewed the statute of limitations when the wife filed a claim with a state agency. The court held that the tolling provision contained in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160(d) merely provided an extension of time in which to bring a claim. It did not, however, authorize the limitation period contained in § 52-555(a) to begin anew. The court found that the time the agency spent reviewing the claim was tolled, but that after the agency authorized the claim, the statute of limitations began to run again. The court further held that the wife failed to file the action against the State before the statute of limitations expired. Thus, the State was entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1440 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hand v. Moore


FSTCV052BJ4003873S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2647



September 26, 2005, Decided  
September 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff automobile accident victim sued defendant driver for personal injuries allegedly resulting from the driver's negligence and statutory recklessness under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-295. The victim sought money damages and double and treble damages pursuant to § 14-295. The driver moved to strike the second count of the complaint and the claim for double and treble damages. The victim filed an objection to the motion to strike.


OVERVIEW: The driver argued that the victim could not allege identical facts in both the recklessness and negligence counts, nor penalize the driver for a negligence complaint disguised as a recklessness claim. Additionally, the driver argued that the recklessness claim had to be specifically pleaded. The court found that the specific pleading requirements for pleading common-law recklessness did not apply to pleading a case of statutory recklessness under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-295. Further, allegations that the driver deliberately or with reckless disregard operated a motor vehicle in violation of one or more of the motor vehicle statutes enumerated in § 14-295 and that the violation was a substantial factor in producing the victim's injuries were sufficient to state a case of statutory recklessness. Additionally, the allegations in the second count validly pleaded a case of recklessness under § 14-295, and, even if the common-law pleading requirements for recklessness were applied, the second count satisfied those requirements as well. Finally, because the second count was not to be stricken, the prayer for relief seeking double or treble damages under § 14-295 was also not to be stricken.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was denied, and the objection to the motion to strike was sustained.

 

1441 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


White v. United States of America Track & Field, Inc.


CV040489840S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2536



September 19, 2005, Decided  
September 19, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by White v. United States Track & Field, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1182 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 18, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an injured party, sued defendants, organizations, a university, a coach, and others, to recover damages for injuries allegedly sustained while warming up for the pole vaulting event at a track meet. The university and the coach moved to dismiss counts one and three of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Count one alleged that the university and the coach were negligent in failing to properly supervise the meet, failing to properly train and supervise employees, and inadequately maintaining the warm-up area. Count three alleged recklessness on the part of the university and the coach. The university and coach argued that they were immune from suit pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. At oral argument, the injured party admitted that he was not opposing the motion to dismiss as to count one and that the motion to dismiss should be granted with respect to the university as to count three. The court found that under the Spring test, the action against the coach was in effect against the state. The coach was a state official, and the action occurred during his employment at a state university. The injured party did not allege anywhere that he was suing the coach in his individual capacity. Thus, the court held that the coach was immune pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. Furthermore, the court found that the injured party failed to show any wanton or reckless conduct on the part of the coach. Thus, the motion to dismiss the third count had to be granted as to the coach as well.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss counts one and three of the complaint by the university and the coach was granted for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

Tylerville Home Ctr. v. Haddam Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV040104469


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2593



September 14, 2005, Decided  
September 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners, appealed from the decision of defendant, a city zoning board of appeals, which denied their appeal of a decision of the city's zoning enforcement officer, who issued a cease and desist order for the removal of a display trailer parked in the front yard set back of the owners' property.


OVERVIEW: The enforcement officer issued the cease and desist order to compel the owners to remove a display trailer which was parked in the set off in front of their property for advertising purposes for the business located on the property. The court initially held that the owners were aggrieved pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(a)(1) based on their ownership of the property. The owners argued that the trailer was not a structure as defined by the city's zoning regulations and thus it was not unlawful to keep the trailer in the setback. The court held that the board's determination that the trailer was a structure was supported by the Haddam, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 3, which defined a structure as a walled or building and other structures. The trailer was eight feet wide, 20 feet long, and was enclosed. Furthermore, the site plan clearly showed that the trailer took up several parking spots, rather than a single vehicle spot. Thus, the court held that the board's decision was supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Scully v. Hartford


CV054010763


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2607



September 13, 2005, Decided  
September 13, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court denies the defendants' motion for summary judgment as to count six, grants the motion for summary judgment as to counts one, two, three, four, five and seven, and grants the motion to dismiss count eight.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, several developers, a town, and the town council, filed a combined motion for summary judgment on plaintiff town residents' counts alleging the town exceeded its grant of authority and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1, by approving an ordinance authorizing municipal bonds and allowing a special services district (SSD). They moved to dismiss a count alleging the council exceeded its authority in allowing the SSD.


OVERVIEW: The residents challenged a town ordinance issuing bonds and approving master agreements (MA) allowing an SSD that was favorable to the developers. They alleged the town exceeded its authority in many ways, including granting exclusive public privileges to the developers contrary to Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. They also claimed the town acted arbitrarily, the MA unfairly placed the burden of repaying bonds on taxpayers outside the SSD without a vote, and the council improperly approved the SSD. The town, developers, and council sought summary judgment on all counts except they sought dismissal of the challenge to the council's action. The court found Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c)(3)(A) allowed the town to dispose of property for public purposes, including to encourage private development. Since the SSD was created for a public purpose, the town did not exceed it authority. Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1, was not violated as public purpose was served. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-339s allowed the bond repayment. The residents raised an issue on whether the town acted arbitrarily. But, dismissal was granted since the residents had standing under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(b) to challenge council's action.


OUTCOME: The court granted the town and the developers summary judgment on all counts except the one alleging the town acted arbitrarily in issuing the bonds and in entering the MA. The court granted dismissal of the count challenging the council's decision allowing the SSD.

Gevers v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV040093063S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2365



September 6, 2005, Decided  
September 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, neighbors, appealed from the decision of defendant, a city zoning commission, to grant a special permit to defendant, a golf club, for construction of a private golf course and for earth excavation in connection with the construction of the course and related amenities.


OVERVIEW: The club proposed to build a private golf course. The portion located in Norfolk was located in a rural residential zone, and a special permit was required. The neighbors argued that the commission acted illegally and arbitrarily and in abuse of its discretion in making it a condition of approval that all construction traffic flow though a single road, while a second road was available in the area. The court held that there was evidence in the record from which the commission could have concluded that the second road was simply inadequate to handle construction traffic while the designated road was capable of handling such traffic. The commission was allowed to impose conditions on a special permit necessary to protect public safety as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2. The neighbors also argued that the commission approved the use of two guest cottages for temporary lodging of members and guests. Norfolk, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 180-24B(11) allowed for customary accessory services, as well as golf, on the property. The court held that the commission did not abuse its discretion in determining that the guest cottages would be a customary accessory service.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Lewis v. H.N.S. Mgmt. Co.


040490979S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2419



September 2, 2005, Decided  
September 2, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant bus company filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff passenger's claim for uninsured motorist benefits (UMB) on the ground that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the company was an arm of the state and, as such, was entitled to sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: The passenger alleged a claim for UMB against the company. The passenger was injured while riding on a bus operated by the company that was struck by an unidentified vehicle, thus causing the passenger numerous injuries. The passenger alleged that the unidentified vehicle qualified as an uninsured motor vehicle, and the company was self-insured and obligated to provide her with UMB. The company filed a motion to dismiss on sovereign immunity grounds. The court found it was undisputed that, in a prior decision, the company had been found to be an arm of the state and entitled to sovereign immunity from UMB claims under identical facts. The court then determined that the decision that the company was an arm of the state was one that could be applied to actions that accrued before the date of that decision. Therefore, the company was entitled to sovereign immunity as an arm of the state.


OUTCOME: The court granted the company's motion to dismiss.

Thomas v. Warden


File No. CV-02 0814633S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


49 Conn. Supp. 416; 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3674; 891 A.2d 1016



August 30, 2005, Memorandum Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 14, 2006.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought habeas corpus relief, claiming that respondent warden wrongly classified him as a sex offender, even though he was acquitted of a sexual assault charge by a jury. He alleged violations of the Fourteenth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 9, and 10.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was acquitted of a sexual assault but was serving a prison term for burglary and assault convictions. In granting habeas corpus relief, the court found that petitioner and his witness were credible and that witnesses for the warden were not. In particular, the director of offender classification at respondent department of correction was not credible in his assertion that he was unaware of the departmental rule that prohibited the use, for classification purposes, of charges on which an offender was found not guilty. The court found, contrary to the department's claims, that petitioner was labeled as a sex offender. Further, petitioner had a liberty interest in not being labeled as a sex offender, his liberty interest was violated by the department, and the department burdened him with an atypical and significant hardship because the classification made him ineligible for certain programs, including minimum security facility, halfway house, work release, educational work release, and community release. The court also found that the classification punished petitioner without clear warrant of law, in violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a writ of habeas corpus and ordered the department to purge any reference to petitioner as a sex offender or as being in need of sex offender treatment; to reduce petitioner's overall risk score and sex offender treatment needs score; and to rely no further on any sex offender charge, police report, and/or presentence investigation report relating to a sexual offense in classifying him.

 

1447 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


NIPMUC Props., LLC v. PDC-El Paso Meriden, LLC


CV020281664S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2094



August 11, 2005, Decided  
August 11, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Nipmuc Props., LLC v. PDC-El Paso Meriden, LLC, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 328 (Conn. App. Ct., Aug. 7, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the original owner of a parcel of land, sought a declaratory judgment for the delivery of a lease, held in escrow, for a leasehold interest in land located in defendant town. Defendant assignee, along with the town, claimed three special defenses. The town also sought dismissal of the action based on lack of subject-matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff had owned 845 acres of land. The assignee obtained rights to the property, which had been transferred to a trust. The rights were outlined in an amended sales agreement between the trust and the original buyer. A power plant was to be constructed on the property. The amended agreement included a clause that leased back 52 acres of land to plaintiff. The lease was held in escrow by the trust. The amended agreement was further memorialized in correspondence between the parties. After the amended agreement was entered into, changes to the power plant plans required additional approval by Connecticut's sitting council (CSC). CSC approved the changes, but not the lease, and ordered that the 52 acres be transferred to the town. The court ruled in favor of the assignee and town on the first special defense that a condition precedent to delivery of the lease had not been met. The amended agreement and the correspondence required approval by CSC of both the plan changes and the lease. The court rejected the special defenses of illegal lease and collateral estoppel. The court also denied the motion to dismiss and ruled that CSC was not an indispensible party to the litigation.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's claim for a declaratory ruling in its favor was denied. Instead, the court ruled in favor of defendants' on the first special defense.

 

1448 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Doe v. Burns


CV030100254S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2164



July 19, 2005, Decided  
July 19, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, school districts and an individual, moved for summary judgment on all counts of an action brought by plaintiff former student based on a sexual assault perpetrated by a teacher.


OVERVIEW: The student became friends with a male teacher. While the student was a visitor at the teacher's house in 1978, he kissed her and touched her inappropriately. The student's mother reported the teacher's action to school officials, who failed to take any action. The third, fifth, and sixth counts alleged that defendants were vicariously liable for the teacher's negligent conduct pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n. The alleged improper conduct took place during the summer at the teacher's home. Thus, the court found that the teacher was not acting within the scope of his employment. Count seven alleged that defendants were negligent in failing to supervise, evaluate, and investigate the teacher. The court found that the fact that the teacher had taken the student to a school dance as his "date" prior to the alleged sexual assault was sufficient to raise an issue of fact as to whether the student was an identifiable victim and thus as to whether the school was immune. The court finally found that the action was brought within the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577d statute of limitations and found that defendants failed to show that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to them.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was granted in favor of defendants on counts three, five, six, and nine. Summary judgment was denied as to count seven.

Doe v. Burns


CV030100215S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2163



July 19, 2005, Decided  
July 19, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former student filed a multi-count complaint alleging that defendant teacher kissed, inappropriately touched, and sexually assaulted her many years before. The former student alleged that defendants, a school employee, regional school district, and supervisory school district, failed to investigate allegations as to the teacher. The school employee, regional school district, and supervisory school district moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The former student was approximately 37 years old when she filed a multi-count complaint against the teacher, school employee, regional school district, and supervisory school district. She alleged that the teacher inappropriately kissed and touched her as well as sexually abused her and sexually assaulted her. She alleged that the school employee, regional school district, and supervisory school district were vicariously liable for the teacher's conduct and were negligent and that she was entitled to indemnification. The school employee, regional school district, and supervisory school district filed a motion for summary judgment on her claims directed against them. The trial court found that they could not be liable to her because the teacher's sexual misconduct did not further any of their interests. It also found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-235 did not provide the former student with a direct cause of action. However, it also found that a genuine issue of material fact existed about whether they were negligent in failing to supervise, evaluate, and investigate the teacher.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted summary judgment to the school employee, regional school district, and supervisory school district on three counts alleging that they were liable to the former student under a vicarious liability theory and granted it as to her statutory indemnification claim against them. However, it denied summary judgment as to her claim that defendants negligently failed to supervise, evaluate, and investigate the teacher.

State v. Stillman


18CR02108923


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1916



July 13, 2005, Decided  
July 13, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed two motions in a criminal case. The first requested a court-ordered psychiatric examination of the child complainant. The second was a motion to dismiss, to terminate jury selection, for a continuance, and to disqualify the State Attorney's office.


OVERVIEW: In defendant's criminal case, he filed two motions. One was for a court-ordered psychiatric examination of the child complainant to determine if the complainant was capable of telling the truth. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-86h automatically allowed the child complainant to testify and that the defense's concerns could be addressed through cross-examination, including examination on the psychiatric report that allegedly indicated the child was unable to tell the truth. The court found that, as to the second motion, the first part that requested the court terminate jury selection had been previously denied and jury selection was completed. Moreover, as to the balance of the motion, it was denied in its entirety. As far as a request for a continuance went, the court had already granted a continuance that was requested by both sides and there was no indication how the State Attorney's comment that defendant's spouse was under criminal investigation compromised the witness to an incurable degree.


OUTCOME: The court denied both motions in their entirety.

 

1451 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Batts v. Corrigan Facility


CV054006037S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1843



July 8, 2005, Decided  
July 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a correctional facility, a nurse at the facility, and the commissioner of the department of correction (state officials), filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff inmate's action alleging a multitude of claims for damages. The motion alleged a lack subject matter jurisdiction due to sovereign immunity and statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that the state officials falsified evidence and disseminated false information, which defamed him, caused him to be arrested, falsely imprisoned, and placed in administrative detention, and caused him emotional distress. He also alleged wilful and malicious conduct. The state officials moved to dismiss on immunity grounds. It was unclear whether the inmate's claims for monetary damages and injunctive and declaratory relief were directed at the nurse and commissioner in their individual or official capacities. In their official capacities, the state officials were immune from monetary damage claims since there was no statutory waiver of sovereign immunity. Also, the inmate never brought his claims to the claims commissioner, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-141 through 4-165b to avoid dismissal. However, the inmate's allegations of fraudulent and illegal conduct were sufficient to claim conduct in excess of the state officials' authority, which justified declaratory and injunctive relief. In their individual capacities, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165, the state officials were not immune from liability for their reckless and willful acts.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state officials' motion to dismiss as to the inmate's claims for monetary damages in their official capacities. The court denied the motion as to the inmate's remaining claims for declaratory and injunctive relief against the state officials in their official capacities or as to his claims for monetary damages against the nurse and the commissioner in their individual capacities.

MJM Land v. Madison Inland Wetlands Agency


CV030484371S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1762



July 1, 2005, Decided  
July 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner land owners brought an appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-43, 8-8, of a decision by respondent county inland wetlands agency on applications for a regulated activity permit (RAP) that allowed the owners to build a subdivision but did not allow them to build a driveway that would disrupt a wetlands area.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought a RAP that included approval of regulated activities, including a wetlands crossing by a proposed driveway. The agency approved the RAP but denied the application insofar as it proposed to fill wetlands to build a driveway. The owners brought several issues on appeal, including whether the agency's decision was supported by substantial evidence, whether it met due process by failing to disqualify certain members from voting due to insufficient preparation or predetermination, and whether the agency stated legally sufficient findings and reasons consistent with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-42a. The court found that evidence supported the agency's determination that any destruction of the wetlands was significant and that the owners failed to meet their burden of showing that no feasible and prudent alternative to their proposal existed concerning the driveway. The court premised its dismissal of the appeal on that reasoning. The court found that evidence existed that a bridge over the wetlands as an alternative to destruction was feasible from an engineering perspective. Finally, the reasons provided in the agency's decisional order were sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

1453 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Griffin v. Seven Horses


CV054008329


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1687



June 28, 2005, Decided  
June 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the Connecticut Chief Animal Control Officer, applied for an order to show cause why he should not have permanent custody of an owner's seven horses pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22-328(b), 22-329a, 53-247(a). The owner moved to dismiss or to strike.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-328(b) authorized the Officer to seek custody of animals that were deemed neglected under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a. Under § 22-329a, the Officer could take charge of an animal neglected or cruelly treated in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22-366, 22-415, 53-247 to 53-251. Prohibited activities under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-247(a) included failing to give an animal proper care, food, drink, or protection from the weather. The statutory provisions were not unconstitutionally vague either as written or as applied to the owner. The term "neglect" was clearly defined in common use and by the statutes. A person of ordinary intelligence could determine with a reasonable degree of certainty whether her treatment of the horses violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22-329a. The court found by a preponderance of the evidence that the owner neglected her horses. Lay witnesses and the Officer's and the owner's veterinarians testified to the horses' living conditions. The corral was full of mud and muck 12 inches deep. The stalls were small. The horses were inadequately protected from cold weather. The veterinarians testified how those conditions jeopardized the horses' health.


OUTCOME: The court denied the owner's motion. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22-328(b), 22-329a, 53-247(a) were not unconstitutional as written or as applied. The court found the owner neglected the horses. The court entered its judgment for the Officer and vested ownership of the horses in the State. The court ordered the owner to pay an amount to the State toward the daily cost of the care of the horses for so long as they were in its care.

 

1454 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


McPhee v. Warden


CV054000348S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1574



June 15, 2005, Decided  
June 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus. The complaint raised the single claim that respondent warden had incorrectly determined the inmate's discharge date. The relief sought by the inmate was the application of statutory good time credits to his controlling sentence.


OVERVIEW: In Connecticut, good time eligible offenses were crimes committed prior to October 1, 1994, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d. Because the inmate's offense date, "1993-1995," straddled or overlapped October 1, 1994, it was not immediately clear whether his controlling sentence was good time eligible. It was clear to the court that the warden in good faith attempted to determine the controlling sentence and discharge date. However, the evidence showed that many instances of the offenses occurred, both prior to and after October 1, 1994. It followed that the inmate was convicted for offenses committed on or after October 1, 1994. Consequently, his controlling sentence was good time ineligible. The court found the inmate's reliance on Rawls and the rule of lenity was misplaced, as there was neither an ambiguity in the applicable good time statutes that triggered the rule of lenity, nor was there any risk of harsher punishment. Blakely was also inapplicable. The critical issue in Blakely was a sentence exceeding the standard range. The underlying sentences in the instant petition did not exceed the statutorily permissible maximum, nor had the inmate made such an allegation.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered denying the petition for a writ of habeas corpus.

 

1455 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Sullins v. Myers


CV044001215S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1473



June 6, 2005, Decided  
June 6, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument granted by, Adhered to Sullins v. Rodriguez, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1532 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 21, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff former inmate's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 suit against defendants, a corrections officer (CO) and a prison warden, the inmate sought to strike the CO's and the warden's special defenses of sovereign immunity, immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165, and failure to exhaust remedies under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 and their claims of setoff. The warden and the CO sought to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sued the warden and the CO in their individual capacities under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 on alleged federal constitutional rights violations after the CO placed him in a locked room with an inmate who assaulted him after he requested segregation from that inmate because he feared an attack. The warden and the CO claimed sovereign immunity, arguing the claims were essentially for money judgments against the state. They claimed there was no proof of reckless or wanton conduct to qualify for liability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. Finally, they claimed failure to exhaust Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 remedies and entitlement to a setoff for money the state paid on the inmate's behalf. The inmate sought to strike the defenses. The CO and the warden sought dismissal of the action. The court found that the inmate's action was against the CO and the warden individually, so sovereign immunity was inapplicable. Moreover, the Supremacy Clause prevented them from avoiding 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 liability based on state statutory immunity. Exhaustion was not necessary since claims were not against the state. Finally, a setoff was unavailable for money owed to the state, which was a third party.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss, and the court struck the special defenses and the claim for a setoff.

 

1456 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Maina


H12MMV050394794S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 12 AT MANCHESTER


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1470



May 31, 2005, Decided  
May 31, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence seized as a result of the detention of his motor vehicle by a police officer; defendant claimed that the officer lacked reasonable suspicion to stop the vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Using the mobile data terminal installed in his car, a police officer performed a registration check of the marker plate on a car. Although the registration was in order, the officer learned that the operator's license of the registered owner was suspended. In an effort to determine whether owner was the operator, the officer stopped the car. He then approached the car and requested that the operator identify himself. Defendant, who was behind the wheel, gave a false name. While the officer was running the false name, defendant approached the officer and confessed that he was the owner and that his license was suspended. Thereafter, defendant was issued a misdemeanor summons for operating under suspension. The court held that defendant had no expectation of privacy in the registration plate displayed on the exterior of the car in plain view. The officer, having a reasonable suspicion that the operator might have been driving with a suspended license, acted within the scope of his authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-217 to verity the operator's identity and license status. Consequently, no Fourth Amendment violation occurred.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1457 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Barber


455605


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1498



May 20, 2005, Decided  
May 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a prisoner, brought a legal malpractice action against defendant, his former special public defender. The defender moved to dismiss the action pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 15-8.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of robbery and conspiracy. The prisoner retained the special public defender to represent him on appeal. The prisoner claimed that the defender was negligent in failing to properly present to the appellate court the claim that the trial court improperly restricted his right to cross-examination, depriving him of his right to confront witnesses. The court held that the prisoner adduced prima facie evidence of the first two elements of his claim for legal malpractice, the existence of an attorney-client relationship and the attorney's wrongful act or omission. However, the court held that the prisoner failed to prove the third element of the claim, causation. The prisoner had to establish not only the defender's negligence, but also that there should have been a better result in the underlying lawsuit or matter. The claim concerning restriction of the prisoner's right to cross-examination was subject to review under the plain error standard or the Golding standard, and defendant failed to present sufficient evidence to meet either standard. The prisoner failed to introduce the transcript of the trial.


OUTCOME: The public defender's motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1458 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wolff v. Town of Watertown


CV030175538S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1267



May 2, 2005, Decided  
May 2, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Wolff v. Town of Watertown, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 777 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 19, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Having found that section 5.4 of the Watertown planning and zoning regulations is invalid as amended, the court finds that it is unnecessary to address the plaintiff's constitutional claim. "Ordinarily, constitutional issues are not considered unless absolutely necessary to the decision of a case." (Internal quotation marks omitted.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought declaratory judgment and other relief against defendants, a town and its planning and zoning commission, alleging that Watertown, Ct., Subdivision Regulation § 5.4 was invalid and unconstitutional in that it violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25. The landowner sought summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The landowner intended to seek subdivision approval. He contested the legality of Watertown, Ct., Subdivision Regulation § 5.4. The court granted summary judgment in his favor, finding that when considered in relation to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25, nothing in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-26, which provided for a commission to adopt regulations specifying the conditions under which a property under consideration for subdivision could be excused from compliance with zoning regulations, could be reasonably construed to permit a subdivision regulation that conditioned approval on the payment of a fee for off site improvements. Furthermore, the court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-26, which provided for a planning commission to adopt regulations specifying the conditions under which a property could be excused from compliance with a zoning regulation, did not validate Watertown, Ct., Subdivision Regulations § 5.4 because § 5.4 went beyond what the statute permitted by allowing the planning commission to condition a waiver of a subdivision regulation on the payment of a fee for an improvement that was neither necessitated by nor connected with the property under consideration for approval.


OUTCOME: The court granted the landowner's motion for summary judgment.
