Betton v. Comm'r of Transp.


CV030090924S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1125



April 26, 2005, Decided  
April 27, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a negligence action filed by plaintiff accident victim alleging failure to keep the highway in a reasonably safe condition, defendant Commissioner of Transportation for the State of Connecticut filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The accident victim was a passenger in a motor vehicle traveling on the highway when a dead and decayed tree limb crashed into the vehicle and injured him. He filed an amended one-count complaint against the Commissioner to recover damages for his injuries, alleging that the Commissioner was negligent for failing to keep the highway in a reasonably safe condition. The Commissioner filed a motion to dismiss, and the court granted the motion. The accident victim had obtained a special act permitting him to file the action against the Commissioner. However, the court found that the special act passed to allow the accident victim's claim served no legitimate public purpose and was an exclusive public emolument in violation of Conn. Const. art. 1, § 1. The accident victim's original claim was denied by the claims commissioner on the ground that it should have been brought directly in superior court, and at the time of that decision, the accident victim had decided to voluntarily withdraw his simultaneous action in the superior court. The state did not disrupt the course of the action and did not bear responsibility for any injustice suffered by the accident victim.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

 

1460 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Curtin v. Town of Brookfield


(X02)CV020178124S, (X02)CV020178123S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 919



April 14, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Kondrat v. Town of Brookfield, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 358 (Conn. App. Ct., Aug. 8, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, six surviving passengers and the estate administrator of a decedent, filed a negligence suit against defendants, a town, the town's tree warden, and a property owner, arising from an accident wherein a tree fell on a minivan. Defendants sought summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: A tree that stood by a road but partly on the private property owner's land fell on a minivan. The tree warden stated that had he inspected the tree, he would have ordered it cut down because it presented a hazard. The court granted the tree warden's motion for summary judgment based on DeConti v. Clone, which ruled that the discretionary act of tree inspection did not fit within the exception to municipal employee immunity. The court also granted the property owner's motion for summary judgment, following the holding in Muratori, which provided that the legislative intent in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 23-59 and 23-65 was to vest exclusive control in the tree warden of all trees standing within the limits of a highway. Lastly, the court denied summary judgment on the portions of the complaint alleging liability against the town under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577n(a) because a jury could reasonably find that the public works director had a ministerial duty to contact the tree warden about the tree; thus, municipal immunity was not available to shield the town from trial on the allegations that the town, through its public works director, negligently failed to act.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motions for summary judgment of the tree warden and the private property owner, but denied the town's motion for summary judgment.

 

1461 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. O'Meara


CV020817587


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 897



April 13, 2005, Decided  
April 13, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nurse sued defendants, the Connecticut Department of Mental Retardation and the Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Mental Retardation, for an alleged violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-5m. The Department and the Commissioner filed a motion to strike and motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The nurse, an employee of the Department, alleged that she was disciplined by the Department and the Commissioner for making several written complaints to the acting clinical director at a training school and the director of nursing services at the training school regarding the unsatisfactory state of the medical equipment at the training school. The nurse further alleged that the disciplinary action was in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51m. The Department and the Commissioner argued that the nurse failed to allege exhaustion of administrative remedies and that the claim was untimely and therefore failed to state a claim for relief. The court found that the failure of the nurse to allege that she exhausted her administrative remedies was not a jurisdictional defect and therefore treated the motion to strike and motion to dismiss as a motion to strike. While the nurse could have stated a cause of action pursuant to § 31-51m if she had in fact exhausted her administrative remedy, she did not state a cause of action for a violation of § 31-51m because she failed to allege that she exhausted that remedy.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted.

 

1462 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Groton Open Space v. Town of Groton


567343


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 946



April 13, 2005, Decided  
April 13, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, nearby property owners and an environmental group, appealed a decision of defendant town zoning commission to approve a special permit application of defendant developer to construct a residential life care community (RLCC) as defined under Groton, Conn., Zoning Regulations (Regulations) § 7.1-1.


OVERVIEW: The group properly intervened under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-19 to challenge environmental issues. The group and the owners challenged the commission's finding that the project met the requirements either for an RLCC under Regulations § 7.1-1, or for a congregate/independent living facility (CILF) in Regulations § 2. Alternatively, they claimed the regulations were impermissibly vague. They also argued that the commission failed to consider environmental impacts on wetlands, as required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-19 and Regulations § 8.3-8(C). The court found that substantial evidence supported a finding that the RLCC was a CILF. It met the affordability requirement of Regulations, § 7.1-1, since the units' features minimized expenses of upgrading as aging residents' needs changed. The Regulations were not impermissibly vague merely for failing to separately define significant terms since the context of the terms and their ordinary definitions left little ambiguity. Finally, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-19's requirement that agencies consider environmental impacts did not expand the commission's jurisdictional limits, which, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2(a), did not include wetlands.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

1463 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Warden


CV030822972


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1017



April 8, 2005, Decided  
April 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Jones v. Comm'r of Corr., 98 Conn. App. 760, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 526 (Conn. App. Ct., Dec. 19, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Jones, 59 Conn. App. 762, 757 A.2d 689, 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 436 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Petition for a Writ of Habeas Corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a request for habeas corpus review to challenge larceny and robbery convictions.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was involved in a scheme whereby a prostitute stole a victim's purse and vehicle. The inmate was later found with the vehicle and the victim's wallet. He filed a petition for habeas corpus after he was convicted of larceny and robbery. In denying the petition, the court determined that the inmate failed to establish that he received ineffective assistance of counsel because there was no showing that representation was deficient or that he was prejudiced. First, the record showed that the inmate's attorney properly investigated the fair market value of the stolen car. Next, there was no need for defense counsel to call a co-defendant to testify based on the fact that no favorable testimony would have been elicited. Further, defense counsel was able to exploit the absence of the witness to argue that the inmate was not responsible for the crime. The court also found that the stolen vehicle report would not have made a difference in the defense strategy. Moreover, it was evidence that was available at trial. As such, it was not newly discovered evidence to support a claim of actual innocence.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1464 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Corr. Officer Rochester


566307


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1034



April 8, 2005, Decided  
April 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court finds that the defendants are shielded by the common law doctrine of sovereign immunity; therefore, the motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a one-count complaint against defendants, a correctional officer and a correctional department doctor, alleging negligence and intentional conduct. Defendants sought to dismiss on grounds of the applicability of the doctrine of sovereign immunity and a lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had a history of severe asthma attacks. He was suffering from asthma and bronchitis and claimed that the night guard had been informed of his condition and advised that he might need medical assistance. The inmate suffered an attack and stopped breathing. His inmate came to his assistance and banged on the cell door, but because the guard was allegedly asleep, he did not come to the cell until 20 or 30 minutes later. The inmate claimed that the prison doctor failed to adjust his prescription medications or refill his inhalers. The inmate filed suit against defendants, but the court found that because the suit was against state employees in their official capacities and sought monetary damages, the doctrine of sovereign immunity applied; thus, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The court found also that because sovereign immunity applied, defendants did not need to demonstrate compliance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 or statutory immunity. The court found also that defendants' alleged conduct, deliberately falling asleep on the job and deliberately failing to provide medical care, could not reasonably be construed as reckless, wanton, or malicious conduct.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

 

1465 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Landmark E. Hampton, LLC v. Town of E. Hampton


MMXCV054001885S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 951



April 7, 2005, Decided  
April 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The court therefore enters judgment declaring that Gen. Stats. § 8-2k does not apply to the plaintiff's Application because the body of water in question is a reservoir. It further orders the defendants to revisit the plaintiffs' Application with no consideration given to § 8-2k of the General Statutes. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer filed an action for preliminary injunctive relief, permanent injunctive relief, and a declaratory judgment regarding the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2k after defendant town planning and zoning commission denied the developer's application for site plan approval of a proposed shopping center after finding that the developer's proposed site was too close to a body of water that the commission found was a lake.


OVERVIEW: The developer's application for site plan approval of a shopping center was denied when the commission determined that the project was prohibited by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2k due to proximity to a lake. The developer appealed, contending that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2h(a) mandated that the application be decided based on zoning regulations in existence when the application was filed and that it complied with those regulations. The developer argued that application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2k was constitutionally improper and that the commission improperly found that the nearby body of water was a lake and not a reservoir. The court found that the evidence before the commission conclusively showed that the body of water was a reservoir and that § 8-2k specifically excluded reservoirs from its application. Having reached that conclusion, which disposed of the developer's prayer for relief, the court did not address the constitutional issues. Finally, a witness's uncontradicted testimony was that there was no way to place a monetary value on the loss occasioned by the commission's denial of the application under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2k, so injunctive relief was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment declaring that denial of the developer's application for statutory reasons was improper since the body of water in question was a reservoir. It further ordered the commission to revisit the developer's application with no consideration given to the statute that prevented developments near lakes.

 

1466 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Yale Univ.


455318


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 921



April 5, 2005, Decided  
April 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a supervisor, a police chief, and a university, moved to strike plaintiff police officer's action alleging a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: The supervisor refused to let the police officer work alone, showed up at her motor vehicle stops, removed the handcuffs from a suspect, publicly ridiculed her, ordered her to write up an incident report on a matter in which she had not been involved, falsely accused her of incompetence, refused to provide backup support, gave her undesirable beat assignments, and caused disciplinary action to be brought against her for a "minor error" in a police report. The police chief ordered the officer to appear at a meeting where she was ordered to "beg" for her job. After she did so, the university immediately fired her. The court found that when defendants made personnel decisions, they were not state actors. Consequently, the police officer failed to show a violation of § 1983. The supervisor's actions might have been mean spirited and overbearing, but they were not so extreme in degree as to go beyond all possible bounds of decency. However, the police chief and the university's actions crossed the line into real atrocity.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the § 1983 claim was granted as to all parties; the motion to strike the claim of intentional infliction of emotional distress was granted as to the supervisor, but was denied as to the police chief and the university.

 

1467 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Mercer v. Strange


CV030523031


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 895



March 28, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Mercer v. Strange, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 278 (Conn. App. Ct., June 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Defendants were performing their duties within the scope of their employment and there are no allegations or evidence of wanton, reckless or malicious behavior; therefore, statutory immunity applies and the motion to dismiss granted on that ground.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant prison employees in their official capacities, alleging violations of Title II of the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq.; § 504 of the Rehabilitation Act of 1973; and the Equal Protection Clause of the Connecticut Constitution and the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The employees moved to dismiss on grounds of sovereign and statutory immunity.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged the employees violated his rights under the ADA and the rehabilitation act because of their refusal to assign him to a single cell. The court held that the employees were not entitled to sovereign immunity because that immunity was expressly abrogated by Congress when, pursuant to its authority under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 5, it enacted the ADA and the Rehabilitation Act. However, the inmate's claims were insufficient to defeat statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. He did not claim that any of the employees acted beyond the scope of their employment. Further, there was no allegation in the complaint from which the court could infer that the employees' conduct was indicative of such a state of mind or that the conduct rose to the level of egregiousness necessary to be considered wanton, reckless, or malicious.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1468 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


McClam v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV030004011


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 849



March 17, 2005, Decided  
March 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. McClam, 44 Conn. App. 198, 689 A.2d 475, 1997 Conn. App. LEXIS 34 (1997)



DISPOSITION: The Petition for a Writ of Habeas Corpus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus against respondent, an agency, challenging his conviction for murder in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner argued that his trial counsel was ineffective for failing to raise a defense of self-defense at trial. The court held that it was imperative that a client be honest with his own lawyer if he expected that lawyer to be able to effectively represent him or her in a criminal matter. In the instant case, the petitioner tried to weave a tangled web and found himself entangled in its lethal snare. The prisoner lied to his attorney about his involvement in the crime and set his own attorney on a path that could never lead to the discovery of the truth. The court found that it was disingenuous to later seek to come into the court for relief when it was not the actions of the attorney that led to the conviction, but the deceitful conduct of the prisoner that rendered his own attorney impotent to assist him. The prisoner testified under oath that he did not shoot the victim. Therefore, the court found that there were no grounds on which a claim of self-defense could have been made.


OUTCOME: The habeas corpus petition was denied.

 

1469 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


B.W. v. H.T.


FA900606785


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, FAMILY SUPPORT MAGISTRATE DIVISION AT HARTFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 736



March 14, 2005, Decided  
March 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion to modify denied by BW v. HT, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3256 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Motion to modify granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut filed a motion on behalf of petitioner father to modify a child support order, claiming that there has been a substantial change in circumstances, due to the fact that the existing current support order deviated from the Connecticut Child Support Guidelines by at least 15 percent.


OVERVIEW: The father was convicted of sexual assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70, based on multiple sexual assaults on his own daughter. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-215c stated that liability for child support for parents incarcerated as a result of a criminal conviction was limited to the parent's actual daily income. The father did not work at the correctional facility and had no outside income, so his income was zero. The guardian ad litem for the child argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-215c should not apply because the legislature failed to consider circumstances wherein the child subject to the support order was also the victim of the crime, and also argued that equity should bar application of the statute in light of the father's reprehensible conduct. The court acknowledged the logic behind the arguments, but held that it could not deviate from the plain language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-215c. The court granted the guardian ad litem leave to appeal, and encouraged him to appeal the issue to the highest court to attempt to gain relief.


OUTCOME: The motion to modify the father's child support obligation was granted. The order was modified to $ 0, plus $ 0 on the arrearage.

 

1470 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bryant v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV030003933


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT SOMERS


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 657



March 8, 2005, Decided  
March 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Bryant v. Comm'r of Corr., 99 Conn. App. 434, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 50 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Bryant, 71 Conn. App. 488, 802 A.2d 224, 2002 Conn. App. LEXIS 412 (2002)



DISPOSITION: The Petition for a Writ of Habeas Corpus is granted, the verdict shall be set aside and the petitioner granted a new trial in the criminal court. In accordance with P.B. § 61-11(a), "proceedings to enforce or carry out the judgment or order shall be automatically stayed until the time to take an appeal has expired.".


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus to overturn his conviction for manslaughter in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55 and to order that his case be returned to the docket for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for manslaughter despite a claim that others committed the crime. After his conviction was affirmed on direct appeal, he petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging ineffective assistance of trial counsel. At the habeas trial, counsel testified that he did not want to bring in any evidence of the "three Hispanic males with a gun," for fear of introducing evidence of a firearm at the scene of the crime that would be attributed to defendant. Despite this stated strategy, it was harmful to defendant and constituted inadequate representation to avoid introducing available and credible evidence of a clearly exculpatory nature in an ill-advised effort to avoid mentioning a firearm. This was especially true given the credibility of the four witnesses that counsel failed to call. All four individuals were law-abiding citizens, there was no meaningful impeachment of their testimony at the habeas trial, and none of the witnesses knew, or were in any way acquainted or associated with, defendant. Failure to pursue them in an attempt to exculpate defendant failed to provide defendant with the effective assistance of counsel guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, set aside his verdict, and granted defendant a new trial.

 

1471 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schultz


CR03101443


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 711



March 8, 2005, Decided  
March 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Schultz, 2007 Conn. App. LEXIS 175 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 24, 2007)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's Motion to Preclude Imposition of Mandatory Minimum Sentence is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to preclude the imposition of the mandatory minimum sentence for his conviction of assault in the first degree by means of a dangerous instrument, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(1), and sought to avoid the five-year sentence required by § 53a-59(b)(1), contending that it violated equal protection because it was higher than the minimum sentence for manslaughter, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of assault, and filed a motion to preclude the imposition of the mandatory sentence under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(b)(1), arguing that it violated equal protection because a person convicted of manslaughter, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(1), which was a more serious crime than assault, would not be exposed to any mandatory minimum non-suspendable sentence and that the sentencing scheme therefore assigned a lesser penalty to a greater crime. The court held that there was ample scope for discovery of a rational basis for the different penalties for each offense. The legislature could have reasonably enacted this sentencing scheme: (1) to reduce the number of permanent and disabling or disfiguring injuries suffered by assault victims, (2) to deter the commission of serious assault offenses upon the belief that they were easier to commit and more frequently committed than homicide offenses, and (3) to deter serious assault offenses with a five-year mandatory sentence, upon the belief that a person convicted of manslaughter in the first degree would probably not in any event receive a sentence less than five years to serve.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to preclude imposition of the mandatory minimum sentence.

 

1472 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bacon


CR030216984S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 582



February 28, 2005, Decided  
February 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss an information charging him with possession of child pornography in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-196d (before 2004 repeal and replacement), arguing that the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-193(13) definition of "child pornography" (before 2004 repeal and replacement) was overbroad and unconstitutionally vague facially and as applied to him because it could include computer-generated images.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for possession of child pornography after images of nude children in pictures that might or might not have been legally obscene if they had involved adults were seized from his computer. He argued that the statute as it then existed was overbroad and vague because it could conceivably have been used to prosecute him for possession of computer-generated images of children. The court disagreed. The definition of "child pornography" specifically referenced live performances to an audience, even if the audience consisted of one person. This requirement could only be satisfied if, at some point, a child had actually participated in a live performance during which the pictures were taken. Furthermore, any vagueness objections were addressed by the requirement that such possession be knowing. Defendant would be free to argue at trial that the pictures were in fact computer-generated, but that would be an issue for the fact-finder.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.

 

1473 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


O'Marra v. Dep't of Pub. Safety


CV044001277S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 502



February 17, 2005, Decided  
February 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The court concludes that the defendants enjoy sovereign immunity with respect to the claims made in counts two, three and four, and the Motion to Dismiss is granted with respect to those three counts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Connecticut Department of Public Safety and two officers, filed a motion to dismiss the counts of plaintiff former employee's complaint that alleged termination for other than just cause in violation of the collective bargaining agreement, fraudulent misrepresentation in the collective bargaining agreement, and promissory estoppel based on representations allegedly made in connection with the collective bargaining agreement.


OVERVIEW: The employee alleged a claim of constructive retaliatory discharge against the Department and officers. The Department and officers alleged that sovereign immunity barred the counts of the complaint that related to the collective bargaining agreement. To get around the hurdle of sovereign immunity, the employee had to allege conduct by the officers that was sufficiently egregious as to constitute conduct in excess of statutory authority. The three counts at issue were concerned with contract law. The employee did not allege that the Department and officers engaged in wrongful conduct in order to promote an illegal purpose, nor was there any specific statement that the actions of the Department and officers exceeded their statutory authority. Merely acting in a manner that was not in compliance with the terms of the collective bargaining agreement was insufficient to elevate a breach of that agreement into conduct that exceeded statutory authority in the manner that had the effect of waiving sovereign immunity. The employee failed to allege reckless, malicious, or wanton behavior under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165 as required to defeat sovereign immunity of the officials.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted.

 

1474 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Jaysean S.


K09CP03009149A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, JUVENILE MATTERS AT WATERFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 463



February 9, 2005, Decided  
February 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF) filed a petition alleging that a minor child was being neglected by defendant, his mentally retarded mother. The mother moved to implead the Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Mental Retardation (DMR) as a necessary party, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-11. The DMR Commissioner filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The mother was mentally retarded and received assistance from the DMR. The DMR Commissioner claimed immunity from inclusion in the action pursuant to the doctrine of sovereign immunity and that the court, therefore, lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The mother contended that as the DCF had the burden of providing services to her, and some of those services were then being provided by the DMR, then the DMR was a necessary party to the action. The court found that, pursuant to the principles that applied to the exception to the doctrine of sovereign immunity for actions where the Connecticut Legislature had waived the doctrine by force of necessary implication, the mother could circumvent the doctrine of sovereign immunity with respect to the State of Connecticut's obligation to provide her with services through the DCF and the DMR, in that the DCF could not assist the mother per its statutory mandate without the special input of the DMR. Further, the DMR was a necessary party to the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1475 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kemper Auto & Home Ins. Co. v. State


569339


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 184



January 24, 2005, Decided  
January 24, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer filed an action against defendants, the State of Connecticut and an employee, which alleged negligence and recklessness. The employee filed a motion to dismiss the recklessness action.


OVERVIEW: A driver was attempting to turn into a driveway when the employee passed on the left and caused a collision. The insurer paid for the property damage to the vehicle and filed an action against the State and the employee to recover the amount expended. The employee's motion to dismiss was denied. The court determined that the employee was not protected by the common-law doctrine of sovereign immunity or statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. As to the common-law immunity claim, the court examined the four-part test set forth in Spring to determine if the action was against the State. The court noted that the employee had been sued, the case concerned an accident that occurred during the scope of employment, the State was not the real party to the suit, and the state indemnification statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-141d(a), was not applicable. As to statutory immunity, the court held that the complaint properly alleged that the employee's actions were reckless due to the violation of quite a few traffic laws. Although the employee was responding to a burglary call, she was under a duty to warn other of a high speed approach under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-283.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the recklessness action was denied.

 

1476 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ertel v. Rocque


CV030100647S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 183



January 21, 2005, Decided  
January 21, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Ertel v. Rocque, 108 Conn. App. 48, 946 A.2d 1251, 2008 Conn. App. LEXIS 255 (2008)
Motion denied by Ertel v. Rocque, 2009 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3282 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Ertel v. Rocque, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2417 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 27, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner filed an action against defendant state employees, alleging violations of the federal and state constitutions with relation to a dispute over a dock. The employees filed a motion to dismiss based on the immunity in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The owner filed an action against the employees after the destruction of his dock was ordered. In granting their motion to dismiss, the court took judicial notice of the prior decisions affecting the case. Next, the court held the doctrine of sovereign immunity did not apply to some cases brought under Conn. Const. art. 1, § 11. However, the owner did not have a property right in the dock he was ordered to remove. Since that claim was dismissed, the court did not consider the Fifth Amendment claim. Also, the owner had no claims under equal protection, substantive due process, or Conn. Const. art. 1, § 20 because there was no evidence that the employees acted unreasonably or irrationally; therefore, there was no selective enforcement. In addition, the record rebutted the owner's claim of a procedural due process violation since there was a contested evidentiary hearing and appellate review. The court found that there was no retaliation claim under the First Amendment because the actions of the employees were not motivated by the owner's prior complaint. Finally, the employees were entitled to immunity because they did not act in a wanton, reckless, or malicious manner.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted.

 

1477 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Baran v. Carvell


FA040072543


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WINDHAM, AT PUTNAM


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 350



January 21, 2005, Decided  
January 21, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Findings of fact/conclusions of law at Baran v. Carvell, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2450 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 11, 2006)



DISPOSITION: The defendant's motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff brought an action for visitation with a minor child pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59. Plaintiff was not the child's biological father. Defendant, the mother of the child, moved to dismiss the action, asserting that plaintiff had not, and could not, meet the jurisdictional prerequisites for such an action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff began a relationship with the child when the child was four months old. The mother and plaintiff held themselves out to the community as a family, including the child, with the plaintiff being treated by the mother as the father of the child. Plaintiff provided substantial care for the child, including periods of sole responsibility for the child, and plaintiff and the mother had a son together. The court found that those allegations clearly articulated that plaintiff had a relationship similar in nature to a parent-child relationship. Moreover, plaintiff alleged that the child had been traumatized by the loss of a parental figure. The child's day care provider testified that the child was distressed and clinging to plaintiff after the separation of the parties, and a child psychologist testified that disruption of a nurturing, caretaking relationship placed a child at very serious risk for emotional and adjustment problems in the future, including coping problems, depression, and inability to relate to or create intimate relationships. The court found that real and significant harm would result should visitation be denied.


OUTCOME: The mother's motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1478 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Philbrick v. State


CV030829941S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 156



January 18, 2005, Decided  
January 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State moved to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction, for failure to file a timely notice of claim, plaintiff patient's action seeking recovery for malpractice that allegedly occurred when she was treated at the state university hospital. The State argued that 2003 Conn. Acts 17 (Spec. Sess.), a special act enacted to cure any timeliness problems, violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 1 as a public emolument for private benefit.


OVERVIEW: According to her complaint, the patient suffered brain damage and lost all kidney function because of a hospital staff physician's mistakes in a routine operation. The hospital did not reply promptly to her first requests for medical records after she began to suspect malpractice, so her notice of claim was not filed within the time limit provided by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(a). As that law permitted, she filed a late notice of claim after the legislature passed a special act based on its finding that allowing her to pursue her claim was equitable and also served the public interest. The court denied the motion to dismiss on two bases. First, it was not convinced that the notice of claim had in fact been filed late, given the operation of the delayed discovery rule. The patient and her attorney would not have been in any position to assess the likelihood of malpractice until her expert had a chance to examine her records, and the notice might well have been timely if those records had been promptly supplied. Secondly, the legislature had also considered the hospital's delay in finding that allowing a late filing would serve the public good as well as the patient.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1479 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Biafore v. Bozeman


FA030082030


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 185



January 16, 2005, Decided  
January 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother, in an action brought by the State, filed a paternity action against defendant father. After paternity was determined, the court decided the issue of child support.


OVERVIEW: The mother received public assistance after the birth of her child. When paternity was established, the State sought child support. However, the father received supplement social security income (SSI) based on a disability. The evidence showed that the father had held several jobs before and after the child's birth. The State contended that the father should have been ordered to pay based on his earning capacity. The court determined that the father was not required to pay any support. Under Conn. Agencies Regs. § 46b-215a-1(11)(B)(ii), SSI was wholly excluded as income for child support purposes. Further, the court was not allowed to impute income to the father based on his earning capacity under 2003 Conn. Acts 130 (Reg. Sess.). The court was precluded from considering earning capacity in computing arrearages as well since 2003 Conn. Acts 130 (Reg. Sess.) applied retrospectively. The court refused to find that 2003 Conn. Acts 130 (Reg. Sess.) was unconstitutionally discriminating against the mother. However, the court was not precluded from considering the actual earnings of the father in setting arrearages. The court entered an order based on the work performed since the birth.


OUTCOME: The father was not ordered to pay any child support, but the court found an arrearage based on the father's actual income after the time the child was born. Income withholding was ordered for the arrearages.

 

1480 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Town of Clinton v. Joseph Schrempp Clinton


CV044000684, CV044000685


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 92



January 14, 2005, Decided  
January 14, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner town brought two actions against respondent landowners in which they sought a court order permitting inspection and testing of the landowners' property pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-13.


OVERVIEW: As a result of a consent order with the Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection, the town was required to undertake studies of its neighborhoods in order to determine which areas were not able to support on-site waste water treatment and would require the conveyance of waste water to an off-site facility for treatment and disposal. Among the areas identified by engineers hired by the town as possible sites were three parcels of land owned by the landowners. The town could not gain the landowners' permission to conduct the investigation and testing. The town brought two actions for an order permitting inspection and testing under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-13. The landowners objected under the takings clauses of U.S. Const. amend. V or Conn. Const. art. I, § 11, arguing they were entitled to compensation prior to the intrusion. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-13 was constitutional on its face under the constitutional takings clauses. Moreover, it was constitutional as applied since the court would oversee the amount of intrusion, would provide compensation afterwards, and would insure against any U.S. Const. amend. IV intrusion.


OUTCOME: The court granted the town's motions, but limited the right of entry to 72 hours written notice and for the sole purpose of conducting minimally intrusive surveys, investigation, photography and the like. The court did not authorize the town to undertake borings or any more invasive activities, without first applying to the court for leave to do so.

 

1481 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Contractor's Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Rocque


CV010808172


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 9



January 5, 2005, Decided  
January 5, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Contractor's Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Comm'r of Envtl. Prot., 283 Conn. 86, 925 A.2d 1071, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 283 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Contractors Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Rocque, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2443 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 2, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Environmental Protection (Connecticut) denied plaintiff property owner's request for permits to construct and operate a hot-mix asphalt plant. The owner filed suit, seeking a declaratory judgment that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-196, which limited the siting of asphalt plants, was illegally retroactive and unconstitutionally lacked a rational basis. The Department argued that the owner lacked standing.


OVERVIEW: The Department issued the owner a permit to construct a hot-mix asphalt plant and a conditional permit to operate it; both permits expired in one year. The owner did not complete construction within one year, and sought a one-year extension of the permits. The Department advised the owner that it could continue construction. Then, § 22a-196 was enacted; it applied only to hot-mix asphalt plants not already in operation as of December 31, 1997. The Department found that the plant had not been completed by that date and was within one-third of a mile of a watercourse, in violation of § 22a-196; therefore, the Department terminated the owner's construction permit. This suit followed. The Department argued that the owner lacked standing to challenge § 22a-196 because, as its permit was no longer valid, it lacked a constitutionally-protected property interest. The court disagreed. The owner's interest in the use of its property had been sufficiently injured by the statute to confer classical standing. Whether it had a valid permit at the time of the statute's enactment was immaterial because standing to bring the action did not depend on possession of such a permit.


OUTCOME: The court held that the owner had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute.

 

1482 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Renkewith v. Bobbi


CV044000554S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 17



January 4, 2005, Decided  
January 4, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought an injunction as to defendant adjacent property owners and the placement of the adjacent property owners' mailbox along the right-of-way on the property owners' property. The adjacent property owners moved to dismiss arguing lack of subject matter jurisdiction on the grounds that the United States Postal Service had exclusive authority and the property owners failed to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Initially, the adjacent property owners' mailbox was located in the corner of the property owners' property, adjacent to the street line, opposite the location of the property owners' driveway. The adjacent property owners unilaterally moved their mailbox to the middle of the property owners' front yard, adjacent to the street line. The property owners requested that the adjacent property owners return the mailbox to its original location. The adjacent property owners refused. The property owners did not invoke any federal statute or regulation in their complaint. The court held that Congress intended that state law and regulations would concurrently apply to the issue of mailbox placement along rural routes. Compliance with both federal and state law was not a physical impossibility as the mailbox would be in compliance with federal regulations in its original location. There was nothing in the application of Connecticut's common law regarding property rights, injunctive relief, rights-of-way, and torts which presented an obstacle to the federal regulations regarding mailbox placement. Finally, the property owners were not required to exhaust any administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1483 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Felicia S.


CP01011139A, CP01011140A


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3786



December 29, 2004, Decided  
December 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Department of Children and Families (DCF), filed a petition to terminate the parental rights of respondents, a mother and father. The father tendered a valid consent to the petition.


OVERVIEW: DCF alleged that the mother failed to achieve statutory rehabilitation. The court found that DCF made reasonable efforts to timely provide the mother with the necessary services to assist in reunification. The mother, however, was unwilling or unable to benefit from any of the reunification efforts made. The mother continually failed to cooperate or follow through with service providers who attempted to address her substance abuse and mental health issues, despite numerous referrals by DCF to a variety of different programs. Thus, the court concluded that DCF's efforts were thwarted by the mother's own behavior. As such, the mother's substance abuse issues continued to affect her ability to function on a personal and parenting level. While the children long maintained their affection for and ties to the mother, despite their removal from her care for more than three and a half years, the court found that it would be detrimental to them to be forced to experience any longer the uncertainty presented by the spectre that the mother may persist in the pattern of failing to achieve rehabilitation while remaining a focus of the children's unrealistic desire to return to her care.


OUTCOME: DCF's petition to terminate the parental rights of the mother and the father was granted. The Commission of the DCF was appointed the statutory parent for each child for the purpose of securing an adoptive family or other permanent placement for them.

State v. Hills


CR0481234


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 19 AT ROCKVILLE


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3854



December 29, 2004, Decided  
December 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with sexual assault in the second degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-71(a)(1), and impairing the morals of a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(2). Defendant filed a motion under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56d for an examination to determine his competency to stand trial. In response to defendant's motion, the court ordered that defendant be examined pursuant to the provisions of § 54-56d(d).


OVERVIEW: Defendant's counsel moved for a competency hearing and thus, had the burden of proving incompetency. There was undisputed evidence that defendant was learning disabled and had great difficulty reading and writing. There was no evidence that defendant was presently mentally or medically ill. Defendant's claim of incompetency rested solely on the contention that he was moderately mentally retarded, and, as a result of his low level of intelligence, could not assist his counsel and/or understand the criminal proceedings pending against him. The main evidence defendant offered in support of his claim were IQ test results and the testing and opinions of a second doctor. However, defendant's cognitive test results and academic performance over an extended period of time prior to his graduation from high school, the transcripts of prior plea and sentencing hearings, and the credible testimony of law enforcement officials and others who observed and interacted with defendant all compelled the court to reject the psychological evidence presented by defendant. Furthermore, the court found that defendant purposely failed to put forth sufficient effort during his evaluation.


OUTCOME: Defendant was found competent to stand trial.

Mahon v. B.V. Unitron Mfg.


X01CV990164084S, X01CV990164438S, X01CV990164107


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3773



December 17, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Mahon v. B.V. Unitron Mfg., 2007 Conn. LEXIS 496 (Conn., Dec. 11, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant boat engine manufacturer sought to reduce the verdicts, and plaintiff estate administrators of a deceased couple sought to increase the verdicts in a death action brought on behalf of the deceased couple against the manufacturer and against settling defendants, a technology company, boat owners, and a boat manufacturer, for damages arising from a boat collision.


OVERVIEW: A young married couple were killed when the lights went out on their boat and it collided with another boat in the dark. Their administrators brought death actions against the engine manufacturer, a technology company, and the other boat owners and their boat manufacturer. The couple's two passengers brought personal injury actions against the couple's estate. All parties settled except the engine manufacturer, and the couple's suit against it proceeded under the theory of products liability. The jury awarded $ 130,000 to the husband's estate and $ 150,000 to the wife's estate. Including the settlements, the total award to the husband was $ 1,069,000 and the total award to the wife was $ 1,024,000. The court found that the verdicts were neither excessive nor shocking to the conscience of the community, noting that the decedents were young, healthy, happily married, and physically active with life expectancies of 50.1 years and 45.08 years. The court declined to increase the verdicts, noting that in light of the total awards, they were not inadequate and that the jury could have rejected the estimates of economic loss and the claim of conscious pain and suffering.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for remittitur and the motion for additur.

Shamberger v. Warden


CV030004076S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 19 AT ROCKVILLE


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3562



November 29, 2004, Decided  
November 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus, arguing that respondent Connecticut Department of Correction incorrectly calculated his discharge date.


OVERVIEW: In 2000, the inmate was sentenced to three years' imprisonment, execution suspended, and three years' probation. In 2001, he was sentenced in each of three cases to two years, to run concurrently, for a total effective sentence of two years. Later in 2001 his 2000 sentence was opened and he was re-sentenced to 23 months for a violation of probation stemming from the 2001 offenses. In 2003 he was sentenced on another case to two years, to run concurrent with the sentences then being served. He argued he was entitled to have the 2003 sentence deemed to have commenced the date the 2001 sentences were imposed. The court held that applying the inmate's reasoning would lead to the impossible scenario in which a defendant completed serving a sentence for an offense that had not yet been committed. Further, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-38(b), a sentence commenced when the prisoner was received in the custody to which he was sentenced. The 2003 sentence began to run when it was imposed -- in 2003. The inmate's claim was wholly without merit.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

State v. Armstrong


CR04196428


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3417



November 18, 2004, Decided  
November 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with conspiracy to commit robbery in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48 and 53a-134(a)(4), and two counts of burglary in the first degree, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-101(a)(2). Defendant moved to suppress pre-trial identifications made by eyewitnesses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the identifications were tainted by impermissibly suggestive police procedure, and were the result of a collaboration of the two witnesses or the result of one party assenting to the others identification rather than two separate independent and untainted identifications. The State conceded that the identification procedure, a one on one show-up, was presumptively suggestive. However, the appellate court held that under the totality of circumstances, the identifications of defendant were reliable. Both witnesses had seen defendant on at least one prior occasion and were familiar with his general physical characteristics. The home invasion robbery in question took place in a lighted kitchen area in close proximity to the victims over several minutes. Within several minutes of the assailants' departure, the witnesses were able to positively identify their assailants under the street lights, strobe lights from several police cars, and under a police spotlight. Finally, although one witness watched the other witness positively identify the three assailants there was no evidence that his identification was influenced by either the first witness or the police.


OUTCOME: The motion to suppress was denied.

 

1488 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gonzalez


CR0324295


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3238



November 12, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Gonzalez, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 183 (Conn., May 30, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was arrested for possession of narcotics, possession of narcotics with intent to sell, possession of narcotics within 1500 feet of a school, possession of narcotics with intent to sell within 1500 feet of a school, and conspiracy on all of the listed charges, moved to suppress all fruits of an allegedly illegal search and seizure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a police officer conducted an illegal search in answering another individual's cellular telephone. The trial court held that defendant had a subjective expectation of privacy in that he was under the impression that he was speaking over the telephone with another individual, not a police officer. Defendant dialed a telephone number he presumably knew to be the individual's cellular telephone and was directly quoted as saying that he wanted to "resupply" the officer. The word "resupply" implied a previous dealing between the defendant and the individual. When defendant was arrested, he was alone, demonstrating an effort to maintain privacy on his end of the conversation. The officer conducted an illegal search when he answered the individual's cellular telephone without consent. As in other challenges that had been rejected, the State arranged to meet defendant personally via a telephone conversation, defendant spoke freely with strangers, and the officer did not affirmatively misrepresented his identity. Thus, defendant lacked standing to challenge the illegal search as he did not have a reasonable expectation of privacy in the telephone calls.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to suppress was denied.

Doe v. UConn Health Ctr.


CV040832437


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3383



November 10, 2004, Decided  
November 10, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant State for negligence, negligent hiring and training, negligent supervision, negligent retention, and medical malpractice. The State moved to dismiss the complaint due to a lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The inmate then filed a request to amend his complaint in order to comply with the requirements set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-160.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged a state employee sexually and physically abused him and that the State took no action to prevent this. The State claimed that he failed to allege exhaustion of administrative remedies by not stating in his complaint that he filed a claim with the Connecticut Claims Commissioner, that the Commissioner authorized suit, and the date of that authorization. The court agreed. Pursuant to § 4-160, by failing to include that information in the complaint, the inmate failed to show that the State waived sovereign immunity; therefore, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. That he supplied evidence that he did in fact file a claim with the Commissioner was immaterial. And Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-592, the accidental failure of suit statute, did not authorize the court to disregard its lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The court could not consider the inmate's motion to amend because it had to consider the jurisdictional issue first, and it determined that it lacked jurisdiction to proceed.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was granted and the case was dismissed.

Maher v. Avon Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV030828489


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, JUVENILE MATTERS AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3302



November 8, 2004, Decided  
November 9, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, neighbors, appealed a decision by defendant, a city planning commission, which granted a special exception and the approval of a site plan to defendants, property owners, for the development of a funeral home building and related infrastructure which abutted the residential neighborhood in which the neighbors resided.


OVERVIEW: The neighbors argued that the commission illegally created a new parking standard and illegally and arbitrarily applied that standard. The appellate court held that the town did not and was not required to establish a parking standard specific to funeral homes because it could reasonably be determined that funeral homes were sufficiently similar to the uses encompassed by an existing category. The parking standard for that category of uses contained clear criteria to guide the commission and to inform those affected of their rights and obligations. The commission's application of the seat-based standard to the funeral home constituted a reasonable interpretation of the existing regulations and was reasonably targeted to meet the normal parking needs of the facility. Therefore, the parking regulations were not impermissibly vague as applied to the funeral home and the commission's application of the regulations was not arbitrary, unreasonable, or illegal. The neighbors also argued that the funeral home was fundamentally incompatible with the neighborhood business zone. The appellate court held that the commission was within its rights in arriving at this discretionary decision.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Cobb v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV000003238


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3423



November 8, 2004, Decided  
November 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, alleging that his convictions and resultant death sentence were defective under both the United States Constitution and the Constitution of the State of Connecticut. The inmate contended that his counsel failed to provide him with effective representation during the sentencing phase of the trial.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of various crimes, including capital felony murder, arising out of an incident where he kidnapped the victim, raped her, bound and gagged her, threw her over a wall, and left her to die. His conviction was affirmed on appeal. Thereafter, the inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, raising issues as to the effectiveness of his trial and appellate counsel. In denying the petition, the court held: (1) that the inmate was not deprived of his constitutional right to effective assistance of trial counsel by the fact that his counsel decided not to call a psychiatrist to testify at the sentencing hearing because numerous details of the inmate's heinous conduct on the night of the murder would have come into evidence, thereby helping to establish an aggravating factor; (2) that there was no showing that the trial counsel provided ineffective assistance by his "ethical lapses" where the actions of the trial counsel inured to the benefit of the inmate; and (3) that the inmate's appellate counsel was not ineffective for failing to challenge the state's death penalty statute because there was no legal basis for such a challenge on the direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

 

1492 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Batte-Holmgren v. Galvin


CV044000287


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3313



November 5, 2004, Decided  
November 5, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Batte-Holmgren v. Comm'r of Pub. Health, 281 Conn. 277, 2007 Conn. LEXIS 56 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Connecticut Commissioner of Public Health and the Connecticut Attorney General, moved to strike a complaint filed by plaintiff restaurant and cafe owners and operators serving liquor (collectively restaurants) seeking a declaratory judgment that 2003 Conn. Pub. Acts 45 violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. 1, § 20 and seeking an injunction prohibiting its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The restaurants serving liquor argued that the ban on environmental tobacco smoke (ETS) violated the equal protection laws as it exempted private clubs and casinos. The trial court assumed that the restaurants had been deprived of substantial business due to the ban, while the exempt businesses had not been harmed. The statute was passed with an objective of protecting and promoting the public health from ETS. There was no fundamental right to smoke and smokers were not a suspect class. Thus, the rational basis test was applied. As it was uncontested that ETS presented serious health risks to those exposed to it, there was a rational basis for the ban. The fact that private clubs were private provided a rational basis for treating them differently. Assuming that the State had the authority to apply the ban to the tribal land on which the casinos were located, the State's concerns over its ability to enforce the smoking ban at casinos provided a rational basis to exempt the casinos. Any political and economic influence of the casinos did not alter the legal analysis. The equal protection claims were without merit.


OUTCOME: The requests for a declaratory judgment and for injunctive relief were denied. Defendants' motion to strike was granted.

 

1493 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dean v. Norwalk Zoning Comm'n


CV020191583S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3204



November 4, 2004, Decided  
November 4, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Dean v. Zoning Comm'n, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 336 (Conn. App. Ct., July 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Dean v. Norwalk Zoning Comm'n, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3206 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 4, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought consolidated review of a decision of defendant zoning commission denying approval of two coastal area management site plans filed regarding, inter alia, development of additional parking spaces, pursuant to an easement, on property owned by intervening defendant neighbor. The neighbor challenged the owner's standing to apply for approval regarding its property.


OVERVIEW: The owner and the neighbor owned adjoining properties along the waterfront. The owner's property was benefited by an easement allowing it to develop parking spaces on the neighbor's property if needed to comply with zoning regulations. The owner's development plan, involving an increased number of boat slips, also created a need for additional parking spaces. The neighbor resisted such activity on its property, but the court held that ownership of the easement interest gave the owner standing as a person aggrieved to appeal the commission's action and that with proper approval, its proposed activity could have been permissible both under the grant made in a recorded easement and under local zoning regulations generally. Nonetheless, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-109 authorized a local zoning commission to deny approval to proposed uses that would violate the policies of planned coastal management, and substantial evidence supported the commission's finding that development under the proposed plans, and particularly the addition of parking spaces, would put a huge strain on the need to provide for water dependent uses, justifying denial of permission.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the property owner's appeals.

 

1494 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Dean v. Norwalk Zoning Comm'n


CV030193760


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3206



November 4, 2004, Decided
