NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Dean v. Norwalk Zoning Comm'n, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3204 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 4, 2004)
Appeal dismissed by Dean v. Zoning Comm'n of Norwalk, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 336 (Conn. App. Ct., July 18, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a general partner of a family partnership, appealed from decisions of defendant Norwalk, Connecticut, Zoning Commission, which denied the partnership's applications for coastal site plans with respect to a parcel of land that the partnership owned, and one that it had a perpetual easement over.


OVERVIEW: The partnership owned a parcel of land in a business zone, as well as a perpetual easement of an abutting parcel that was used for a parking lot. As the properties involved were within the Coastal Zone, the partnership filed two coastal area management site plans with the Commission in its efforts to add 10 docking slips to its own property, and to add additional parking to the easement area. The Commission denied the applications, and the partnership filed a timely appeal as well as additional site plan applications. The additional applications were also denied, and on appeal, the court initially found that the partnership was an aggrieved party for purposes of standing to bring the appeal. Thereafter, the court determined that the partnership complied with the applicable municipal regulations involving both properties. The court reviewed the record and determined that substantial evidence supported the Commission's finding that the proposal would have an adverse impact on water-dependent uses, and that the adverse impact had not been mitigated. Further, construction of a single-family home would impact public access. Accordingly, denial of the applications was proper.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the partnership's appeals.

 

1495 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Reardon v. Town of Stonington


567065


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3166



October 29, 2004, Decided  
October 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to strike count two of plaintiffs' complaint granted. Plaintiffs' second prayer for relief requesting punitive damages stricken.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trustees and the interest holders in property (collectively, trustees) filed suit against defendants, a the town and its board of assessment appeals (collectively, town). The town filed a motion to strike the count of the complaint alleging violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-62a and 12-63, for which the trustees sought an injunction requiring the town to conduct a reassessment of all real property in the town and punitive damages.


OVERVIEW: The trustees did not plead a statutory basis for their suit. The appellate court held that the trustees alleged sufficient facts to assert a cause of action under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-119 despite their failure to specifically identify the statute. The trustees alleged that the assessment of their property was grossly excessive, that the town was required to assess the property at 70 percent of its actual valuation, and that the town exceeded that percentage. Further, the trustees sufficiently alleged that the town violated Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-62a and 12-63. The trustees could seek injunctive relief as they were not seeking to enjoin the collection of taxes, but to reassess all properties in the town in a uniform manner and at the mandated percentages. However, the trustees failed to give notice of the suit to the other property owners in town and their claim for injunctive relief was stricken. Finally, the prayer for punitive damages was stricken as the trustees were not entitled to punitive damages under any of the statutes governing tax appeals and they did not allege that the town acted in a wanton or wilful malicious way.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the count of the complaint alleging a violation of the tax assessment statutes, for which the trustees sought an injunctive order requiring the town to conduct a new revaluation of all real property in the town, was granted. The prayer for relief requesting punitive damages was stricken.

 

1496 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Univeristy of Conn. v. Wolf


CV030482479S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3094



October 25, 2004, Decided  
October 26, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In its action alleging defendant debtor defaulted on a promissory note, plaintiff state university filed a motion to dismiss, under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 10-30, -31, the debtor's counterclaim that the university violated the Fair Debt Collection Practices Act (FDCPA), 15 U.S.C.S. § 1692 (2004), and that the university's actions damaged the debtor's credit rating, thus justifying dismissal of the action and damages.


OVERVIEW: The university commenced an action against the debtor, alleging default on a promissory note and unjust enrichment arising from the debtor's non-payment of a debt. The debtor alleged that the university did not credit her for numerous payments and refused to accept her tendered satisfaction of the debt. In a cross-complaint, the debtor sought dismissal, monetary damages, and equitable relief based on the university's alleged violation of the FDCPA. The university moved to dismiss the counterclaims, arguing that, as an agent of the state, sovereign immunity protected it, especially where the debtor did not follow the procedures in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 et seq., for bringing a monetary claim against a state agent. The court found that, by initiating the action, the university voluntarily invoked the court's jurisdiction and subjected itself to any proper cross-claim arising out of the subject matter of its action. Thus, the university waived sovereign immunity with regard to the debtor's counterclaim, which clearly arose from enforcement of the promissory note. Moreover, once the university consented to the counterclaim by bringing suit, the statutory procedure was not required.


OUTCOME: The court denied the university's motion to dismiss.

 

1497 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Morrow v. Ripley


CV044001070S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2998



October 12, 2004, Decided  
October 12, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion for expedited stay of proceedings granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the fiancee of defendant mother's ex-husband, brought an action for slander and other claims against the mother and defendant grandmother. Defendants, through a State of Connecticut Victim Advocate, moved for an expedited stay of the proceeding based on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-235e.


OVERVIEW: After the mother and the ex-husband's divorce, the fiancee, among other claims, contended that the mother, assisted by the grandmother, directed the mother and the ex-husband's minor child to make allegations of sexual abuse by the ex-husband and the fiancee. These allegations led to the fiancee's arrest on criminal charges. Defendants contended that, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-1k, they were crime victims, as members of the minor child's immediate family, and that a stay under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-235e was appropriate. The fiancee argued that since there had been no adjudication of the allegations against her in the criminal proceeding, there was no "crime victim" under § 52-235e. The court found the language of § 52-235e made it clear that the legislature did not require a stay only after an adjudication in the underlying criminal proceeding. By liberally construing § 52-235e, the grandmother was a "crime victim" under § 52-235e, as a member of the minor child's "immediate family." The fiancee's allegations directly implicated the grandmother in the events leading to the fiancee's arrest, and under the circumstances § 52-235e's protection should to be available to her.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion for expedited stay of proceedings was granted. The matter was stayed during the pendency of the criminal proceeding concerning the fiancee.

 

1498 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ahmad v. Yale-New Haven Hosp., Inc.


(X02)CV040183725S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2765



September 29, 2004, Decided  
September 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Class certification denied by Ahmad v. Yale-New Haven Hosp., 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 291 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 25, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital filed motions to dismiss portions of plaintiff patients' complaint and to strike all 15 of the counts in the complaint. The complaint alleged that the hospital violated statutory provisions governing the patients' right to obtain bed funds under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-509b (2003), which would have entitled them to free hospitalization and medical care, and that the hospital engaged in unlawful collection activities.


OVERVIEW: The patients claimed that the hospital failed to provide them with adequate notice of bed funds that would have provided them with free medical care. They charged violations of the bed funds statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-509b (2003), the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a, and the collecting at cost statute, Conn. Gen. Stat, § 19a-673(b), along with counts based on common law. The court denied the hospital's dismissal motion because the patients demonstrated standing to enforce the bed funds statute. That statute implied a private right of action and the patients were aggrieved. The finding of standing defeated the motion to dismiss. The CUTPA claim was properly pled. The patients' could reopen judgments obtained against them for not paying their bills after the four month period in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-212a because they alleged CUTPA violations. Moreover, the patients properly pled violations of the bed funds statute. However, because the hospital billed them, but had not begun collection, the collecting at cost statute was inapplicable. Finally, the court summarily found that the common law claims were not sufficiently pled.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss. The court granted the motion to strike the counts of the complaint alleging breach of contract, rescission, tortious interference, and violations of the collecting at cost statute, but the court denied the motion as to all other counts.

Roxo Constr., L.L.C. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Bridgeport


CV020395418


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2704



September 28, 2004, Decided  
September 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the owner of a parcel of land and the lessee of several nearby parcels of land, appealed, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8, from a decision of by defendant city planning and zoning commission, which denied plaintiffs' application for a zone change pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-9 of the city's zoning regulations.


OVERVIEW: The owner and the lessee applied for a zone change from residential to light industrial in order to reflect the historic use of their properties as a storage yard for contractor materials and equipment. The commission denied the application on the grounds that the proposed change did not comply with either the master or comprehensive city plan, it was spot zoning, the predominant use in the area was residential, and the change would create a nonconformity by placing existing residential uses in an industrial zone. The owner and the lessee appealed, arguing the evidence did not support the commission's grounds for denying their application. The lessee separately alleged that denial of the application resulted in a practical confiscation of its leased property. The court found that the city's plans encouraged stability and preservation of residential neighborhoods, so sufficient evidence supported the decision. Also, the lessee likely did not have standing to bring an inverse condemnation claim because that right existed in the property owner. Nevertheless, the lessee did not meet its burden of showing that the decision did not allow any reasonable alternative use of the property.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the plaintiffs' appeal.

 

1500 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zapadka


CR030078263S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


49 Conn. Supp. 248; 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2786; 873 A.2d 270



September 27, 2004, Decided  
September 27, 2004, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Memorandum on the defendant's motion to dismiss.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with criminal possession of a firearm in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss based upon the provisions of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-8(5), (8), and (9), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56, the Sixth Amendment, the Fourteenth Amendment, and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 6,7, and 8.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's legal argument was based upon claims that the replica antique pistol which he allegedly possessed was not a "firearm" within the meaning of state statutes, and that it was exempt from the statutory prohibition set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-217. Accordingly, he claimed that the charge should be dismissed because he has not committed an offense. The court found that the replica antique pistol allegedly possessed by defendant was fired, and that it propelled via gun powder a shot that mortally wounded the defendant's spouse. Accordingly, the court found that the gun in question was a pistol, revolver or other weapon from which a shot could be discharged, as defined by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-3(19). The court further found that, contrary to defendant's contention, it was not likely that the general assembly intended to create an exception to the criminal possession statute that would permit serious offenders to arm themselves with large-caliber, multiple-shot, operational replica antique pistols.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1501 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence Mall of New Haven v. City of W. Haven


X06CV030183330S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2691



September 22, 2004, Decided  
September 22, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by Lawrence Mall of New Haven, Inc. v. City of W. Haven, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 816 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 20, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class of real property taxpayers sought a temporary injunction enjoining defendant city from charging taxpayers who were delinquent in paying their real property taxes a collection fee on the grounds that the fee was unreasonable and in violation of Connecticut statutes and the Connecticut and United States Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The city entered into a written contract with a collection company by which the company was to provide services to the city for the collection of delinquent real estate taxes. Under the agreement, the company was paid by the city a servicing fee of 15 percent of the amount actually collected. The fee was a contingency fee in that it was only paid by the city to the company if the company was successful in collecting the arrearage. The taxpayers sought a temporary injunction, contending that a collection fee of a fixed percentage was not authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-166 and that such a fee was unreasonable because it was not based on the amount of work performed by the company. The court disagreed, finding that § 12-166 provided for a collection fee and that the fee was reasonable because it was a contingency fee and as such there was a risk of no recovery; therefore, the company was allowed to charge a premium for its services in return for assuming those risks. Lastly, the court found that it was sufficient to sustain the constitutionality of the delegation of authority contained in § 12-166 that the court had implied a standard that tax collection fees be reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request for a temporary injunction.

State v. Bronov


S2NCR030101244S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT NORWALK


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2797



September 16, 2004, Decided  
September 24, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with manslaughter in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3). Defendant moved for dismissal of the information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the prosecution of him for the offense of manslaughter in the first degree under the facts and circumstances of the case was a violation of due process of law because, under the facts, a reasonable person would not be put on notice that such conduct would be a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-55(a)(3). The court disagreed, noting, contrary to defendant's contention, judicial precedent established otherwise. Among other things, the court noted that defendant was operating his vehicle at a high rate of speed at the time of the accident, that he did not attempt to negotiate the curve in the road, and that he had a blood alcohol level of 0.240. In addition, defendant told the officers that he had been drinking in an area several miles from the site of the accident. Defendant also argued that his prosecution was violative of his rights to equal protection under the state and federal constitutions. The court found no violation as defendant failed to demonstrate that he was similarly situated to defendants in the cases cited in his brief who were charged only with a lesser offense.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion was denied.

Perry v. Conn. Pub. Defenders Serv. Comm'n


CV010386523


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2581



September 13, 2004, Decided  
September 13, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Perry v. State, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 146 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Perry v. Conn. Pub. Defendant Serv., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 40 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 8, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former client filed a legal malpractice suit against defendants, Connecticut Public Services Commission and its attorney, seeking damages for their alleged negligence in handling his case.


OVERVIEW: The client was arrested on a warrant charging him with first-degree robbery for an alleged knife point robbery. The victim had complained that she was robbed by a "light skinned" black male. The public defender's office lawyer represented the client, who had been arrested three times previously, was on probation, and had a prior conviction for failure to appear in court. The client was held in custody awaiting trial on a $ 50,000 bond and was released nine months later when, during jury selection, the victim had an opportunity to view the client and told the prosecutor that he was not the perpetrator. The client sued defendants, and the court ruled in favor of defendants, finding that due to the client's previous arrests and conviction for failing to appear in court, the lawyer's failure to seek a bond reduction was reasonably prudent and in no way an act of malpractice. The court found also that because the victim had selected the client's photo as the perpetrator, and pointed to photos of what she thought was "light skinned" that were close to the client's skin tone, the lawyer's strategy of opposing a voluntary lineup prior to trial to avoid re-identification was sound.


OUTCOME: The court entered judgment in favor of defendants and against the client.

 

1504 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Brookheights, L.L.C. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Newtown


CV030349197S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2385



August 20, 2004, Decided  
August 20, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer appealed a decision by defendant town planning and zoning commission (PZC), which denied the developer's application for approval of a subdivision on property it owned in the town.


OVERVIEW: The developer applied to the PZC for approval of a subdivision on its property. Prior to that application, the local conservation commission had filed an application necessitated by the existence of wetlands on the developer's property. The Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection (DEP) made a tentative decision to approve the wetlands application. Based on the DEP's decision, the PZC denied the developer's subdivision application. The developer appealed. The court found that since there was no application before the conservation commission, the DEP had issued only a tentative, and not a final, decision, and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-26 explicitly stated that the PZC could not render a decision until the DEP submitted a report with its final decision. Since there was no dispute that the application was no longer before the conservation commission and that the DEP's decision was tentative and not final, the PZC's action was seriously flawed and the developer's appeal was sustained.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the developer's appeal.

Wang v. Griffin


CV040199068S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2367



August 18, 2004, Decided  
August 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a tenant, sued defendant, an estate of a landlord, alleging breach of the parties' residential lease, negligence, and a violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b. The landlord moved to strike the CUTPA count.


OVERVIEW: The tenant claimed to have suffered keratitis to both eyes, which was caused by the landlord's breach of certain provisions of the lease and the landlord's negligence relating to the property. In the CUTPA claim, the tenant argued that the alleged contractual breaches and negligence of the landlord constituted unfair or deceptive acts or practices in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110b, and caused the tenant to suffer an ascertainable loss of money or property. The estate argued that the CUTPA action did not survive the death of the landlord under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-599, the survival of action statute. The court found that because CUTPA was a remedial, not a penal, statute, such an action survived the death of the landlord pursuant to the survival statute. However, the court held that the tenant had not pled any facts that would support a CUTPA violation based on the landlord's alleged breaches of the lease. Particularly, the tenant failed to set forth any facts showing any aggravating factors, such as acts of misrepresentations or deceptions of the landlord. Therefore, the motion to strike had to be granted.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the CUTPA claim was granted.

Celentano v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV030483928S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2354



August 13, 2004, Decided  
August 13, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In challenging a zoning plan change by defendant, a city planning and zoning commission, plaintiff, a property owner, moved to supplement the record pursuant to Conn. Gen. Laws ch. 8-8.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(k)(2) stated that a court had to allow any party to introduce evidence in addition to the contents of the records if it appeared additional testimony was necessary for an equitable disposition of the appeal. The court found that where it was claimed that a re-zoning constituted a taking of property without just compensation in violation of the federal and state constitutions, additional evidence was necessary because an inverse condemnation could not be raised before a commission until the zoning revision was adopted. Thus, the court concluded that the property owner should be allowed to introduce additional evidence regarding (1) zoning comparisons from other towns relating to open space, set back, and height requirements, (2) testimony from an appraiser or land use planner relative to open space, set back, height requirements and devaluation of the property, (3) testimony, reports, and maps, but only to the extent that this evidence supported the allegation that the open space requirement of the zoning change constituted an unlawful taking in violation of the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The property owner was allowed to introduce additional evidence to the extent that this evidence supported the allegation that the open space requirement of the zoning change constituted an unlawful taking.

MJM Land Dev. v. Madison Inland Wetland Ass'n


CV030484371S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2392



August 13, 2004, Decided  
August 13, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court will not allow the record to be supplemented by this field inspection report. The only addition to the record will be the first item, the letter of David Lord, dated August 3, 2003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought review of a zoning decision made by appellee inland wetland association, and moved to supplement the record pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought to supplement the record with (1) a letter of a certified soil scientist, (2) a page from a wetland commissioner's guide site plan review handbook, and (3) a field inspection report. The association did not object to admission of the letter. The court noted that it had discretion to take additional evidence under § 8-8 only when the record was insufficient or when there was an extraordinary reason for doing so. As to the handbook, the developer alleged that one or all of the association's commissioners looked at it during the hearing. There was no showing, however, that any commissioner or the association as a whole relied upon or referred to the particular page sought to be introduced. Without any suggestion of irregularity as to what the association did or did not consider, this evidence could not be added to the record. As to the field inspection report, there was nothing to indicate that the association considered it for any purpose, that it was prepared at the association's behest, or that any of the association's members adopted the observations made in the report.


OUTCOME: The only addition to the record was the letter of the certified soil scientist.

State v. Henderson


CR9385061


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 17 AT BRISTOL


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2395



August 11, 2004, Decided  
August 11, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Henderson, 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 20 (Conn. App. Ct., Jan. 10, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Henderson, 82 Conn. App. 473, 844 A.2d 922, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 154 (2004)



DISPOSITION: This sentence was harsh, but cannot be vacated as illegal under the limited jurisdiction afforded to him under the motion presented to this court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an enhanced sentence of 10 years, imposed upon him pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-40b by a motion to correct an illegal sentence under Conn. Gen. Book, R. Super Ct. § 43-22.


OVERVIEW: Prior to his conviction, defendant had been convicted of many relatively minor crimes over the course of 15 years, and he was also accused at his sentencing hearing of committing numerous crimes while released on bond and while on trial. The trial judge exercised his discretion and sentenced him to serve 15 years of a possible 21 year term, based upon charges for which he was either convicted or pleaded guilty. Defendant disputed that his plea was fully understood and voluntary at the time of his canvass on the second-part charges. However, the claims presented in defendant's case were distinguishable from the constitutional claims involving double jeopardy, as well as the areas of jurisdiction that authorized the trial court to correct an illegal sentence. Where defendant claimed an Apprendi violation since there was no jury trial on the facts that gave rise to his enhanced sentence, accurate information regarding the predicate charges was before the court through the second part of the information, and defendant admitted the facts attendant to that information when he pleaded guilty and was canvassed by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1509 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rottier v. Town of Guilford Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CVX20030480942


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2231



August 5, 2004, Decided  
August 6, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adjoining property owners appealed from the decision of defendant city planning and zoning commission, which granted an application by retailer for a special permit to expand its grocery store.


OVERVIEW: The retailer sought to transform the existing 35,000-square-foot supermarket into a 55,700-square-foot World Class Market. This expansion would increase the shopping center's footprint from roughly 153,000 to 167,700 square feet and, therefore, required a special permit under Guilford, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 273-128L. Among other errors, the adjoining owners argued that the proposed building violated the zone's maximum expansion regulation. To apply, Guilford, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 273-131 required a building that existed as of its effective date and that the building be non-conforming under the regulations with respect to maximum building size, maximum coverage, or maximum floor area. If those two requirements were satisfied, the building could expand by special permit only, and that expansion could not exceed five percent of the building's total floor area. The court found that the shopping center in question met the two standards. Furthermore, the court found that the proposed expansion exceeded the permissible five percent. Therefore, the court held that the commission erred in granting the variance.


OUTCOME: The appeal was sustained.

Villanueva v. Hartford Democratic Registrar of Voters Olga I. Aviles


CV044001055S, CV 04 4001055 S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2091



August 4, 2004, Decided  
August 5, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court finds that on balance a preliminary injunction should not issue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff congressional candidate sought an injunction to compel defendant Connecticut State Elections Enforcement Commission to recertify her as a primary candidate, arguing that the commission's actions violated her due process rights and required protection under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983 and 1988. The commission moved to strike her complaint.


OVERVIEW: The candidate's brother circulated petitions on behalf of her primary candidacy. He forgot that he had lived outside the district briefly and had to re-register as a local party member before his involvement would be legal under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410. Although he registered as soon as he realized his mistake, the signatures had been gathered and it was too late. The court considered the Commission's argument that the candidate lacked standing to seek expedited action under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-329a, and it decided that while she probably lacked standing under that provision, it was not clear that she was seeking relief thereunder. It therefore went on to consider whether she had met the test for entitlement to preliminary injunctive relief. Since Conn. Gen. Stat. § 9-410 was a regulatory scheme designed to preserve the good order of elections, the burden was on the candidate to show likelihood of success on the merits. The candidate had not met that burden, particularly since she had not made a constitutional challenge to that statute in her pleadings.


OUTCOME: Although the court did not strike the candidate's complaint, it did deny her request for a preliminary injunction.

 

1511 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Harrison v. New Haven Bd. of Zoning Appeals


CV030477037


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2204



August 2, 2004, Decided  
August 2, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Harrison v. New Haven Bd. of Zoning Appeals, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1832 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a cease and desist action, plaintiff property owner moved for permission to present additional evidence concerning the nature of the use of an easement involved.


OVERVIEW: The owner was ordered to cease and desist the use of his rights of way because they were established in violation of New Haven, Conn. Zoning Ordinance § 12 B.2(c). Specifically, the order recited that the establishment of rights of way without a special exception in the residential was a violation of the zoning ordinance. The owner contended that under the circumstances a special exception was unnecessary and §12.B.2.(c) was inapplicable in that that provision only regulates non-residential uses. The use of the subject rights of way was entirely residential. Counsel for the owner wrote a fairly lengthy and quite articulate letter to the chairman of the board prior to the hearing date. The letter was read into the record by counsel at the request of the chairman and fully set forth the background regarding the easements and the owner's position. There was nothing to prevent the presentation of that evidence at the hearing before the board. The additional evidence would not have been admissible under one of the "as of right" categories previously discussed by the court.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1512 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Shenkman v. Borough of Fenwick Historic Dist. Comm'n


CV030102997


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2024



July 26, 2004, Decided  
July 26, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant borough historic district commission denied portions of plaintiff owners' application to enclose a screened porch on their property. The owners requested review. The commission moved to strike the owners' two counts for declaratory judgments, asking the court to declare certain of the criteria utilized by the commission to be fundamentally unfair, unduly vague, and unconstitutional, both facially and as applied.


OVERVIEW: The commission contended that the administrative appeal could not be joined in the same action with claims for declaratory judgments, as they would have had the effect of declaring the very regulations under which the owners had brought their requests to the commission to be unconstitutional. The court noted, however, that the rule had been relaxed in Connecticut in the interests of alternative pleading and in the interests of judicial economy. Therefore, the court allowed the owners' declaratory judgment counts (regarding the constitutionality of the land use regulations) to remain. The court's decision was based in part upon the owners having followed the notice provisions applicable to declaratory judgment proceedings, such that all potentially interested property owners had been notified. The court also noted a recent case that stated the constitutionality attack constituted the kind of general attack upon land use regulations that it indicated were to be the subject of a declaratory judgment action rather than an appeal from the denial of an application submitted pursuant to the land use regulations.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to strike.

 

1513 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hong T.


CR02563146S, CR02562000


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


48 Conn. Supp. 610; 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2062; 854 A.2d 827



July 21, 2004, Decided  
July 22, 2004, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and new trial denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a judgment of acquittal or a new trial after the court convicted him of two counts of assault in the third degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-61(a)(1), one count of assault in the second degree with a dangerous instrument in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-60(a)(2), and one count of injury or risk of injury to children in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with assault, assault with a dangerous instrument, and injury or risk of injury to children, for violations against his 14-year-old daughter. She alleged that he struck her in the vagina with an iron and that he violated her vagina with a sexual aid. Defendant was convicted. He then sought a judgment of acquittal or a new trial. The court denied his motions, finding that the medical evidence from the doctor who examined the victim and a DNA expert who examined the sexual aid supported the jury's verdicts. The court also found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-21(a)(2) provided fair warning of the conduct that it prohibited and that defendant's vagueness argument that the statute did not fairly warn that its terms could be violated when the victim may already have been "morally impaired" would only be applicable if, at the time defendant was committing the acts constituting the offense, he knew the victim was engaged in sexual conduct with someone else. However, the court found that the evidence showed that defendant did not learn of the existence of his daughter's relationship with her boyfriend until after the sexual assaults.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motions for judgment of acquittal and a new trial.

 

1514 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Russo v. Conair Corp.


CV030483600


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1797



June 30, 2004, Decided  
June 30, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchaser sued defendants, a manufacturer and a retailer, under claims of product liability and punitive damages, arising from injuries received by the purchaser. The manufacturer and the retailer filed an answer and sought special damages. The purchaser filed a motion to strike three of the special defenses of failure to state a cause of action on which relief could be granted, laches, and the constitutional right of equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser's claims arose from using a heating pad that the manufacturer had made and which was sold by the retailer. The special defenses alleged that (1) the purchaser's allegations claiming recklessness failed to state a cause of action on which relief could be granted; (2) her action was barred by the doctrine of laches, and (3) her punitive damages claims were unconstitutional because they violated the right to equal protection. The court found that, as to the first special defense, the manufacturer and the retailer improperly challenged the recklessness cause of action with a special defense deficient in supporting fact. Further, as to the second special defense, although the purchaser requested relief in equity, the nature of the action in the alleged counts sounded in product liability and recklessness as an action at law, and as such, the statute of limitations in the applicable statutes applied to the exclusion of the equitable doctrine of laches. Finally, the manufacturer and the retailer limited their third special defense to constitutional grounds, and the purchaser demonstrated that punitive damages were constitutional in actions for product liability.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike certain of the special defenses was granted.

 

1515 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ferrigno v. Leblang


CV0455031S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1762



June 28, 2004, Decided  
June 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a teacher and school officials, a town board of education, and the town, filed a motion to strike a variety of counts from a complaint by plaintiff, an injured minor and his parents, arising from the teacher's having thrown a lacrosse block/baton at the minor, which struck him in the face and caused injury.


OVERVIEW: The counts that were the subject of the motion to strike alleged causes of action for res ipsa loquitur, constitutional violations under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and counts pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 10-235 and -240. The trial court granted summary judgment to the city on several counts, including the count under § 10-240. As to the remaining counts sought to be stricken, the court noted that res ipsa loquitur was a doctrine of evidence and not a cause of action distinct from a claim of negligence. Accordingly, the claims of negligence already pleaded against each defendant made the res ipsa loquitur claims duplicative, as well as procedurally improper. The court found that the claim against the teacher under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 was proper, as the facts were sufficient to support an abuse of power that was "literally shocking to the conscience." However, the claim was insufficient as to the other defendants, as there was no basis to show an equal rights violation or that those defendants condoned such actions. The claim pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-235 was stricken against the board, as there was no statutory direct action available thereunder for prospective plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to strike all of the viable counts raised in the motion, except as to the claim under § 1983 against the teacher.

 

1516 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Naglak v. Ashline


FA920049874S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1580



June 14, 2004, Decided  
June 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed from a decision by the Family Support Magistrate (Connecticut), which granted defendant father's motion to modify his child support obligation. The order eliminated the father's child support obligation pursuant to 2003 Conn. Acts 258 (Act).


OVERVIEW: The mother conceded that the father was incarcerated and that the magistrate was bound by the Act to eliminate the father's child support obligation. The appellate court held that the mother properly raised her constitutional challenge to the Act for the first time on appeal, as a magistrate could not rule on the constitutionality of a statute. The Act did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, as child support guidelines legislation was not under judicial control. The statute also did not violate the Due Process Clause. The legislature provided constitutionally adequate process by enacting the statute, publishing it, and affording those within the statute's reach a reasonable opportunity both to familiarize themselves with and to comply with the Act's requirements. Further, a procedural due process challenge had to be evaluated in context, and there was no indication that the father owned anything of value. Finally, the mother did not belong to a suspect class and did not allege the impairment of a fundamental constitutional right. The mother failed to show that the statute was arbitrary or had no rational basis.


OUTCOME: The decision of the magistrate was affirmed.

 

1517 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Consumer Credit Coalition of Conn. v. Lodi


CV030100918S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1297



May 18, 2004, Decided  
May 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, employees of the Connecticut Department of Banking, filed a motion for summary judgment in an action by plaintiffs, a consumer debt adjustment company and its president, which alleged violations of plaintiffs' First Amendment and equal protection rights in an action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Some of the counts in the 12-count complaint had been previously dismissed.


OVERVIEW: The company was regulated by the Department. One of the employees conducted a routine unannounced audit, which the president indicated was at a very busy time. Nonetheless, he cooperated until the employee engaged in an elaborate delaying ritual, which caused the president to become frustrated and he asked the employee to leave. This led to the president writing a long email to another employee, which resulted in multiple investigations and threats of regulatory reprisals. Plaintiffs brought the instant action. Claims against one Department official were dismissed due to immunity, and claims by the president were dismissed due to lack of standing. Defendants sought summary judgment on the remaining claims. The court found that the company had committed violations of the banking laws, which formed the basis of the employees' actions in conducting an investigation, imposing a penalty, and revoking its license. The Department's actions were objectively reasonable, and the company failed to show, for purposes of overcoming the qualified immunity, that the employees acted on an improper motive. Nor was there any connection between the protected speech and the employees' actions.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion.

 

1518 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gillespie


CR760197288


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1315



May 7, 2004, Decided  
May 21, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Gillespie, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 456 (Conn. App. Ct., Nov. 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a motion to reopen judgment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 17-4 and to enter the same judgment as previously entered, except it requested that the judgment be entered on the correct docket number. Defendant, filing a motion to dismiss, claimed that the error deprived the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of assault. He was committed to the jurisdiction of the Connecticut Commissioner of Mental Health for 20 years. The maximum term of commitment expired on May 1, 1995. In a later case, defendant was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of murder. He was committed to the Commissioner for a period of time not to exceed 25 years. Defendant's maximum term of commitment had an expiration date of January 24, 2004. As defendant's release date in the murder case approached, the State petitioned for continued commitment beyond the release date. The State inadvertently filed the petition under the docket number for the assault file. The defect was a circumstantial defect that, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-123, did not abate the pleadings or deprive the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction. Defendant was aware that the file at issue was the murder file. The murder file was the only one of the two files over which the trial court retained jurisdiction. Furthermore, the parties understood during every aspect of the proceeding that the proceeding pertained solely to the murder file.


OUTCOME: The State's motion to reopen judgment was granted. The orders of the trial court on December 23, 2003, stood, and the orders were applied to the correct docket number.

 

1519 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bolton v. City of Bridgeport


040409828


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1128



April 29, 2004, Decided  
April 29, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff firefighter applicants filed an action against defendants, a city, its fire department, and its civil service commission, seeking declaratory relief to determine the legality of the rank order list of firefighter positions to be filled, and also seeking injunctive relief to nullify the list and to order a new firefighter examination.


OVERVIEW: The applicants for the entry-level firefighter position completed their application and were eligible for hire. Based on their test performance, they were ranked on a hiring list. The court considered an order to show cause as to why a preliminary injunction should not issue, restraining the commission from hiring candidates pursuant to the existing rank order list. Defendants sought dismissal, alleging that the applicants had not exhausted their administrative remedies and accordingly, that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The court analyzed relevant portions of the city charter and determined that the claims all involved the administrative work of the personnel department under Bridgeport, Conn., Charter § 206(a)(4). Accordingly, the applicants should have exhausted their administrative rights to appeal before seeking judicial intervention. There was no due process violation caused by vagueness, as they had fair warning of their right to appeal to the commission. Their claim of a violation of the Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq., also was barred by a failure to exhaust the administrative remedy available to them.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the complaint as to all applicants except one who had administratively appealed. As to that applicant, the court treated the motion to dismiss as a motion to strike and granted that motion. The court denied the application for temporary injunctive relief.

Jacques v. Town of Waterford Planning Zoning Comm'n


566413


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1139



April 27, 2004, Decided  
April 28, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a decision of defendant town planning and zoning commission (Connecticut), which granted a neighboring property owner's application for a zone change and which also approved certain amendments to the zoning regulations.


OVERVIEW: The court initially determined that the property owners were statutorily aggrieved pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(a)(1). The neighbor was granted a zone change and an amendment to the town zoning regulations in order to create a seaside preservation zoning district and to provide regulations for such district. The court found that the regulations were reasonably precise and adequate to give affected parties notice of their rights and obligations. Further, both the change and the amendments were found to be consistent with the comprehensive plan and reasonably related to the police power purposes found in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-2. Accordingly, the zone change was not spot zoning, nor would it disturb the tenor of the neighborhood. Rather, the zoning amendment was tied directly to the existing regulations which made up the comprehensive plan. The zone change furthered the preservation of historic properties and assured waterfront access to the public.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

1521 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Graff v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV010095652


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1008



April 14, 2004, Decided  
April 14, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Graff v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 277 Conn. 645, 894 A.2d 285, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 106 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Graff v. Town of Killingworth, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3398 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 22, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner challenged a decision by defendant town zoning board of appeals, which voted to uphold a zoning enforcement officer's (ZEO) cease-and-desist order (CDO) requiring the landowner to remove pet dogs from her property because they numbered more then four.


OVERVIEW: The ZEO made a CDO requiring the landowner to remove some of her 14 pet dogs because she was not in compliance with the town's zoning regulations regarding the operation of a kennel. The landowner denied she operated a kennel and she challenged the CDO, but the board upheld it on a finding that the landowner was not in compliance with an allowed accessory use of being able to keep four or fewer dogs on the property. The landowner appealed, primarily arguing that the board acted in an ultra vires manner when it voted to uphold the CDO because there was no numerical limit in the zoning regulations on the keeping of dogs as household pets. The landowner further claimed that the board could not uphold a zoning commission's resolution that defined the keeping of four or fewer pet dogs as an allowed accessory use because that was an impermissible attempt to adopt a zoning regulation. The court found that the board acted in an ultra vires way by making a decision predicated on a commission resolution that was adopted without adherence to notice and public hearing requirements of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3(a).


OUTCOME: The court sustained the landowner's appeal.

 

1522 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. K.B.


MV02043554266, CR020098809S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT NORWALK


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1836



April 14, 2004, Decided  
June 24, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested after being observed driving erratically and was charged with driving under the influence in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a, reckless driving in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-222a, and risk of injury to a child in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21. She elected bench trial, and argued that she had not been informed that the allergy medication she was taking would interact badly with other medications.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was being treated for depression, Crohn's Disease, and other problems, with attendant medications. She took an over-the-counter allergy medication that was contraindicated for use with her other medications shortly before taking a short drive with her young daughter. Defendant had not been warned about the dangers of extreme drowsiness, and was arrested after being observed driving erratically. The court found defendant guilty of driving under the influence despite the involuntariness of her intoxication, because it was a general intent crime, and she should simply have stopped driving when she began to feel symptoms. The court found her not guilty of the other two crimes, however, because as charged, they included components of recklessness, and involuntary intoxication could be a defense to crimes of recklessness.


OUTCOME: The court found defendant guilty of driving under the influence but found her not guilty of the other two offenses.

Ellef v. Select Comm. of Inquiry


CV040832432, CV040832411, CV040832524


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 991



April 8, 2004, Decided  
April 8, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at Tunxis Plantation Country Club, Inc. v. Select Comm. of Inquiry to Recommend to Impeach Governor John G. Rowland, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1096 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 23, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff investigative targets filed a complaint for injunctive relief and motions to quash subpoenas duces tecum after defendant legislative committee issued subpoenas to them in its investigation of the governor's alleged misconduct and possible impeachment. The legislative committee moved to dismiss and alleged the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the investigative targets' complaint and motions.


OVERVIEW: The legislative committee issued subpoenas directed to the investigative targets in the legislative committee's investigation of alleged misconduct and possible impeachment of the governor. The investigative targets responded by filing a complaint for injunctive relief and motions to quash subpoenas duces tecum. The legislative committee, in turn, filed a motion to dismiss the complaint for injunctive relief and motions to quash subpoenas duces tecum and alleged that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The trial court considered the materials filed and granted the legislative committee's motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. It first found that the legislative committee's issuance of the subpoenas to the investigative targets was immune from judicial review at that stage in the proceedings pursuant to the Speech or Debate Clause of the Connecticut Constitution, art. III, § 15. It also found it could not intervene in the legislature's exclusive jurisdiction over impeachment proceedings because the investigative targets had not alleged sufficient facts to support an egregious and irreparable constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The legislative committee's motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1524 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


184 Windsor Ave., LLC v. State


CVH7060, H1255


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, HOUSING SESSION AT HARTFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 828



April 1, 2004, Decided  
April 1, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by 184 Windsor Ave., LLC v. State, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 256 (Conn., July 5, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sued the State of Connecticut for breach of a lease. The State of Connecticut moved to dismiss the case.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's predecessor in interest entered into two leases with the State. The landowner alleged that the State failed to pay additional rent under real estate tax escalation clauses in the two leases. The Office of the Connecticut Claims Commissioner denied the landowner permission to sue the State because the lease clauses concerning additional rent for tax increases were invalid, as they were never approved by the Connecticut State Properties Review Board. The court found that the property interest asserted by the landowner was a rent escalation clause that was declared illegal and unenforceable by the Claims Commissioner. The landowner could have returned to the State Properties Review Board to have the modification in the lease approved. After the Claims Commissioner invalidated the escalation clause in the leases, the landowner could have sought assistance at the Connecticut General Assembly. However, the landowner did neither. The court did not consider the invalid lease term to be property within the meaning of the proprietary protections afforded by the State and Federal Constitutions. Therefore, the case was barred by sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1525 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wolff v. Town of Watertown


CV030175538S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 777



March 19, 2004, Decided  
March 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by Wolff v. Town of Watertown, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1267 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 2, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a town and its planning and zoning commission, alleging that the commission lacked the authority to compel him to contribute to the town sidewalk fund, that the town had been unjustly enriched, and that Watertown, Conn., Subdivision Regs. § 5.4 violated Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25 and was unconstitutional. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Several years before the owner filed suit, the commission approved the owner's application to construct a subdivision subject to the condition that he contribute to the town's sidewalk fund in lieu of constructing sidewalks. The owner paid in full but brought this action after the commission amended Watertown, Conn., Subdivision Regs. § 5.4 four years later to specifically authorize such a contribution. Dismissing only the first two counts, the court held that (1) the owner could not collaterally attack the commission's decision because the condition did not violate public policy as it ceased to exist once the owner made the contribution and because the commission's lack of jurisdiction was not "entirely obvious," the owner had the opportunity to challenge commission's jurisdiction at the time, and the commission's conduct was not so far outside what could have been regarded as a valid exercise of its power; but (2) the owner satisfied the conditions necessary to challenge the constitutionality of the amended regulation because he satisfied the classical aggrievement test and all other conditions necessary to maintain an action under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 17-55.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dismiss the count challenging the constitutionality of the town's amended subdivision regulation, but it granted the motion to dismiss the owners' collateral attacks on the initial condition.

St. Pierre v. Town of Berlin


CV030523835S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 785



March 18, 2004, Decided  
March 18, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff businessman filed suit in the trial court (Connecticut) against defendants, a town and its manager, seeking to have Berlin, Conn., Ordinance art. IV, § 14 declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The businessman argued that the ordinance was void as it made violation of the ordinance subject to sanctions more severe than allowed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c)(10)(A). The trial court held that the suit was capable of resolution without passing upon the ordinance's constitutionality. Berlin, Conn., Municipal Code § 14-243 provided the penalty for violation of the ordinances on sexually oriented businesses. The trial court was unable to find authority that granted the town the power to arrest an individual and charge him with a misdemeanor for violating the sexually oriented businesses ordinance. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-148(c) did not grant such power. Although the town did not have the power to charge those violating the ordinance with a misdemeanor, the entire ordinance was not invalid. The trial court's power to sever was an inherent judicial power. There was no indication that the town intended the misdemeanor provision to be unseverable, and Berlin, Conn., Municipal Code § 1-13 showed that the town preferred severance in the event of a successful legal challenge. The portion of the ordinance enabling a misdemeanor arrest for a violation of its provisions was ultra vires.


OUTCOME: The portion of the ordinance enabling a misdemeanor arrest for a violation of the ordinance regulating sexually oriented businesses was invalid. The remainder of the ordinance was valid.

 

1527 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Turonis v. Patterson


X08CV030198437, X08CV040465933


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT STAMFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 669



March 12, 2004, Decided  
March 12, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Two cases dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a proposed plan to convert defendant mutual savings bank (MSB) to a capital stock bank under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36a-136, plaintiff depositors sued the MSB, directors, and corporators, for fiduciary duty and contract breaches, tortious interference, and violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. Defendants moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Two similar putative class action suits were consolidated to decide motions to dismiss. The court, in granting the motions, decided that the depositors had not exhausted their Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36a-136 administrative remedies with the banking department (BD) to contest the plan, which the BD had conditionally approved, to determine if it was "fair to depositors" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36a-136(j), primarily by not using the BD's Conn. Regs., Conn. State Agencies § 36-1-46 declaratory judgment procedures. Those procedures clearly were available to the depositors, and had been adopted by the BD under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176(b) for use by "any person" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-176(a) and "any interested person" under Conn. Regs., Conn. State Agencies 36-1-46. The depositors essentially alleged that the 1838-created MSB's equity was owned by all depositors and that the plan was fundamentally unfair to them as it enriched and entrenched defendants and MSB management at depositor expense without fair, adequate, and full compensation. That was essentially the same, not a different and separately justiciable, "fairness" issue the BD was first to decide under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 36a-136.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motions to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, and dismissed both actions.

 

1528 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Letz v. Town of N. Stonington


565415


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 561



March 2, 2004, Decided  
March 2, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The appeal is sustained and the decision appealed from is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner challenged a decision by defendant town zoning board, which granted defendant land purchaser's application for a zoning regulation variance.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser bought a lot and wanted to sell the lot as a home, but needed a variance to do so. The board granted the variance, and the neighbor appealed. The board and the purchaser argued the neighbor could not appeal because he was not an owner of adjoining land and was not an "aggrieved person" under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(a)(1). The court found that the neighbor's fiduciary deed was sufficient to convey good title to the neighbor, and the neighbor's land abutted the purchaser's lot, so he was statutorily aggrieved under § 8-8(a)(1) and could prosecute the appeal. The court next found that the purchaser did not meet the burden of proof required for a variance. The purchaser failed to show that strict application of the town's zoning regulation produced an unusual hardship simply because he could not convert the property into the use he wanted. Moreover, the purchaser failed to show that the requested variance would not substantially affect the town's comprehensive zoning plan. Therefore, the board exceeded its authority by granting the variance after the purchaser wholly failed to meet either of the conditions required for a variance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision granting the variance.

 

1529 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hurdle v. Somanath


(X02)CV030176929S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1072



February 25, 2004, Decided  
February 25, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, as executrix and individually, filed a medical malpractice action against eight defendant healthcare providers as a result of the death of her son. The private healthcare providers filed a "notice of intent to seek apportionment" against former federal healthcare providers. The executrix moved to strike any apportionment claim.


OVERVIEW: Two of the federal healthcare providers had argued they were federal employees under the Federally Supported Health Centers Assistance Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 233, and had removed the case to federal district court which then substituted the United States as a defendant, thus essentially dismissing the claims against them. The district court then dismissed the case against the United States for failure to exhaust administrative remedies under the Federal Tort Claims Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 2671 et seq. The state court held that for the first 120 days after the return date, the individual federal providers were parties to the action, thus Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-102b(a) was inapplicable. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-102b(c) was inapplicable because the executrix did not settle or release the federal providers as they were dismissed. Thus, the federal providers were no longer parties. There was no statutory authority for the apportionment claims. The federal providers were immune from liability in the state court and, pursuant to § 52-102b(c), could not become apportionment defendants. In any case, sovereign immunity shielded the United States and its employees from suit.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted.
