State v. Mills


132873


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 345



February 19, 2004, Decided  
February 19, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to preclude a capital penalty hearing and alleged in it that Connecticut's capital felony sentencing statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a, was unconstitutional on a number of grounds in a case where defendant was convicted of killing three people, including two children, and the State sought to have the death penalty imposed on defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of committing a triple homicide, which was considered especially horrific because two of the victims were children. The State sought to have the death penalty imposed on defendant. In response, defendant filed a motion to preclude a capital penalty hearing. He argued in support of that motion that the Connecticut capital felony sentencing statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a, was unconstitutional on a number of grounds. After considering his motion, the trial court found it had to be denied. The trial court so concluded because it found that all of the grounds defendant asserted had been rejected by either the United States Supreme Court or the Connecticut Supreme Court. Indeed, it noted that the Connecticut Supreme Court had recently upheld the constitutionality of that statute. Defendant conceded that his arguments were not persuasive and informed the trial court that the arguments were made to preserve the issues in question for reviewing courts. The trial court also found that his claims related to race had to be presented in a habeas corpus proceeding.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to preclude the capital penalty hearing was denied.

 

1531 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Stock v. Pavlucik


CV02977632


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 196



January 26, 2004, Decided  
January 27, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff zoning enforcement officer alleged new construction on defendant homeowners' premises violated city zoning ordinances. The homeowners subsequently obtained a permit. The court considered the homeowners' motion to dismiss and the officer's motion to strike the homeowners' special defenses.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners argued the matter was moot because no actual controversy existed after they obtained the zoning permit, and, by extension, that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. Further, they claimed the fact that the officer still sought attorney fees and costs did not prevent the matter from being rendered moot. The court found the officer met her burden of proving the court had subject matter jurisdiction, as an actual controversy remained regarding damages; the court could still grant the officer practical relief in the form of costs and attorneys fees pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-12. In addition, the doctrine of the law of the case supported this conclusion. The court had previously denied the homeowners' summary judgment motion and held the matter was not moot. Therefore, the court denied the homeowners' motion to dismiss, as they relied on the same grounds and no new circumstances had arisen. Because the court previously ordered the homeowners to obtain a zoning permit and they subsequently complied, the question of the special defenses' legal sufficiency was moot.


OUTCOME: The homeowners' motion to dismiss was denied, and the officer's motion to strike the homeowners' special defenses in their entirety was granted.

 

1532 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rottier v. Town of Guilford


CVX2030480942


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 170



January 23, 2004, Decided  
January 23, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A supermarket applied to defendant zoning commission for site plan approval and a special permit with respect to its property. The zoning commission approved the special permit and site plan, and plaintiff property owners appealed the decision. The commission filed a motion to dismiss the appeal under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-31(1) for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The supermarket's proposal requested permission to add to and expand a pre-existing retail store with associated changes to parking areas and landscaping. The zoning commission approved the special permit and site plan subject to certain conditions. The owners claimed that the supermarket's proposal did not conform to the town's zoning regulations and the commission added conditions which it intended to delegate to other agencies. In its motion to dismiss, the commission argued that the owners were collaterally estopped based on a final decision in an earlier appeal by the owners. The court found that the collateral estoppel claim only applied to one paragraph of the owners former complaint. Also, one of the owners was not a plaintiff in the former action. Consequently, there was no justification for dismissing her as a plaintiff. Further, in the commission's other arguments as to standing, the court found that they were intertwined with the commission's collateral estoppel argument, and thus, for the foregoing reasons, the court did not consider the issue of collateral estoppel by way of a motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The commission's motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1533 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lawrence Mall of New Haven v. City of W. Haven


CV030478088


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 176



January 20, 2004, Decided  
January 20, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a group of city taxpayers, commenced a declaratory judgment action against defendants, a city and a collection agency. The suit sought temporary and permanent injunctive relief prohibiting defendants from charging a 15 percent collection fee when collecting said back taxes. Defendants filed an objection to the class certification, stating that there was no need to certify the class.


OVERVIEW: The legal action alleged various causes of action against defendants arising out of their practices and procedures for the collection of back taxes. The taxpayers argued that their action satisfied the requirements of Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 9-7 and 9-8, in that the necessary elements of numerosity, commonality, typicality, and adequacy were sufficiently met, as were the requirements of predominance and superiority. Defendants argued that the decision as to the constitutionality of the statutes, as claimed by the taxpayers, would bind defendants without the need for class certification. The trial court found that the class potentially consisted of a minimum number of over 2,500 taxpayers. The class included many persons of different income levels, educational levels, ages, and physical abilities, making it unlikely that the proposed class members would seek and retain individual counsel to prosecute their individual claims. Additionally, it would be difficult for the court to manage in excess of 2,500 individual claims. This proposed class challenged defendants' taxing procedures and practices on their face and as they were applied. As such, the class was certified.


OUTCOME: Defendants' objection to class certification was overruled.

 

1534 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Warden


565525


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 96



January 16, 2004, Decided  
January 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Wright v. Radgowski, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 574 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 11, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, sought a writ of habeas corpus. In his petition, the prisoner alleged that he was being denied a parole hearing by an unconstitutional ex post facto application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b).


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of conspiracy to commit murder, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-48 and 53a-54a. The prisoner received a total sentence of 15 years. At the time he was convicted, the prisoner's public defender informed him that he would be eligible for parole upon the completion of 50 percent of his sentence. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a set forth the basic statutory parameters for parole eligibility. Conspiracy to commit murder was not listed as an offense that was not eligible for parole. After defendant's conviction, the Board of Parole amended its rules to include some conspiracy crimes as parole-ineligible crimes. To establish a cognizable claim of an ex post fact violation, the prisoner had to make a colorable showing that the new policy created a genuine risk that he would be incarcerated longer under this new policy than under the previous situation. An employee of the Board of Parole stated that based on defendant's actions, which included shooting the victim in the head to make certain he was dead, the Board of Parole would not have granted parole to the prisoner. Therefore, the court held that there was no ex post facto violation of the prisoner's rights.


OUTCOME: The petition was dismissed.

 

1535 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Elias v. Town of Mansfield Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV020079678


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 135



January 15, 2004, Decided  
January 15, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8, the decision of defendant planning and zoning commission, that granted the application of defendant, an educational society, for a special permit to build a theater complex on their property that bordered the owners' property.


OVERVIEW: The property was owned by the society, and was on the grounds of a local state university. The property owners objected to the commission's approval of the application, contending that the commission failed to take into account parking problems associated with the theater and the fact that similar applications had been denied because such businesses were not authorized in an RAR-90 zone. The court found that the commission's decision regarding the issue of parking was reflective of the uniqueness of the society's proposed use of the subject property and was not arbitrary, capricious, or an abuse of discretion. The record indicated that this proposal was unique. The theater proposal was not a movie theater or a commercial theater venue, it was a replica of an ancient Greek theater designed as a mechanism to promote the goals of the society, the preservation of the Greek language and the cultivation and promotion of Hellenic heritage in the new world. Thus, the commission did not abuse its discretion in determining that the theater was an educational use permissible in an RAR-90 zone.


OUTCOME: The property owners' appeal was dismissed.

 

1536 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Manifold v. Regaglia


CV020124891


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 104



January 14, 2004, Decided  
January 16, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment denied by Manifold v. Regaglia, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2427 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 27, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Manifold v. Regaglia, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2172 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 31, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant government officials filed a motion to reconsider the unsuccessful motion to dismiss that they had earlier filed on the grounds of common-law and statutory sovereign immunity, asserting that the case relied upon in the denial of the motion was subsequently overruled.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' complaint was against the officials in their official and individual capacities. The complaint sought, in part, monetary damages and various injunctions. The trial court had denied the officials' motion to dismiss based on caselaw. The law in Connecticut changed subsequent to the denial of the motion to dismiss. On a claim for money damages, regardless of whether plaintiffs alleged that the officials acted in excess of statutory authority, plaintiffs had to seek a waiver from the claims commissioner before filing suit. The officials, however, did not have statutory immunity for wanton, reckless, malicious actions, or for actions not performed within the scope of their employment. Plaintiffs could circumvent sovereign immunity in declaratory or injunctive relief actions where the officials acted in excess of statutory authority. Thus, the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over plaintiffs' claims filed against the officials in their official capacities that sought monetary damages, because the waiver of the claims commissioner had not been obtained. The claims for injunctive relief and alleging wanton, reckless, or malicious behavior remained.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted insofar as plaintiffs sued the officials in their official capacities seeking monetary, punitive, and exemplary damages and costs and fees. The motion to dismiss was otherwise denied.

State v. Livi


CR2246890


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA-MILFORD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 22 AT MILFORD


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 82



January 13, 2004, Decided  
January 13, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with one count of risk of injury to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1) and one count of breach of peace. Defendant filed a pretrial motion to dismiss the risk of injury count, asserting that § 53-21(a)(1), as applied to the facts of the case, was unconstitutionally vague in violation of state and federal due process.


OVERVIEW: The complainant, while on her way to school, was approached by an older white male, who was later identified as defendant, operating a black vehicle. Defendant was alleged to have told the complainant that he really liked her skirt and asked her if she wanted a ride to school. When the complainant told defendant that she did not want a ride, defendant was alleged to have continued to ask the complainant if she wanted a ride and stated that her skirt was nice and that it might get ruined while walking to school. The complainant said that she did not know who defendant was and that she became extremely upset over the incident. There was no indication in the incident report that defendant ever exited the vehicle or touched the complainant. The court held that defendant approached the complainant, made suggestive remarks to her, and put her in a situation that caused her extreme upset and fear. A person of ordinary intelligence had adequate notice that such a course of conduct would offend Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1538 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Marquez


377482


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 44



January 5, 2004, Decided  
January 5, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion for stay and to preclude offer of judgment interest, his motion for reduction of the verdict due to collateral source payment and his motion in arrest of judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury returned a verdict for plaintiff in her personal injury action against defendant arising out of a motor vehicle accident, defendant filed a motion to stay and preclude the award of offer of judgment interest under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a, objected to certain items in plaintiff's bill of costs pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-257, and moved for a collateral source reduction of the economic damages under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-225a.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff filed an offer of judgment, which defendant chose not to respond to. Subsequently, defendant became aware that plaintiff's injuries had increased. Defendant filed an untimely acceptance to the offer of judgment, but it was rejected by the court, and the case proceeded to trial. Addressing defendant's motions, the court held that (1) because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a conferred a substantive right to interest, Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 1-8 could not abridge that right; (2) defendant was not entitled to preclusion of interest because he was deemed, by operation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a, to have rejected the offer, which was not subject to acceptance unless refiled; (3) plaintiff was entitled to certain items listed in the bill of costs under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-257; and (4) economic damages were not subject to collateral source reductions authorized by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-225a because the partial amount paid by plaintiff's insurer was reduced by the percentage of plaintiff's contributory negligence and offset by the costs of insurance, and because § 52-225a did not authorize a reduction in damages for the health care provider's write-offs.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for stay and to preclude offer of judgment interest, his motion for reduction of the verdict due to collateral source payment, and his motion in arrest of judgment, and it entered judgment for plaintiff, plus interest pursuant to her offer of judgment, together with taxable costs.

1540 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Prigge v. Ragalia


X06CV010167912S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3526



December 18, 2003, Decided  
December 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purported guardians brought an action against defendants, a department of children and families (DCF) commissioner and four DCF employees, in their individual capacities, asserting that defendants acted tortiously and in violation of federal law and the Connecticut and United States Constitutions in their treatment of the guardians concerning the placement of an orphaned child. Defendants moved to strike each count of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The guardians tried to take custody of the child, per his parents' will, after the parents died. Defendants refused to place the child with the guardians based on allegations about their religious practices. The guardians sued under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985, 1986; the Connecticut Constitution; and for intentional infliction of emotional distress (IIED). The court denied the motion to strike the federal claims, which rested on the First Amendment, because there were sufficient facts to state a claim of religious discrimination and specific allegations of a conspiracy. The guardians failed to state a claim under the Connecticut Constitution because there was no direct cause of action thereunder and a statutory remedial scheme for religious discrimination was in place. Defendants were not entitled to qualified immunity because it had been established that it was unconstitutional for state officials to penalize individuals for their religious beliefs. The guardians' willful misconduct and IIED claims survived given the claim of intentional religious discrimination. The court declined to strike the claim for injunctive relief ordering defendants to destroy all relevant DCF records.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendants' motion to strike the guardians' claims that asserted causes of action directly under provisions of the Connecticut Constitution. In all other respects, defendants' motion to strike was denied.

Salaam v. Warden


CV023581, CV023582


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3457



December 15, 2003, Decided  
December 15, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed two amended petitions in which he alleged that respondent state prison warden had failed to correctly calculate the inmate's presentence confinement credit, resulting in the inmate's incarceration being in violation of the Fourth, Fifth, Sixth, Eighth, and Fourteenth Amendments of the United States Constitution as well as of the Connecticut Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had numerous criminal convictions and challenged two dockets in particular, arguing that he was entitled to 546 days of presentence confinement applied to docket one, as well as 304 days of presentence confinement to be applied to docket four. The inmate was totally discharged from the docket one sentence about two years prior to filing the instant petitions. The court had subject matter jurisdiction over the claim as to the discharged sentence in docket one because the inmate was "in custody" for a consecutive sentence that comprised part of an aggregate term. As to the 546 days sought in docket one, the inmate was not entitled to presentence confinement credit for time simultaneously held both in lieu of bond and as a sentenced prisoner. As to docket one, the inmate had received all of the presentence confinement credit to which he was entitled under the law. As to the docket four sentence, the inmate's current controlling sentence, the inmate was not entitled to any presentence credit whatsoever because he was already a sentenced prisoner at the time he was arrested on docket four and remained such during the entire presentence confinement portion on that docket.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's petitions for writs of habeas corpus and entered judgment dismissing the petitions.

Colon v. Malcolm


CV000439285S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3524



December 12, 2003, Decided  
December 18, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state agents and employees, filed a motion for summary judgment in the trial court (Connecticut), which was considered as a motion to dismiss, in a suit for damages under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 9, and 20; 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988; U.S. Const. art. 4, § 2; U.S. Const. amends. V, VIII, and XIV; intentional infliction of emotional distress; and negligence brought by plaintiff injured prisoner.


OVERVIEW: The officials argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction, as they had statutory and sovereign immunity. Specifically, the prisoner claimed that defendants failed to transport him to followup visits after his medical treatment and failed to provide him with the recommended physical therapy. However, the trial court found that the complaint did not sufficiently state a cause of action in recklessness so as to strip defendants of their statutory immunity pursuant to Conn. Gen. 1543 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Santos v. Zarif


CV000158747S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3403



December 10, 2003, Decided  
December 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor filed a motion to set aside the verdict, a motion for remittitur, and an objection to the bill of costs; and plaintiff widow filed a motion to impose offer of judgment interest. The widow sued, seeking to recover monetary damages for wrongful death and loss of consortium as a result of medical malpractice on the part of the doctor.


OVERVIEW: The evidence supported the jury's award to the decedent's estate where the decedent was an accomplished artist and sculptor. Also, evidence of the decedent's artistic endeavors was properly admitted and was not confusing. The widow's surgical expert had a special skill or knowledge directly applicable to reading radiological films and his testimony was helpful to the jury in considering the issues. The fact that he was not a radiologist went to the weight of the testimony, not admissibility. The jury awarded a total amount of $ 2.2 million. While the amount was a considerable sum, given the death of a talented 64-year-old man, who left a widow who had little left for herself in her new country, the award did not shock the sense of justice of the court. The award was supported by the evidence, and remittitur was denied. An award of offer of judgment interest was ordered pursuant Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a(b). Costs related to certain mechanical drawings and photographs were reasonable. Finally, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-260(f), where a full day fee for a doctor was a windfall, the fee was reduced.


OUTCOME: The doctor's motions to set aside the verdict and for a new trial and his motion for remittitur were denied. The widow's motion to impose offer of judgment interest was granted. The doctor's objection to the bill of costs was sustained in part, whereby the costs were reduced by $ 4,000.

 

1544 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re State's Exhibit 11


CV032318


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3420



December 9, 2003, Decided  
December 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Counsel, who represented defendant, referred to as "acquittee," in a criminal trial, and who had, at the request of the acquittee, moved for the trial court to order a grand jury investigation of how the acquittee's redacted e-mail message, referred to as Exhibit 11, got into the State's possession for admission in the trial. The trial court denied the motion and gave counsel notice proposing sanctions. Counsel moved to not impose them.


OVERVIEW: The acquittee was found not guilty of the two charges against her. Exhibit 11 allegedly had a negative effect on her dissolution action and relationship with her child, in spite of her fortuitous acquittal. The counsel contended that Exhibit 11 (1) was an attorney-client privileged communication, (2) had been altered by someone other than the acquittee, (3) was not admissible, and (3) was not subject to any waiver of the privilege. The acquittee was attempting to use unorthodox procedures to find out who was responsible for Exhibit 11, possibly the State or her husband, but should have complained to law enforcement persons or commenced a civil suit. The trial court, discussing the duality of the duty of counsel to the trial court as well as the acquittee, essentially found that counsel's claims were frivolous enough to subject him to sanctions. The frivolousness finding was based, in part, upon the trial court's conclusion that the law was clear that his positions were not sustainable. Counsel had not objected to the admission of Exhibit 11 at trial, and had, in fact, admitted an unredacted version of it at trial. The trial court found the privilege was clearly waived.


OUTCOME: The trial court found clear and convincing evidence that the counsel violated rules of professional conduct regarding his duties to the trial court as an officer of the trial court, frivolous positions, and engaging in conduct that was prejudicial to the administration of justice, denied the counsel's motion not to impose sanctions, and decided it was going to imposed sanctions.

 

1545 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Perley v. Brookfield Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV030347934S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3308



December 4, 2003, Decided  
December 4, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of two decisions of defendant Brookfield, Connecticut, Zoning Board of Appeals. In the first decision, the Board denied their appeal from a zoning enforcement officer's denial of a zoning permit to build on two adjoining properties, and in the second, the Board denied their requests for variances from lot size requirements applicable to those properties.


OVERVIEW: The landowners conveyed their property to a family trust of which they were beneficiaries, leaving themselves with a life interest. The court held that this interest was sufficient to make them aggrieved parties with standing to appeal denial of permission to develop the two substandard-sized, adjoining lots. Because they failed to introduce evidence in the administrative record in the form of a deed predating the regulations that increased the minimum lot size for their district, the landowners failed to show that their lots were entitled to grandfathered status as buildable nonconforming lots. The standard for obtaining a variance pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6 was very high--the landowners would have to have shown that the effect of the minimum lot size would have been the complete deprivation of use of their property. Since the landowners could still develop their lots as a single parcel instead of two, they could not meet that standard.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeals.

 

1546 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Sajgovic v. Warden


CV030003906


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 19 AT SOMERS


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3289



November 24, 2003, Decided  
November 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's Motion to Dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner, who had been returned to prison after he violated parole, requested a writ of habeas corpus against respondent prison warden. The prisoner's request was precipitated by the parole board's setting a date for his next parole hearing 15 years in the future. The warden moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The warden's motion was to dismiss (1) for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the prisoner had not pleaded a cognizable claim, and (2) for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The prisoner had originally been incarcerated, in 1980, for a term of from 15 years to life for the crime of murder. After the prisoner's concessions, the prisoner was saying that he was properly being held in detention, had no right to demand another parole hearing, and that the parole board had no obligation to ever schedule another parole hearing, but that the parole board's rescheduling his hearing 15 years in the future was arbitrary and capricious. That argument was not valid, since the prisoner had conceded that he never had a right to have a hearing scheduled in the first place. The trial court summarized the history of the important writ of habeas corpus, but concluded that the prisoner had not stated a cognizable claim that he had been illegally confined. The prisoner had not stated a legal right of which he had been deprived. There was no illegal confinement.


OUTCOME: The trial court dismissed the petition.

 

1547 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Pools by Murphy & Sons, Inc. v. Dep't of Consumer Prot.


File No. CV-03 0519089S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


48 Conn. Supp. 248; 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3220; 841 A.2d 292



November 21, 2003, Decided  
November 21, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 3, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed to order Murphy make restitution to Fisher of $ 2700 deposit. Appeal of Murphy sustained to commissioner's order Murphy reimburse Fisher for $ 1000 in attorney's fees paid by Fisher to his attorney.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner pool contractor filed an administrative appeal pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183 to challenge a decision of the Commissioner of the Department of Consumer Protection, which found that it had violated the Home Improvement Act (the Act), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-418 et seq., and ordered that the contractor, among other things, was to pay restitution to a consumer pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-432(h) and was not entitled to setoff.


OVERVIEW: The contractor and the consumer entered into a written contract for construction of a pool that fully complied with the requirements set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-429 and contained a notice of the consumer's right to cancel. The consumer properly exercised that right, but the contractor's salesman negotiated an oral agreement that was never reduced to writing. The contractor rendered certain services in the nature of preliminary work, and the consumer again cancelled the contract, but the deposit was never returned. Affirming in part and reversing in part, the court held that: (1) the contractor could not recover via a theory of quasi-contract of quantum meruit for partial or even full performance of the contract because the contract did not comply with the Act; thus, the commissioner properly denied setoff; (2) the contractor did not carry its burden of showing beyond a reasonable doubt that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-432 was unconstitutional under Conn. Const. arts. 2, 4, § 1 because the Act did not significantly interfere with the orderly conduct of superior court judicial functions; but (3) there was no direct evidence of the reasonableness of the consumer's attorneys fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the commissioner as to his order that the contractor make restitution to the consumer of the deposit, but the court sustained the contractor's appeal as to the commissioner's order that the contractor reimburse the consumer for attorneys fees.

 

1548 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Reid v. Armstrong


CV010813272S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3287



November 19, 2003, Decided  
November 19, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Reid v. Comm'r of Corr., 2006 Conn. App. LEXIS 16 (Conn. App. Ct., Jan. 10, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Petition for habeas corpus DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a former prison inmate, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus after his parole was revoked. The inmate claimed that the condition upon which his parole was revoked was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: In 1957, the inmate was convicted of murder, and sentenced to death. The death sentence was subsequently commuted to life in prison, and the inmate was eventually paroled. However, the inmate's parole was revoked after being accused of inappropriate sexual advances upon a counselor. In his petition for habeas corpus, the inmate claimed that a certain phrase contained in his parole orders was void for vagueness and was, therefore, unconstitutional. The trial court concluded that no reasonable person would not know that attempted sexual assault, inappropriate sexual advances which included physical touching in the woman's private parts which in itself was a sexual assault, and threatening the woman with such language as she had described that clearly put her in fear of her life, were actions by the inmate which were incompatible with the welfare of society. Accordingly, the phraseology of condition 11 of the inmate's parole was not unconstitutionally vague. Further, the trial court noted that at least 16 other states utilized the standard that the conduct must be compatible with the welfare of society.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

1549 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Tedesco v. Town of Watertown


CV030177612S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3183



November 17, 2003, Decided  
November 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a town and the town planning and zoning commission, moved to dismiss plaintiff property owner's action arising from a subdivision approval dispute on the grounds that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. Specifically, the commission argued that the property owner did not exhaust his administrative remedies with respect to three counts and the matters were not ripe for review in a fourth count.


OVERVIEW: The property owner applied for a residential subdivision on land that he owned. As a condition for approval, the commission required the property owner to install sidewalks on adjacent property which he did not own at the time. However, he subsequently purchased that property. The commission approved the property owner's plan with a condition that the property agreed to install so much of the sidewalk as allowed by the inland wetlands agency and he would pay into a separate account the necessary monies enabling the town to install the remaining sidewalk. As of the date of the complaint, the town had not completed the remainder of the sidewalk. At the time the application was approved, there was no ordinance or regulation authorizing a "sidewalk fund," nor was there any state statutory authority. Nonetheless, the property owner failed to appeal the commission's decision pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8. The court held that while the commission's actions were not in conformance with its own regulations, that was not enough to find that the property owner had met the high standard allowing for collateral attack. Thus, there was not any actual pending controversy between the parties.


OUTCOME: The property owner's counts were dismissed.

 

1550 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


George v. Town of Watertown


CV030177611S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3198



November 17, 2003, Decided  
November 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by George v. Town of Watertown, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 438 (Conn. App. Ct., Oct. 19, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff zoning applicant instituted a complaint against defendants, a town and a planning and zoning commission, and claimed that the commission's sidewalk fund assessment was illegal, that the town was unjustly enriched, and that a new regulation regarding a sidewalk fund was unconstitutional. Defendants moved to dismiss the applicant's complaint on the ground that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The commission approved the applicant's request for residential subdivision and required him to contribute to a sidewalk fund in lieu of building sidewalks in the subdivision. The applicant paid an assessment in accordance with the subdivision plan. At the time that the application was approved, the town did not have an ordinance or regulation authorizing a sidewalk fund. However, the applicant failed to appeal the commission's decision. The commission later amended its regulations and authorized the payment of fees to a sidewalk fund. The applicant then sued. The court dismissed the applicant's counts that alleged that the commission's sidewalk fund assessment was illegal and that the town was unjustly enriched because the applicant had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies and he further failed to meet the high standard required to permit a collateral attack. The court dismissed the applicant's claim that the new regulation was unconstitutional because he had no pending dispute or controversy with the commission. As there was no actual pending controversy, the matter was not justiciable and invoking Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17-55 did not create subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the applicant's complaint.

 

1551 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Alexander v. Comm'r of Admin. Servs.


468821


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3197



November 12, 2003, Decided  
November 12, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Alexander v. Comm'r of Admin. Servs., 86 Conn. App. 677, 862 A.2d 851, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 562 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Alexander v. Comm'r of Admin. Servs., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 331 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 11, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Connecticut Commissioner of Administrative Services, Commissioner of Correction, and Attorney General, filed a motion to strike the substitute complaint of plaintiffs, an inmate and a decedent's executrix, which alleged a violation of the inmate's constitutional rights after the State applied Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-85b(b) and made a claim against the inmate's inheritance for repayment of his incarceration costs.


OVERVIEW: A decedent's executrix and the inmate filed their original action, which asserted a denial of the inmate's substantive due process rights by the State's attempt to take his inheritance for repayment of incarceration costs, in that the inmate's sentence predated § 18-85b(b). That complaint was stricken and plaintiffs filed a substitute complaint which focused on a violation of the inmate's equal protection rights. The court found that the allegations of the complaint were insufficient to state a cause of action. The court noted that there was nothing that required that taxation had to be equal and uniform. There was no dispute by the inmate as to his incarcerated status, nor to the lien amount, and accordingly, any procedural due process violation was de minimus at best. The court also noted that an inmate had no vested right to free room and board while incarcerated, thereby negating the inmate's substantive due process claim. The equal protection claims lacked merit, as asserting the cost lien randomly was permissible where there was no invidious or illegitimate use of such a lien. The equal protection claims against § 18-85b(b) failed under the rational basis standard.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion.

 

1552 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Comm'r of Transp. v. Oil Barons


CV000438538S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2892



October 17, 2003, Decided  
October 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Comm'r of Transp. v. Oil Barons, Inc., 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1428 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 1, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Where the motion to dismiss filed by plaintiff Commissioner of the Connecticut Department of Transportation in the eminent domain proceeding, alleging that defendant landowner could only appeal the matter with a citation and the appeal was filed beyond the limitations period under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-76, was denied, the trial court revisited the matter in light of a recent Supreme Court of Connecticut decision.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner filed a notice of condemnation and assessment of damages. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-76, the landowner had six months from the filing of the notice to appeal the assessment of damages. Only after the expiration of the six-month period did the landowner receive notice. The six-month limitations period did not begin to run until the landowner received notice of the condemnation. The landowner was not entitled to attorneys fees under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-76a, due to the delay between the filing of a map under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-57 and the filing of a certificate of taking under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13a-73. There was no evidence that the delay caused the landowner to incur attorneys fees. The landowner was entitled to severance damages. The landowner's property was a gas station. The taking made the property less desirable, as it created sloped driveways, and it impacted upon commercial truck access to the gas station. Prior to the taking, the property had a fair market value, based on the income approach, of $ 1,700,000. As a result of the decrease in rental income, the fair market value was reduced to $ 1,270,000, resulting in a loss of $ 430,000.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered in favor of the landowner and against the Commissioner for $ 442,000. In addition, the landowner was entitled to interest at the rate of eight percent per annum from the date of taking, plus a reasonable fee for its appraiser's report.

Webb v. Warden


CV000003239


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 19 AT ROCKVILLE


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2877



October 8, 2003, Decided  
October 8, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Webb, 252 Conn. 128, 750 A.2d 448, 2000 Conn. LEXIS 19 (2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a pro se petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking to challenge the sentence of death that was imposed upon him. Respondent, a warden, filed a motion to dismiss several portions of the instant petition.


OVERVIEW: The warden argued that the prisoner failed to state grounds upon which relief could be granted, failed to satisfy the cause and prejudice test, and that the claims were barred by res judicata or collateral estoppel. The court held that the petition essentially argued that the prisoner's detention and convictions were illegal because he was deprived of his constitutional right to counsel. The court held that it was clear that the petition did, at least on its face, state some grounds upon which relief could be granted. Therefore, the motion to dismiss had to be denied as to all portions of the petition which alleged ineffective assistance of counsel. However, the court held that it lacked authority to declare any final decision of an appellate court, either state or federal, to be in error. A number of the prisoner's claims sought to overturn prior appellate decisions, and the motion to dismiss had to be granted as to those claims. Defendant's claim that Connecticut's capital punishment scheme constituted cruel and unusual punishment also had to be dismissed, as this issue was decided adversely to defendant on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted as to paragraphs 8(b), 8(g), 8(h), 8(i), 8(k), 8(l), and 8(o), and denied as to paragraphs 8(c) 8(d), 8(e), 8(f), 8(n), 9(a), 9(b), 9(c), 9(d), 9(g), 9(m), 9(n), 12(a), 12(b), 12(c), 12(d), 12(f), 12(g), 12(h), and 12(n).

 

1554 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


White v. Conte


CV030081299S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2725



October 6, 2003, Decided  
October 6, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a father, filed suit against defendants, the State, the state support enforcement services division, and a support enforcement officer, seeking injunctive relief; compensatory and punitive damages from the support officer only pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983; and attorney fees and costs from all defendants pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the support officer's recordation of a judgment entered against him for delinquent child support payments, which he allegedly did not owe, violated his constitutional rights. The trial court held the father neither alleged a statutory basis for a waiver of sovereign immunity nor any facts to establish that defendants acted in excess of their statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. The support officer was protected by absolute judicial immunity, as her activities were integrally related to the judicial process and her actions were taken in the course of her official duties. The support officer was entitled to qualified immunity as to the claim for money damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because she did not violate any of the father's clearly established statutory or constitutional rights. Finally, the father's failure to exhaust administrative remedies deprived the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction. The father did not allege that he availed himself of his remedies under the Connecticut Family Support Magistrate's Act, nor did he allege that it would be either futile or inadequate for him to have pursued such relief.


OUTCOME: The father's request for injunctive and monetary relief against defendants in their official or individual capacities was denied. The father was not entitled to costs and attorney fees. Defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction was granted.

 

1555 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Isaiah B.


CP03013615


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3646



September 29, 2003, Decided  
September 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF) moved for articulation, requesting the court to set forth the duties and responsibilities of the guardian ad litem (GAL) who was appointed for respondent mother. The DCF also requested that the court delineate the obligation of the mother's attorney to look to the GAL for decisions made on behalf of the mother.


OVERVIEW: Respondent father had filed an order of temporary custody application, along with a petition alleging that the child was neglected and uncared for. The court appointed a GAL for the mother. The mother had the ability to communicate and function at the level of a person who was aged six to nine. She could not reason in an abstract way. She was incompetent for purposes of trial. The mother made it clear that she preferred the immediate return of her child who was in DCF's care. She did not want the child to remain in the care of others. But DCF's opposition did not, in and of itself, mean that the mother's preferences were not reasonable or that they had not been strongly articulated. Although the mother was not competent for purposes of trial, that status did not extinguish the constitutional protections to which she was entitled as the child's biological parent. The court determined it should hear both the position advocated on behalf of the mother, and the position taken by the GAL, as such a protocol would aid in the achievement of the fair and impartial resolution which was called for.


OUTCOME: The court found that the interests of justice were best served by allowing the GAL to address the mother's best interests, while her attorney advocated to achieve her expressed preferences during the pre-trial and trial proceedings.

 

1556 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fontanella v. Marcucci


CV010275970S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2715



September 23, 2003, Decided  
September 23, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Fontanella v. Marcucci, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 246 (Conn. App. Ct., June 21, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorneys filed a motion for summary judgment against plaintiffs, a car accident victim and his mother, arising out of their claims of legal malpractice and breach of contract against the attorneys.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs retained the attorneys to investigate a potential product liability action on their behalf arising from the car accident, which was possibly due to a defective seatbelt. Before the vehicle's seatbelts were properly inspected, the victim's mother sold the car to her insurer, which then sold it at an auction and it was thereafter destroyed. The legal malpractice claim alleged that the attorneys breached their duty of care by failing to prevent spoliation of the evidence, and that they breached their contractual agreement to provide legal services. The attorneys moved for summary judgment and the court held that the claims were barred by the applicable limitations periods. The legal malpractice claim sounded in negligence due to the alleged breach of the duty of care and came within the three-year tort limitations period of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577. The contract limitations period, whether covered by Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-576 or 52-581, also had run on the claims. There was no relation back to plaintiffs' earlier dismissed action, nor were plaintiffs' constitutional rights to redress violated by imposing limitations periods.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorneys' motion for summary judgment.

 

1557 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


McGovern v. McGovern


FA030194664S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2619



September 16, 2003, Decided  
September 22, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's Motion to Dismiss dated July 10, 2003 and her Motion for Summary Judgment dated July 10, 2003, DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents sought to enforce a decision of the Superior Court, Pima County (Arizona) by registering the foreign matrimonial judgment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-70. The Arizona court determined that defendant mother was not acting in the best interest of a minor child in failing to grant rights of visitation to the grandparents and that the presumption of parental primacy had been rebutted by clear and convincing evidence.


OVERVIEW: The child in question was born in Arizona in 1994 and her mother opposed the grandparents' visitation. The matter had a long procedural history, during which the mother was represented by counsel and took an active role in the case with the exception of leaving the jurisdiction on the eve of a hearing. The grandparents sought to enforce the Arizona judgment and the court held that the Arizona decree was a foreign matrimonial judgment within the meaning of § 46b-70 because the mother was aware of the action's pendency, she had an opportunity to participate fully, and there was no due process violation. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 provided that visitation could be granted upon application of "any person" and the term "grandparent" was included within the broader term "any person" under the statute. Thus, the Arizona decree granting visitation rights to the grandparents did not per se violate the public policy of Connecticut. The court had jurisdiction over the matter pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-1 and the mother's motion to dismiss was denied. The court denied the motion for summary judgment because, at best, it was premature, and as pleaded, the mother did not meet her burden.


OUTCOME: The court denied the mother's motion to dismiss and her motion for summary judgment.

 

1558 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Town of E. Haven v. Town of N. Branford


CV000438153


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2583



September 10, 2003, Decided  
September 11, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court denied defendants' motion for judgment for Counts One through Six and granted defendants motion for Counts Seven through Twenty-Nine.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a town, its mayor, and its manager, moved for summary judgment in the trial court (Connecticut) in the suit filed by plaintiff, a town, seeking injunctive relief and damages for defendants' failure to construct a dam. The suit contained counts for, inter, alia, nuisance, trespass, violations of the Connecticut Environmental Protection Act (CEPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-14, and due process violations.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The trial court held that plaintiff town owned land affected by flooding, and had standing to bring the action. The suit was not moot as to the manager, because plaintiff town sought damages, as well as injunctive relief. Defendants were not entitled to summary judgment due to governmental immunity because a factual issue remained as to whether the cause of plaintiff town's damages was defendants' conduct. Defendants' actions were clearly discretionary, but plaintiff town was within the foreseeable victim exception. There were factual issues as to whether plaintiff town's damages were caused by defendants' refusal to construct the dam for purposes of the nuisance claim. Summary judgment was granted on the trespass claims since there was no evidence that an affirmative, intentional act of defendants caused an invasion or intrusion onto plaintiff town's property. Allegations of omission to prevent flooding were not amenable to remedy under the CEPA. The due process claims failed because plaintiff town provided no support for its allegations that it had been deprived of property.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion for summary judgment was denied as to the nuisance counts. Defendants' summary judgment motion was granted as to the remaining counts.

 

1559 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Drapp


CV030402737


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2516



September 5, 2003, Decided  
September 5, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim commenced an action against defendant alleged stalker for stalking, invasion of privacy, and intentional infliction of emotional distress (IIED). The alleged stalker moved to strike each count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that no civil cause of action for stalking existed in Connecticut. The court agreed, concluding that there was no recognized civil cause of action equivalent to the criminal offense of stalking, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-151e. However, the victim implicitly, if not expressly, alleged sufficient facts to substantiate a cause of action for invasion of privacy. She specifically alleged that the alleged stalker commenced a long and continuous course of conduct involving following, photographing, and telephoning the victim, as well as trespassing on the premises of the victim. She further alleged that the conduct continued throughout the year 2002, during which time defendant was repeatedly arrested for and once convicted for stalking. Finally, the victim properly alleged a cause of action for IIED. Although she did not specifically use the words "outrageous" or "extreme" to characterize the numerous acts alleged, the simple recitation of the acts and the universal abhorrence associated with such conduct permitted a finding that the requisite elements of a cause of action sounding in IIED had been properly pled. Intent could be inferred from the conduct.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the count in the complaint for stalking was granted. The remaining motions to strike were denied.

 

1560 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Courchesne


CR980273002


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2433



September 4, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Courchesne, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2428 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Courchesne, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2365 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 13, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved that the court enter an order precluding the death penalty hearing because he could not be constitutionally sentenced to death under the existing statutory scheme. The court had considered similar claims presented by defendant in his motion to impose a life sentence, which had been denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that since Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(e), (f), and (j) as it related to the weighing of aggravating and mitigating factors did not establish a defined burden of proof, the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court found that the issue was before the Connecticut Supreme Court, but under the existing law the procedure for a weighing determination was constitutional. The requirement that defendant prove that the mitigating factors were mitigating by a preponderance of the evidence did not create a constitutionally intolerable risk that when weighing the aggravating and mitigating factors, jurors would not include mitigating factors. There was nothing in the statutory language or in the law interpreting the language to lead to the conclusion that the jury would refuse to consider mitigating evidence. The statute did not violate the Sixth, Eighth and Fourteenth Amendments to the United States Constitution or Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 9 because there was a meaningful basis for determining when the death penalty was imposed. The statute was not unconstitutional because of its failure to charge individual persons with sentencing authority.


OUTCOME: The motion to preclude the penalty hearing because defendant could not be constitutionally sentenced to death under the existing statutory scheme was denied.

 

1561 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Contractors Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Rocque


CV01080172


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2443



September 2, 2003, Decided  
September 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Contractor's Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Rocque, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 9 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 5, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Contractor's Supply of Waterbury, LLC v. Rocque, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 897 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 19, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land owner's permit to construct and operate a stationary source of air pollution was administratively terminated by defendant, the Department of Environmental Protection (Connecticut), because the plant would violate Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-196, which was enacted after the permit had been issued. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the owner was issued a permit to build a hot mix asphalt plant, § 22a-196 was enacted, which banned siting such plants within one-third of a mile of a watercourse. Since the plant would violate this ban, the Department terminated the owner's permit. The owner alleged that application of § 22a-196 to its permit was an illegal retroactive application of a substantive statute, and that § 22a-196 lacked a rational basis and was thus unconstitutional. The court held that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction because these claims were not justiciable. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-174(n), which went into effect before Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-196, placed a moratorium on the issuance of permits for asphalt batch plants; by its terms, this moratorium applied to the owner. Before the effective date of the moratorium, the owner had a right to proceed with the permitting process in accordance with relevant law; imposition of the moratorium suspended this right and rendered it speculative. No matter how the court ruled on the merits, the owner would still not be able to proceed with the permitting process unless and until the moratorium expired or was otherwise lifted by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the action.
