Morgan v. Bubar


562555


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2404



August 29, 2003, Decided  
August 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment denied by Morgan v. Bubar, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1828 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 15, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, supervisors and coworker, filed a motion to strike the complaint filed by plaintiff injured party alleging common law defamation and violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The injured party, a state employee, claimed that on two separate occasions, the coworker made defamatory statements against the injured party, accusing her of doing violence to the coworker. The statements were communicated to the supervisors of the coworker and injured party. The injured party alleged that the supervisors knew or should have known that the coworker's accusations were false, but they failed to comply with the requirements of an executive order requiring the supervisors to initiate an investigation of violence in the workplace. The 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims made against the supervisors in their official capacities were not subject to being stricken. The trial court found that the suit was brought under § 1983 against the supervisors in their individual or personal capacities for their official actions, as such an action was alleged in two counts of the complaint. Although the injured party failed to adequately set forth an equal protection claim, a motion to strike could not be granted, because the trial court could not strike only the equal protection portion of the § 1983 count, which alleged violations of both due process and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was denied.

 

1563 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Consumer Credit Coalition of Conn., Inc. v. Lodi


CV030100918


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2418



August 27, 2003, Decided  
August 27, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a consumer credit coalition and its president, filed suit against defendants, employees of the Connecticut Department of Banking, in their individual capacities, alleging violations of the First Amendment and equal protection rights of the coalition and its president. The employees moved to dismiss the complaint for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, and moved to dismiss the complaint as to the individual for lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The employees moved to dismiss the suit as to the president for lack of standing. The trial court held that the complaint did not allege a direct injury to the president, separate and distinct of the injuries suffered by the coalition. The president lacked standing to bring the suit and the counts brought in the president's individual capacity were dismissed. The employees' actions in conducting an examination of the coalition's business records were administrative in nature, and thus, the employees were not shielded by absolute immunity. The motion to dismiss as to those claims brought by the coalition against the employees was denied. However, the action against the employee who ordered the revocation of the coalition's license for its failure to cooperate with the Department's investigation was acting in a quasi-judicial capacity and was entitled to absolute immunity. The suit was dismissed against the employee who ordered revocation of the coalition's license.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted as to the counts brought by the president individually. The motion to dismiss was denied as to the official acts of the employees in conducting an examination of the coalition's business records. The motion to dismiss was granted as to the employee's act in ordering the revocation of the coalition's license.

 

1564 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Courchesne


CR980273002


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2298



August 13, 2003, Decided  
August 13, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Courchesne, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2361 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Courchesne, 262 Conn. 537, 816 A.2d 562, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 81 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to declare Connecticut's death penalty statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a, unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. VIII, XIV, and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 9, 20.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that under contemporary standards, capital punishment was not decent, reliable, or of any measurable benefit to society and that it was arbitrary, capricious, and discriminatory. The court held that Connecticut's death penalty statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a, met the minimum constitutional standard under U.S. Const. amend. VIII, XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 9, 20. The multi-tiered pyramid met the prerequisite of consistency and reliability. It channeled the discretion of a sentencing judge or jury to assure that the death penalty was being imposed consistently and reliably and permitted a sentencing judge or jury to consider an individual defendant's character or record and the circumstances of a particular offense. Because it was not within the court's province to overrule or discard the decisions of the U.S. Supreme Court, it was bound to follow them.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1565 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Tuchman v. State


CV030472731S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2333



August 11, 2003, Decided  
August 11, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Tuchman v. State, 89 Conn. App. 745, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 254 (Conn. App. Ct., June 24, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a trucking company and its owners, sued defendants, the State, the department of environmental protection, and an individual, seeking a declaratory judgment that defendants violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and the Connecticut Constitution, a permanent injunction restraining defendants from prohibiting plaintiffs from operating their business, compensatory and punitive damages, and attorney fees. Defendants moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: After the enactment of legislation authorizing the department to regulate the transshipment of hazardous waste, the department issued a notice of violation to plaintiffs and ordered them to cease all transshipment activities or face fines of $ 25,000 per day. Defendants moved to dismiss on the ground that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because they were protected from suit by the doctrine of sovereign immunity and no exception to that doctrine applied. In deciding whether to grant the motion, the court considered whether plaintiffs' allegations and the factual underpinnings of those allegations demonstrated in incursion upon constitutionally protected interests such that sovereign immunity did not bar plaintiffs' action. Among other things, the court found that the plaintiffs did not have a legitimate claim of entitlement to the permit because under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-454, the commissioner had the discretion to deny the application. In addition, the court concluded that keeping one from conducting business did not equate to a taking of property. Finally, plaintiffs failed to show that they were treated differently than any other similarly situated company.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction was granted.

 

1566 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Manifold v. Regaglia


CV020124891


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2172



July 31, 2003, Decided  
August 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Claim dismissed by Manifold v. Regaglia, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 104 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 14, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss counts one and four denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, children and their mother, sued defendants, employees of an agency in their individual and official capacities and others, for damages arising from the agency's action of removing the children from their mother's custody. The agency defendants moved to dismiss counts one and four, which alleged intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress against those defendants.


OVERVIEW: An agency employee received an anonymous call that the children were being abused. A doctor determined that the children were victims of physical abuse, and the children were removed from the mother's custody. While in agency custody, the discoloration of one of the children's skin worsened, and a blood test uncovered the fact that the child had a blood disorder which caused the discoloration that was mistaken for bruising. The mother alleged that agency employees were abusive, insulting, and threatening. The mother also claimed that agency employees continued their harassment after the children were returned. The agency defendants claimed that they were entitled to sovereign immunity and statutory immunity pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The court found that plaintiffs claimed that the agency defendants' conduct was wanton, reckless, or malicious. These allegations, read broadly in plaintiffs' favor, could lead a fact finder to conclude that the agency defendants were acting beyond the scope of their authority. Therefore, the agency defendants were not entitled to sovereign or statutory immunity.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss counts one and four was denied.

 

1567 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conn. Motor Club, Inc. v. Planning Comm'n of Danbury


CV020347398S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2175



July 31, 2003, Decided  
July 31, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Decision of Commission upheld and appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8, plaintiff property owner appealed the decision of defendant, the Planning Commission of the City of Danbury (Connecticut), which denied an application for a special exception because the application created conditions that would adversely affect the traffic safety as specified in Danbury, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 10.C.4.a.(3).


OVERVIEW: The property owner owned a lot that had a 39,540-square-foot building on it. General office use of the property was allowed, but a special exception was needed for uses that generated more than 500 daily vehicle trips. The property owner procured as a potential tenant a group of dermatologists. Because the dermatology practice would generate 600 daily vehicle trips, a special exception was required. On appeal, the property owner raised three claims: that the regulations were unconstitutionally vague, that the Commission's decision was not supported by the record, and that the Commission's decision was against the weight of the expert witness testimony. The court found that there was ample testimony at the hearing as to the heavy traffic congestion that surrounded the property. The property owner's own traffic engineering study and testimony from residents in the area provided a substantial basis for the Commission's decision. In addition, the Commission was not bound to follow any expert's opinion, there was nothing unreasonable, illegal or arbitrary about its decision, and the property owner had not met its burden of showing that the regulations were unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The Commission's decision was upheld and the appeal was dismissed.

Thomas v. Ocif


CV990166939S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2146



July 30, 2003, Decided  
July 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Case dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a terminated deputy, filed a five-count revised complaint against defendant, a fellow deputy, alleging tortious interference, defamation, invasion of privacy by false light, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and negligent infliction of emotional distress. Defendant moved for summary judgment as to all claims on the ground of sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff worked part-time as a bartender. On several occasions, plaintiff engaged in sexual conduct with female customers. At least one woman complained that plaintiff coerced her into having sex. Defendant learned of plaintiff's activities, and reported the information to the sheriff. Defendant also provided an investigator with materials from plaintiff's personnel file which dealt with complaints made against plaintiff while defendant was plaintiff's supervisor. Defendant claimed that sovereign immunity barred the suit because he was acting in his official capacity at all times and at no time exceeded his authority. The court held that nothing defendant was alleged to have done in the present action was outside the scope of his employment. Defendant's conduct in the present action was in furtherance of a legitimate state purpose related to his employment, namely the sheriff department's investigation into allegations of professional misconduct involving a deputy sheriff. Even if defendant was not the proper person to transmit the personnel file materials, such conduct did not rise to the level of being in excess of statutory authority so as to defeat sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The case was dismissed.

 

1569 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gai v. Austin


CV030081648S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2151



July 30, 2003, Decided  
July 30, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a professor, sued defendants, university officials, alleging breach of a mediation agreement. The officials moved to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The professor claimed the parties entered into a contract to suspend all administrative and judicial proceedings and to initiate no new proceedings until a mediation process was completed regarding the professor's continued employment by the university. The professor claimed that the officials breached this agreement by pursuing termination proceedings against the professor. The officials argued that the action was barred by sovereign immunity. The court held that the professor neither sought nor obtained authorization for the suit from a state claims commissioner. The court further held that the professor's claim for injunctive relief did not assert a constitutional or statutory transgression. The court held that an exception to sovereign immunity for action for injunctive relief on constitutional or statutory grounds did not apply where the injunctive relief sought merely asserted a breach of contract. Therefore, the court held that sovereign immunity applied, and the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear and determine the case.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1570 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Edwards v. Univ. of Conn. Health Ctr.


CV010452826S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1990



July 7, 2003, Decided  
July 7, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Edwards v. Univ. of Conn. Health Ctr., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1994 (Conn. Super. Ct., July 7, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State, a hospital, and an individual, moved for summary judgment on the basis of sovereign immunity in plaintiff patient's unlawful disclosure action for a money judgment.


OVERVIEW: The patient sought money damages based on an alleged disclosure of his patient records. The court held that in the absence of specific legislative authority, the claims against the State and the hospital were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. The individual enjoyed the same immunity. There was no claim that the individual acted pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. Even if the sovereign immunity were not available to the individual, she would enjoy statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. There was no evidence of any wanton, reckless, or malicious conduct on her part. Although the patient sought future injunctive relief against possible disclosure or destruction of his medical records, the complaint itself was silent on such possibilities. Therefore, the exception was moot and defendants were entitled to summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1571 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guillory


CR000011284S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 17 AT BRISTOL


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1830



June 27, 2003, Decided  
June 27, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with engaging in the business of a new home construction contractor or holding himself out as a new home construction contractor without having a current certificate of registration, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-417d(d)(5). After a mistrial was declared due to a hung jury, defendant moved to dismiss the charge. The State opposed the motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into agreements with a couple regarding the construction of a new home. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to justify placing him on trial, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction, and the statute defining the offense charged was unconstitutional. The court denied the motion to dismiss holding that the agreement fell within the purview of the New Home Construction Contractors Act. The evidence established that defendant contracted with the owners to construct, for a fee, portions of a home that was in the process of being newly constructed and was not yet occupied. No reasonable interpretation of the term "home remodeler" could have included such activity. Further, a person of ordinary intelligence would have had fair warning that defendant's conduct of contracting with owners of a vacant lot to construct portions of the owners' new home would constitute a violation of the New Home Construction Contractors Act. Thus, the definition of "new home construction contractor" was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the defendant's conduct. Whether or not defendant classified himself as a sub-contractor or home remodeler was irrelevant.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1572 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kearns v. State of Conn. Judicial Dep't


CV020515773S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2024



June 24, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Connecticut Judicial Department filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff former employee's action alleging wrongful discharge on the basis of a physical disability.


OVERVIEW: The employee was employed as a juvenile detention officer by the Department. He alleged that he suffered a severe injury in the course of his employment. He received workers' compensation. The employee returned to work and was assigned to a position that did not require physical contact with detainees. He claimed that he was told that the position would accommodate his medical restrictions. The employee was terminated and was allegedly told that the termination was due to his disability. The employee filed a complaint with the commission on human rights and opportunities, and the complaint was dismissed. The employee's claims under the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 were waived absent express language waiving sovereign immunity. None of the statutes upon which the employee relied, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46a-54, -56, 77, waived sovereign immunity expressly or by necessary implication. Furthermore, a release from jurisdiction document under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46a-100 from the commission did not waive sovereign immunity, as the commission never had jurisdiction over an ADA claim.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted for all claims except for the discriminatory discharge claim.

Carmen v. DOT


CV020512243S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1726



June 11, 2003, Decided  
June 11, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court dismisses the plaintiffs' appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, five individuals who sought to obtain Connecticut marine pilots licenses, challenged the constitutionality of Conn. Agencies Regs. § 15-15a-15, pursuant to which defendant, the Connecticut Commissioner of the Department of Transportation (DOT), declared a moratorium on the issuance of new marine pilot licenses, and declined to issue licenses to those individuals.


OVERVIEW: The individuals challenged the authority of the DOT to regulate the issuance of licenses in their administrative petitions for declaratory judgment ruling requesting that they be issued Connecticut Marine Pilots Licenses, and that the moratorium or freeze pursuant to the regulations be held unconstitutional and void, and for other relief. On appeal, for the first time, the individuals challenged the declaratory judgment ruling as a denial of due process and equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The trial court concluded that the agency properly determined that the moratorium did not place an impermissible burden on interstate commerce. Further, no evidence was presented by the individuals to show how they were treated any differently from anyone else nor to demonstrate why the classification made by the legislature was irrational, and not related to the ends of protecting the public.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1574 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rubenstein v. Statewide Griev. Comm.


CV020516965S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1727



June 10, 2003, Decided  
June 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' appeal dismissed. Judgment may enter in favor of the defendant, the Statewide Grievance Committee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorneys appealed from decisions of appellee Connecticut Statewide Grievance Committee, which affirmed the reviewing committee's decision and reprimanded the attorneys for violations of Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 1.8(e), 7.2(c), but which refused to find that one attorney violated Rule 7.2(c).


OVERVIEW: The attorneys argued that their payment of clients' medically related costs as court costs and expenses of litigation was permitted under Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 1.8(e)(1). The appellate court rejected an extension of the rationale for approving an advancement of the cost of an MRI to the cost of medical treatment. Rule 1.8(e) was narrowly construed. The attorneys' selection from their clientele of individuals whom they concluded needed to have medical treatment expenses advanced in order to better develop the clients' claims constituted unregulated lending to clients and was prohibited. The attorneys' contention that the prohibition of advancing medically related costs to clients was unconstitutional under Conn. Const. art. I, § 10 was also rejected. One of the attorneys also violated Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 7.2(c) by paying employees for client referrals, as the practice amounted to a payment for recommending the firm. The attorney's argument that the payments were bonuses, permissible under Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 5.4(a), was rejected. Conn. R. Prof. Conduct 7.2 prohibited anything which provided value to the referrer, including payments and bonuses for case referrals.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed. Judgment was ordered in favor of the Connecticut Statewide Grievance Committee.

State v. Wilson


CR78216507


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 14 AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1593



May 29, 2003, Decided  
June 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The Motion to Dismiss is GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant acquittee moved to dismiss the State's Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) motion to recommit the acquittee; the acquittee claimed that the recommitment would violate his rights to due process and equal protection of the law, inter alia, under Conn. Gen. Stat. art. I, §§ 8, 20.


OVERVIEW: After the acquittee was found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect of the crime of second-degree arson, a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-112, the acquittee was sentenced to 10 years in the custody of the Connecticut Commissioner of Mental Health. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) for successive periods of confinement. The court held that the State's motion to re-commit the acquittee exceeded the 10-year maximum period of confinement for the offense. As a result, the acquittee's rights to due process and equal protection under Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 20 would be violated.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1577 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kinney v. State


CV010456273S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1610



May 29, 2003, Decided  
May 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by Kinney v. State, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2560 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 16, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Kinney v. State Judicial Dep't, 1992 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3628 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 18, 1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix sued the State for negligence in assigning excessive duties to the decedent, a judge, causing the decedent to develop stress and pressure resulting in medical complications to his coronary system, including myocardial arteriosclerosis, which resulted in cardiovascular disease which caused his death. The State moved to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The Connecticut Legislature enacted 1994 Conn. Acts 13 (Spec. Sess.) to permit the administratrix to pursue her claim. The State's fundamental position was that the action of the Legislature in enacting Act 13 violated Conn. Const. art. I, § 1 as a public emolument, serving no public purpose. The State further argued that because the Claims Commissioner of Connecticut had earlier determined that it was without jurisdiction to hear the claim and because the Legislature was without jurisdiction to grant permission to sue, the court lacked jurisdiction over the matter based on sovereign immunity. The court found that it did not lack subject matter jurisdiction over the claim based on sovereign immunity. Furthermore the Act did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 1 because the Act was not a public emolument serving no purpose, as the Act served the public purpose of helping to determine whether an employer could be held negligent for overworking an employee, a public policy question that the Legislature was looking to the courts to resolve.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1578 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Logozzo v. Town of Haddam Zoning Bd. of Appeals


CV010096256


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1637



May 29, 2003, Decided  
May 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the appeal is hereby dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Haddam, Connecticut, Zoning Board of Appeals denied plaintiff owner's application for a variance from Haddam, Conn., Zoning Regs. §§ 4.1.b.3.f., 4.1.b.4., regarding, respectively, 150 feet minimum lot width for a point no more than 500 feet back from a public street, and such a lot to be one acre larger than the minimum required for its zone, to subdivide his 5.67 acres into two interior lots. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner's predecessor owned the land when the State acquired a portion bisecting the land in fee simple, absolute ownership, in 1871 for construction of a railroad. The State's abandonment of the railroad line did not create a reversion to the owner or reserve rights to him. The assumption was made that the predecessor was compensated by the State. The zoning was not a practical confiscation and, under a balancing of private and public interests, was not an unconstitutional taking since the owner's residential use was a valuable use even if not the highest and best use; the land was not rendered practically worthless. The owner did not have a vested right to obtain a variance because the owner was not being denied a permitted use of the land previously allowed before the zoning regulations were enacted. The owner's act of subdivision created the nonconforming use. The owner had actual knowledge of the railroad bisection and was presumed to have actual knowledge of the zoning regulations. Therefore, the owner's hardship was self-created by his purchase of the land. Substantively, the land subdivision did not satisfy either of the two zoning regulation requirements.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court found that the Board did not act arbitrarily, illegally, or in abuse of its discretion and dismissed the appeal.

 

1579 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Bridgeport v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Bridgeport


CV960336304S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1627



May 23, 2003, Decided  
May 29, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Planning and Zoning Commission of the City of Bridgeport (Connecticut) adopted two zoning regulations, Bridgeport, Conn., Zoning Regs. §§ 14-4 7-1(b), 14-4 7-1(c). Plaintiff zoning board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The zoning board argued that the adoption of Bridgeport, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 14-4 7-1(b) precluded it from granting any use variance within certain specified zones. The court found that the zoning board was classically aggrieved. The court held that a zoning commission's legislative discretion was not to be disturbed by the courts unless it acted arbitrarily or illegally. The record did not support the wholesale destruction of the zoning board's ability to grant a use variance pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6(a)(3). The Commission was prohibiting the legislatively authorized zoning board from exercising its statutory powers. The amendment was an improper complete divestment of the zoning board's powers to grant use variances. In adopting the amendment, the Commission acted beyond its power. The mandatory site plan review of Bridgeport, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 14-4 7-1(c) did not inappropriately contradict, limit, or displace the authority of the zoning board to grant variances pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-6, and its adoption was not contrary to law and was not an abuse of the Commission's broad discretion.


OUTCOME: The appeal was sustained with regard to the Commission's adoption of the first zoning regulation and dismissed with regard to the adoption of the second regulation.

Martinez v. Rivera


CV020817261


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1573



May 21, 2003, Decided  
May 22, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to strike counts one, two, three, four and seven denied. The defendants' motion to strike counts five and six granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff assault victim sued defendants, police officers and a city, alleging that the actions and omissions of the police officers and the city were reckless and negligent in relation to an investigation of confrontations with the assault victim, and deprived her of her equal protection rights. The police officers and the city moved to strike all seven counts of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The assault victim reported to the police that she was attacked. After a second confrontation, a protective order was issued. A third confrontation occurred after the protective order was issued. When questioned by the police officers, the attacker admitted that he had confronted the assault victim. The police officers did not arrest the attacker, however. The court found the complaint alleged acts and omissions from which a pattern showing indifference on the part of the police officers could be inferred. The complaint sufficiently alleged causes of action based on a deprivation of the assault victim's equal protection rights and a failure to act based on an unlawful pattern, custom, practice, or administrative classification against females. Since, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-38b(a), the police officers owed a duty to the assault victim to protect her from the attacker, the complaint survived the claim of governmental immunity. However, two counts were devoid of factual content as to claims of recklessness. Since the police officers may have been liable, claims for indemnification under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 7-101a, 7-465a were properly asserted.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike counts one, two, three, four, and seven was denied. The motion to strike counts five and six was granted.

 

1582 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Capozzi v. Russo


CV000162404


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1252



April 28, 2003, Decided  
April 28, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retired city employee appealed the decision of respondent Waterbury Retirement Board (Connecticut), which awarded him an annual pension of $ 46,291. The employee claimed that he was entitled to an annual pension of $ 48,259.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the city continuously from February 15, 1965, until October 20, 2000. The employee's years of service totaled 39.92, which included military service. On appeal, the primary issue was whether the fractional share of the employee's total service (.92) was included in the pension calculation. The second issue was whether the city violated specific sections of the contract by refusing to include the contractual "Top Step Bonus" in the pension calculations. The court concluded that the Board's decision in awarding the employee a service pension without the fractional share was not unreasonable, arbitrary, illegal, or an abuse of discretion. The Board properly based its calculation on the 39 full years of service without the inclusion of the additional .92 years. Military service was utilized to determine an employee's length of service with the city and his entitlement to a pension, while the amount of the actual pension was calculated by reference to completed years of service. In addition, the court found that the "Top Step Bonus" was not to be included in the calculation of regular annual pay for the purpose of computing the employee's pension benefit.


OUTCOME: The Board's decision was affirmed.

Morgan v. Warden


CV023711


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 19 AT ROCKVILLE


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1249



April 25, 2003, Decided  
April 25, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's motion to dismiss granted as to the First Amendment claim. As to Eighth Amendment claim, the motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent prison warden moved to dismiss petitioner prisoner's habeas corpus action, arguing that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction and that the prisoner failed to state a claim on which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner's habeas corpus petition claimed that the warden and others had violated his First Amendment rights by interfering with his access to the courts by interrupting his legal mail and other limitations on his activities, and that his confinement with gang members who had threatened him constituted cruel and unusual punishment violating the Eighth Amendment. The court noted that habeas relief in Connecticut was no longer strictly limited to challenges to confinement, so the Eighth Amendment claim could be heard, since it was closely related to the fact of confinement. The prisoner's First Amendment claims, however, were more in the nature of challenges to particular conditions of confinement, and these would have to be pursued in the 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action that the prisoner was simultaneously pursuing in a federal court.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss the Eighth Amendment claim but granted it as to the First Amendment claim.

McNair v. Mastropietro


CV030822774S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1404



April 25, 2003, Decided  
April 25, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Chairman of the Workers' Compensation Commission (Connecticut), filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff claimant's declaratory judgment action, which asserted that the guidelines of the Commission were unconstitutional, illegal, and invalid. The claimant also sought an injunction against the implementation of the guidelines.


OVERVIEW: The court initially found that the matter was against the State, in that it had been asserted against the Chairman in his official capacity. Sovereign immunity did not bar the bringing of the action, as the claims fell within two of the noted exceptions to immunity because she alleged constitutional infringements, as well as violations and actions in excess of statutory authority. The claimant contended that the guidelines constituted violations of her due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. The court found the Chairman's claim that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the claim was not justiciable lacked merit. The court found the elements of justiciability were all satisfied in that there was a controversy, the parties were adverse, and relief could resolve the issue. The claimant had standing to bring the action because she was within the zone of interests which were protected by the Workers' Compensation Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-275 et seq. Lastly, the court found that although the claimant had not pleaded the necessary elements for injunctive relief, such was not necessary where she also sought declaratory judgment.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

Reilly v. Smith


CV020467282S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1225



April 17, 2003, Decided  
April 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Reilly v. Smith, 84 Conn. App. 849, 855 A.2d 1000, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 381 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Reilly, 60 Conn. App. 716, 760 A.2d 1001, 2000 Conn. App. LEXIS 545 (2000)



DISPOSITION: Application for a Writ of Mandamus dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought an order in the nature of mandamus compelling defendant claims commissioner to reconsider his decision that the applicant's claim against the State was barred by the applicable statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the applicant argued that the commissioner erroneously concluded that the applicant's claim was time-barred and that the court had the power to order the commissioner to reverse his ruling and entertain the claim. The court concluded that the application for mandamus would amount to judicial review of an action of the commissioner rejecting a claim based on his determination of law and fact relating to the statute of limitations, in contradiction to the mandated finality of the commissioner's determination. The commissioner issued a discretionary ruling that the applicant's claim against the State was time-barred. No constitutional rights were implicated by that ruling, in which the commissioner did no more than apply the statute of limitations to the facts underlying the applicant's claim. The applicant's remedy was with the legislature, not the court. Although the applicant would prefer a direct judicial review of the commissioner's adverse decision regarding the application of the statute of limitations, Connecticut laws did not provide for it.


OUTCOME: The application for a writ of mandamus was dismissed.

Hunter v. Inland Wetlands & Watercourses Comm'n of Branford


CV010454478S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1227



April 17, 2003, Decided  
April 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal of the plaintiffs, Floyd Hunter and Carolee Hunter, DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners appealed from a decision by defendant wetlands commission (Connecticut) after it denied, after a public hearing, their application for a permit to permit them to construct a three bedroom, single family residence, including an access driveway and an on-site septic system.


OVERVIEW: The owners contended that the commission's decision was not supported by substantial evidence. The appellate court held that the owners were aggrieved parties. The evidence focused on the location of the septic system, which was in close proximity to the wetlands. The evidence was not so complex and intricate as to be beyond the understanding and evaluation of the lay commissioners and members of the public. Each of the reasons given for the commission's decision were supported by substantial evidence. The potential for flooding was buttressed by pictorial and descriptive evidence. The relevant facts and circumstances mandated by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-41 were considered. The site was one-third wetlands, and the owners had difficulty in obtaining a two to one ratio for the mitigation required. The belief that installation of a successful septic system was questionable was supported, as the proposed septic system was located 25 feet from the wetlands. The failure to identify, on the record, feasible and prudent alternatives was not fatal, as the statutory criteria were considered, and the commission discussed alternatives with the owners during the hearings.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1587 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Cross-Sound Cable Co., L.L.C. v. Rocque


CV030473582


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 941



April 9, 2003, Decided  
April 9, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Application for writ of mandamus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant Commissioner of the Department of Environmental Protection of the State of Connecticut (DEP), relying on Conn. Gen. Stat. § 25-157, refused to consider plaintiff cable company's application for a Certificate of Permission (COP) pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-363b to allow it to operate its electric cable across Long Island Sound, the company sought a temporary writ of mandamus to compel the DEP to consider its application.


OVERVIEW: The company applied for the COP in January 2003, so that it could operate the cable while curing areas where the cable was above the depth required by its DEP permit. An act codified at Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 16-241j, 25-157, 25-157c imposed a one-year moratorium starting June 3, 2002, on agencies considering applications relating to, inter alia, electric power line crossings of Long Island Sound. The company argued that the moratorium did not apply to its COP request and that it was unconstitutional. The court held that only two of the three mandamus requirements were met. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-363b(d) imposed a mandatory duty on the DEP to consider the COP request, and there was no adequate legal remedy aside from mandamus, but there was no clear legal right to have the application considered, as the moratorium clearly applied to the application. The constitutional claims also failed. The company had no property interest in the permit or a modification to support a due process claim. The Commerce Clause was not violated, as the moratorium did not discriminate against foreign entities and its burden on interstate commerce was not clearly excessive in relation to its local benefits.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for a writ of mandamus.

Simso v. State


CV020819172S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 996



April 7, 2003, Decided  
April 7, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Simso v. Connecticut, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 85791 (D. Conn., Nov. 27, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Connecticut filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff truck owner's action, which sought recovery of monetary damages as well as declaratory relief arising from the State's handling of administrative and judicial proceedings involving his purchase of a defective truck from a licensed used car dealer, which had spanned more than 10 years. The motion was based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The truck dealer refused to fix the owner's truck, and the owner brought a civil action as well as filing a consumer complaint with the department of motor vehicles (DMV). The DMV entered into a consent agreement with the dealer, but the owner was not happy with it. After multiple administrative and judicial steps, the claims commissioner denied the owner the right to sue the State. The owner contended that his rights to equal protection through due process had been violated by agents of the DMV and by attorneys from the attorney general's office. The State's motion to dismiss was based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction due to the doctrine of sovereign immunity and due to the State's allegation that the owner was attempting to appeal prior decisions in an inappropriate manner. The court found that the matter was not within any of the exceptions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-142 as to a waiver of the State's sovereign immunity. Further, it found that the common law exceptions to sovereign immunity were inapplicable. There were no facts which indicated that state agents acted in excess of their statutory authority or that they violated the owner's constitutionally protected rights.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

Atl. Mortg. & Inv. Corp. v. Stephenson


X08CV010182996


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT STAMFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1106



April 4, 2003, Decided  
April 4, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Atl. Mortg. & Inv. Corp. v. Stephenson, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1489 (Conn. Super. Ct., May 15, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike the special defenses and the set-off granted. Motion for summary judgment on the issue of liability under the complaint and to dismiss the fraud count granted. Motion for summary judgment as to the first and third counts denied to the extent set forth above.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mortgagee sued to foreclose a mortgage. Defendant mortgagors filed an answer asserting a set-off and special defenses (including violation of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq.) and counterclaims for breach of warranty, fraud, and a violation of CUTPA. The mortgagee filed motions to strike the special defenses, the set-off, and the counterclaims, and for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee previously filed a foreclosure action, but withdrew it (allegedly on the eve of trial). The court struck the set-off and the mortgagors' special defenses: (1) they failed to allege the elements of equitable estoppel; (2) the "unclean hands" defense had no bearing on enforceability of the note or mortgage; (3) collateral estoppel and res judicata did not apply, as no issues were determined nor judgments entered in the first action; (4) they did not allege, in support of their laches defense, how the delay in filing the second action prejudiced them; (5) 12 U.S.C.S § 4907 did not apply; and (6) they did not allege the elements of a CUTPA violation. Since the mortgagee submitted an affidavit stating that the note was in default, and the mortgagors did not controvert it, the mortgagee was entitled to summary judgment as to liability. As to the counterclaims, the mortgagors failed set out facts to support their fraud claim, which had to be pled with specificity. However, material facts existed as to whether the mortgagee's withdrawal of the first foreclosure action and failure to negotiate an insurance check violated CUTPA or breached the implied covenant of good faith.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the special defenses and the set-off was granted. The motion for summary judgment on the issue of liability under the complaint and to dismiss the fraud count of the counterclaim was granted. The motion for summary judgment as to the breach of warranty and CUTPA violation counts of the counterclaim was denied.

 

1590 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKoy


CR01553994S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 959



April 1, 2003, Decided  
April 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to suppress granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a police officer's warrantless search of defendant's person uncovered a gun, defendant was charged with loitering and carrying a pistol without a permit. Defendant moved to suppress the weapon.


OVERVIEW: Police officers conducting a "proactive" patrol at night noticed several men standing on a public sidewalk. Intending to cite these men for loitering in violation of Hartford, Conn., Mun. Code § 25-8, the officers ordered the men up against a fence so they could conduct pat down searches for the officers' personal safety and to check for identification. There had been no complaints, and none of the officers knew any of the men or had reason to believe they were armed. The court held that defendant had been "seized" for purposes of Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 9 (which provided greater protection than the Fourth Amendment), since a person in his position would believe he was not free to leave. The officer had no grounds to seize defendant for loitering, since an essential element of that offense -- impeding another's use of a sidewalk -- had not been present. The court also found that defendant did not try to flee, nor did he engage in any furtive movements. Due the illegal seizure of defendant, the gun had to be suppressed as fruit of the poisonous tree.


OUTCOME: The motion to suppress was granted.

 

1591 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vines v. Warden


File No. CV-01 0003438S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 19 AT ROCKVILLE


49 Conn. Supp. 1; 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 920; 858 A.2d 915



March 31, 2003, Decided  
March 31, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected October 5, 2004.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Vines v. Warden, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2339 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 13, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Vines v. Warden, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 406 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Memorandum of decision on reconsideration of the petitioner's motion for appointment of counsel in habeas corpus proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Motion for appointment of counsel denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a habeas corpus petition challenging the conditions of his confinement and moved for the appointment of a public defender to represent him. After denying the motion, the court, sua sponte, reconsidered it.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged he was placed in administrative segregation and assigned to a different facility without due process. Neither the United States nor Connecticut Constitutions required the appointment of counsel to represent a habeas corpus petitioner. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 51-296(a), in a habeas corpus proceeding arising from a criminal matter, an indigent petitioner was entitled to the appointment of counsel. Rather than providing that any indigent habeas petitioner was entitled to the appointment of counsel, the legislature limited those entitled to such representation by adding the words "arising from a criminal matter." A habeas petitioner who filed a habeas petition that did not arise from a criminal matter was not entitled to appointed counsel. The inmate was not challenging the underlying criminal order which caused him to be incarcerated, and his petition arose from the conditions of his confinement, rather than from a criminal matter, so he was not entitled to appointed counsel under § 51-296(a). The issues presented by the inmate's petition did not merit the appointment of counsel under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 51-291(11) or 51-293(a)(2).


OUTCOME: The inmate's motion for the appointment of a public defender to represent him was denied.

 

1592 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Maslak


MV18020209137


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 18 AT BANTAM


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 962



March 31, 2003, Decided  
April 1, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving while under the influence (DUI). The State filed a Second Part of Information charging defendant as a subsequent offender on account of three prior convictions for DUI, including an out-of-state conviction. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the second part of information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had three prior convictions for driving under the influence (DUI), including one entered in New York. He was then charged with DUI in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a. The State alleged he was a subsequent offender due to those three prior DUI convictions. Defendant moved to dismiss and argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws, that the language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a(g) was unconstitutionally vague, and that he was not adequately advised regarding his New York plea. The trial court denied the motion. It found the statute only punished him for conduct occurring while it was in effect and, thus, was not an ex post facto law. It also found that the statute's language that an out-of-state conviction had to be based on elements "substantially the same" as those in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a was not unconstitutionally vague. Finally, it found that his constitutional rights could not have been violated by the New York proceeding, as that court could not have advised him that violation of its law might one day allow his sentence to be enhanced in Connecticut under a statute not then in effect.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1593 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rosado v. Caceres


FA960621680


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, FAMILY SUPPORT MAGISTRATE DIVISION AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1312



March 29, 2003, Decided  
April 17, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Velez v. Torres, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 4216 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 27, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Connecticut commenced a support petition against defendant father. The father moved for a court order for genetic tests. Plaintiff mother did not oppose the motion, but the State opposed the motion on the grounds that paternity was not at issue, having been determined by the acknowledgment. The father moved to open the judgment some three years after support was ordered and nearly five years after the acknowledgment was filed.


OVERVIEW: The mother gave birth to the child, and two days later, she signed an affirmation naming who the child's father was. At the same time, the father executed the same form thereby acknowledging under oath that he was the father. The form included an advisement of rights on the reverse side, and a waiver of right to counsel, genetic tests, and trial just above the signature line. The father filed a motion to open the paternity proceedings more than three years after the date of the acknowledgment. The trial court found that this was well beyond the time bar in the statute. Therefore, the court did not have the authority to grant the motion absent proof by the moving party of an extraordinary factor such as fraud, mistake, or duress. Further, the acknowledgment form included a waiver of rights. There was no doubt that the father freely and voluntarily signed the acknowledgment. There was no evidence that the mother induced him to acknowledge the child or made false statements. The trial court found that the father had sufficient opportunity to raise the issue of paternity. He did not exercise reasonable diligence in pursuing such opportunities.


OUTCOME: The father's motion was denied.

 

1594 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hanrahan v. Egan


559287


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 801



March 20, 2003, Decided  
March 20, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Hanrahan v. Egan, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2610 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 1, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Judgment entered for all of the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff special deputy filed an action against defendants, the high sheriff, the chief deputy sheriff, and the State, alleging that defendants violated his civil rights under Conn. Const. art. 1, §§ 1, 4 and 20, when they retaliated against the special deputy by removing him from his assignment to the transportation unit. Defendants filed special defenses of sovereign immunity and statutory immunity pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The special deputy claimed he was reassigned from the transportation unit because he failed to help with the high sheriff's campaign and refused to sign a statement placing blame on another special deputy. Defendants claimed that they were entitled to the protection of sovereign immunity, and alleged that the special deputy failed to prove that the high sheriff and the chief deputy were acting in excess of their authority since they had the authority to reassign special deputies without a hearing. Defendants also alleged that the special deputy was reassigned due to, inter alia, his having left a loaded gun in an unlocked van, damaging a van and failing to report the damage, and turning off his radio before being released for the day. In entering judgment for defendants, the superior court concluded that the special deputy had no proprietary right to work in transportation exclusively. The high sheriff and the chief deputy had the right to reassign him without a hearing; and finally, the special deputy produced no evidence to prove any causal connection between his reassignment and his alleged refusal to sign any statement or failure to support the high sheriff's campaign.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered for defendants.

 

1595 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Frederick v. Ingala


FA020459410S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 933



March 17, 2003, Decided  
March 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to Reopen and Dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nonparent petitioned for visitation with respondent fit parent's child and alleged the nonparent had a parent-like relationship with the child, and that denying contact between them was very detrimental to the child's well-being. The parties stipulated to visitation between the nonparent and the child, which the trial court entered as a stipulated judgment. The fit parent then filed a motion to reopen and dismiss that judgment.


OVERVIEW: A child was born to the fit parent. The fit parent had a long-standing domestic partnership with the nonparent, and the child was born as a result of the fit parent's artificial insemination. Shortly after the child's third birthday, the nonparent brought an action for visitation with the minor child. The petition alleged both that the nonparent not only had a parent-like relationship with the three-year-old child, but in fact that she had a parenting relationship. The nonparent also alleged that the fit parent's actions in denying contact between the child and the nonparent were extremely detrimental to the child's well-being. The parties then entered into a written stipulation setting forth a visitation plan between the nonparent and the child, which the trial court entered as a stipulated judgment. Thereafter, the fit parent moved to reopen and dismiss, and contended that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to enter the stipulated judgment. The trial court found that it had subject matter jurisdiction and the issue of whether the petition contained sufficient allegations warranting visitation could not be decided on a motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The motion to reopen and dismiss the stipulated judgment involving the nonparent's visitation plan was denied.

 

1596 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hamlin


CR01552475T


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 837



March 12, 2003, Decided  
March 21, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Hamlin, 2005 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3002 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 22, 2005)
Affirmed by State v. Hamlin, 90 Conn. App. 445, 878 A.2d 374, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 324 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's Motion to Suppress Identification DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested and charged with the crimes of assault in the first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-59(a)(5), and carrying a pistol without a permit in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a). Defendant filed a motion to suppress the identification of defendant as the perpetrator of the crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was identified as the person who committed the crime by the victim and a friend of defendant. To succeed on the motion to suppress, defendant had to prove that identification procedures were unnecessarily suggestive, and that the resulting identification was not reliable in the totality of the circumstances. The court held that the procedures used did not give rise to a very substantial likelihood of irreparable misidentification. The police in both instances used multiple photographs, and did not rely upon a single photo. The arrays themselves were composed of photos of individuals who all strongly resembled defendant. There were no suggestions made to either witness that a photo of the suspected perpetrator was located in the arrays presented to them. The court also held that the circumstances of the commission of the crime lent themselves to a determination that the identification was reliable. The perpetrator and the victim were in close proximity during daylight hours when the shooting occurred. Defendant's friend was in close proximity to the perpetrator and the victim when the shooting occurred. Therefore, the court held that suppression was not warranted.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to suppress identification was denied.

 

1597 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Glorioso v. Police Dep't


File No. X0I CV 02-0168481S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


48 Conn. Supp. 10; 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1013; 826 A.2d 271



March 10, 2003, Decided  
March 10, 2003, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 8, 2003.
Cause dismissed by Estate of Glorioso v. Town of Burlington Police Dep't, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2554 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 9, 2003)
Summary judgment granted by, in part Glorioso v. Town of Burlington Police Dep't, 49 Conn. Supp. 200, 867 A.2d 160, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3570 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2004)



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the estate of a decedent, brought claims against several parties, including the movant, a hospital, in connection with responses to a call to 911 for emergency medical attention when the decedent became ill while visiting relatives. The hospital moved to strike nine of the 12 counts against it.


OVERVIEW: The hospital moved to strike counts 107, 118, and 129 on the ground that they duplicated claims made in counts 74, 85, and 96. The trial court found that the counts at issue did not suggest that the decedent's wife was making any claim other than a derivative claim. The challenged counts stated a cause of action, albeit a repetitive one, and the motion to strike them was be denied. Neither party demonstrated that the context of the good samaritan law or its legislative history or any other key to meaning offered a different reading than the words of the statute support with regard to the creation or abolition of any cause of action. As such, courts could hardly have been using gross negligence as a point of comparison if gross negligence did not exist. The hospital's argument that there was no cause of action for gross negligence would have led to the absurd conclusion that in enacting the good samaritan law, the legislature was providing immunity for a cause of action that did not exist anyway. There was a real difference between negligently failing to respond to a call for emergency aid and intentionally failing to do so.


OUTCOME: The hospital's motions to strike were denied.

 

1598 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Wiseman v. Armstrong


CV020821661S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 616



February 25, 2003, Decided  
February 27, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss Fourth Count granted, and motion to dismiss Fifth, Ninth, Tenth and Eleventh Counts denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator of an estate sued defendant correctional officers, alleging that various acts and omissions led to the death of the administrator's decedent. The correctional officers filed a motion to dismiss five counts of the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed while an inmate at a correctional institution. The decedent was mentally ill, and the complaint alleged that the correctional officers failed to properly treat his mental illness. This allegedly led to an incident where the decedent was killed by officers trying to subdue him. The first challenged count alleged that the correctional officers had lied about a prior incident involving another mentally ill inmate. The court found that the officers had no duty to the decedent to tell the truth about this incident. Since the administrator had standing to allege a failure to properly supervise employees, and since another challenged count was not duplicative of other counts, it was properly included. Finally, the correctional officers argued that three counts should have been dismissed since they alleged violations of the Patients' Bill of Rights, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 17a-540 to 17a-550. The court ruled that the Patients' Bill of Rights included department of correction facilities, and that the fact that inmates could be deprived of certain privileges did not invalidate the other portions of the Patients' Bill of Rights which did apply to inmates.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss one count was granted, and the motion to dismiss four other counts was denied.

 

1599 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Feliciano v. City of Hartford


CV010806525S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 527



February 21, 2003, Decided  
February 21, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to strike counts six and ten of the revised and amended complaint granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff arrestee sued defendants, a city and its former police chief (city defendants), and defendant police officers, seeking money damages for personal injuries and emotional distress he allegedly suffered when the officers used unreasonable force in his unlawful arrest and detention. The city defendants moved to strike counts six and 10, which alleged that the city defendants violated Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 8, 9.


OVERVIEW: The city defendants argued that governmental immunity protected them and that there was no recognized cause of action for money damages under the state constitution against a municipality or a supervisor for a police officer's unconstitutional conduct. The arrestee argued for the right to pursue a state Bivens cause of action against the city defendants. The trial court found that a damages claim against the city defendants would have chilled the zeal with which governmental functions were undertaken and would have hindered the deterrent effects of the Bivens remedy by allowing claimants to sue a city and its officials instead of the offending officers. Moreover, common law and statutory remedies provided the arrestee adequate means of redress. The arrestee simply failed to allege sufficient facts to support his constitutional cause of action against the city defendants. Although the arrestee also contended that the city defendants were liable for the inadequate training and supervision of the officers, such activity involved discretionary governmental acts for which the city defendants enjoyed governmental immunity absent allegations of malice, wantonness, or intentional conduct.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted defendants' motion to strike counts six and 10.

 

1600 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Plemmons v. Newton


FA000557263


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 485



February 20, 2003, Decided  
February 25, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Plemmons v. Newton, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 4180 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 7, 2002)



DISPOSITION: In the interest of the public, the state's motion to vacate the family support magistrate's determination that General Statutes § 46b-172(a)(1) unconstitutional, granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, on behalf of plaintiff mother, moved to vacate a decision by the Connecticut Family Support Magistrate Division which declared Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172(a)(1) unconstitutional. The family support magistrate had rendered a decision granting defendant alleged father's motion for genetic testing asserting that portions of § 46b-172(a)(1) violated the separation of powers doctrine in the paternity and child support action.


OVERVIEW: The alleged father, who the court later determined lacked capacity, executed an acknowledgment of paternity. The State then commenced a support petition. The appellate court decided to address the magistrate's constitutional ruling even though the issue was moot based upon the public interest in avoiding future challenges to § 46b-172(a)(1)'s constitutionality. The appellate court held the Connecticut Family Support Magistrate Division was a creature of statute and not a constitutional court. Thus, the magistrate did not have the authority to address the issue of the facial constitutionality of § 46b-172(a)(1). Moreover, the necessity of the situation before the magistrate was insufficient to require the magistrate to address the constitutional question. The magistrate should have sustained the State's objection to the motion for genetic testing and directed the alleged father to file the requisite motion to open and set aside the judgment. Despite that, the magistrate held a full evidentiary hearing on the issue of capacity, and the issue was ultimately resolved on grounds other than the constitutional claim, to which the State did not object. Thus, the issue was moot.


OUTCOME: Although the issue was moot, due to the likelihood of future challenges to the statute's constitutionality, the appellate court found that vacatur was appropriate with respect to the magistrate's constitutional determination. Accordingly, in the interest of the public, the State's motion to vacate the family support magistrate's determination that the statute was unconstitutional was granted.
